People v. Wicks


102388


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


73 A.D.3d 1233; 900 N.Y.S.2d 485; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3737; 2010 NY Slip Op 3811



May 6, 2010, Decided 
May 6, 2010, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by People v. Wicks, 15 N.Y.3d 857, 935 N.E.2d 826, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 3064, 909 N.Y.S.2d 34 (2010)
Subsequent appeal at, Application denied by People v. Wicks (Mark L.), 2011 N.Y. LEXIS 3820 (N.Y., Dec. 14, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the County Court of Warren County (New York) convicted defendant of the crimes of sexual abuse in the first degree, Penal Law § 130.65, and petit larceny. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim awoke in the early morning hours to find a strange man in her bed, with his hand inside her underwear and touching her vagina. After the man finally obeyed the victim's demands that he leave, she called her mother, who arrived and called the police. Eventually, defendant was identified as the intruder. The appellate court found that the convictions were supported by sufficient evidence. The only element of sexual abuse that was at issue was whether the victim was "physically helpless" at the time that the sexual contact occurred. Although the defense attempted to show that the victim awoke when defendant entered her bed, and was therefore awake when the sexual contact began, the victim clearly testified that when she awoke, the stranger's hand was already inside her underwear, touching her vagina, and attempting to put a finger inside her. As she was asleep when the sexual contact began, she was incapable of consenting because she was physically helpless. Her testimony constituted legally sufficient evidence to support the charge, and the jury's finding was not against the weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Sexual Abuse--Sufficiency of Evidence.--Conviction of sexual abuse in first degree was supported by legally sufficient evidence which established that victim was "physically helpless" at time that sexual contact occurred (Penal Law § 130.65 [2]); although defense attempted to show that victim awoke when defendant entered her bed, and was therefore awake when sexual contact began, victim clearly testified that when she awoke, stranger's hand was already inside her underwear, touching her vagina and attempting to put finger inside her; as she was asleep when sexual contact began, she was incapable of consenting because she was physically helpless.

Crimes--Larceny--Sufficiency of Evidence.--Conviction for petit larceny was not against weight of evidence; victim testified that she had approximately $ 105 in her purse when she went to bed; only other people in apartment between that time and when she noticed that money was missing were her boyfriend, her mother and defendant; boyfriend and mother each testified that they did not take any money from victim's purse; this circumstantial evidence was legally sufficient to support inference that defendant stole victim's money while he was in her apartment.

Crimes--Identification of Defendant--Showup

Crimes--Right to Counsel--Effective Representation

Crimes--Sentence

Rimany v. Town of Dover


2008-06862, 2008-07384, 2008-09763


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


72 A.D.3d 918; 904 N.Y.S.2d 422; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3286; 2010 NY Slip Op 3298



April 20, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Remitted by Rimany v Town of Dover, 72 AD3d 924, 904 NYS2d 426, 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3268 (N.Y. App. Div. 2d Dep't, Apr. 20, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners appeal a judgment by the Dutchess County Supreme Court (New York) in favor of defendant town in their action to recover damages for injury to their property; the trial court found that the owners' action was barred by the statute of limitations and failed to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The owners alleged that pursuant to permits issued by the town, defendant mobile home park constructed a flood wall on its property adjacent to a river, which caused their property to sustain substantial damage as a result of extensive and repeated flooding from the waters of the river. The appellate court found, inter alia, that since the owners alleged that the earliest possible time that they could have known of the injury was January 2005, their 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1988 action was filed well within the three-year limitations period. Nonetheless, the actions were properly dismissed with prejudice because the owners failed to allege that the town took their property for public use or benefitted from the alleged invasion of their property. Accordingly, the complaint failed to state a cause of action against the town. In addition, since the town itself did not excavate or place fill in the navigable waters of the state without first obtaining the requisite permit, the owners did not have a cause of action against it to recover damages under Navigation Law § 31. Therefore, all of the owners' claims against the town were properly dismissed with prejudice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Limitation of Actions--Three-Year Statute of Limitations--Federal Civil Rights Claim.--Claim pursuant to 42 USC § 1983 and concomitant 42 USC § 1988 claim were not time-barred as against Town--injury that was basis of 42 USC § 1983 claim was extensive and repeated flooding of plaintiffs' property commencing in or around January 2005 that allegedly amounted to taking by Town of their property without just compensation in violation of United States Constitution--thus, earliest possible time that plaintiffs could have known of injury that was basis of their 42 USC § 1983 claim was January 2005, and plaintiffs commenced action well within three-year limitations period.

Civil Rights--Federal Civil Rights Claim.--Allegations that, as result of flood wall constructed by neighbor on its property adjacent to river pursuant to permits issued by Town, plaintiffs' property sustained extensive and repeated flooding from waters of river causing substantial damage to property, failed to state cause of action against Town pursuant to 42 USC §§1983 or 1988--while plaintiffs alleged that actions of Town in issuing permits to neighbor to construct flood wall constituted taking by Town of their property without just compensation in violation of United States Constitution, plaintiffs failed to allege that Town took their property for public use or benefitted from alleged invasion of their property (see US Const Amend V).

Waters and Watercourses--Liability for Flooding.--Allegations that, as result of flood wall constructed by neighbor on its property adjacent to river pursuant to permits issued by Town, plaintiffs' property sustained extensive and repeated flooding from waters of river causing substantial damage to property, failed to state cause of action against Town pursuant to Navigation Law § 31--plaintiffs alleged that Town was required in accordance with statute to obtain permit from Department of Environmental Conservation before constructing flood wall but failed to do so, and that Town's failure was proximate cause of damage to plaintiffs' property; however, Town itself was not involved with physical construction of flood wall; even if private cause of action for damages could be implied under Navigation Law § 31, since Town itself did not excavate or place fill in navigable waters of state without first obtaining requisite permit, plaintiffs did not have cause of action against Town to recover damages under Navigation Law § 31.

Matter of Riches v. New York City Council


106116/08, 1380


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


75 A.D.3d 33; 899 N.Y.S.2d 177; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2946; 2010 NY Slip Op 3046



April 15, 2010, Decided 
April 15, 2010, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Riches v. New York City Council, 15 NY3d 735, 931 NE2d 1057, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 1312, 905 NYS2d 801 (N.Y., June 24, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens brought a proceeding, pursuant to NY City Charter § 1109, against respondent city council, requesting a summary judicial inquiry concerning the city council's practice of allocating funds to non-existent entities during its initial budgeting process. The Supreme Court, New York County (New York), dismissed the proceeding. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizens argued that the practice of allocations to non-existent organizations, which had been publicly disclosed and discontinued, violated NY City Charter § 100(c). However, the appellate court found that § 1109's use of the word "may" gave the trial court discretion to determine when such an inquiry was called for or appropriate. Where the trial court justice declined to conduct the inquiry and articulated reasons for refusing to do so, the decision should not have been reviewed except where there was a clear abuse of discretion. The trial court furnished several legitimate reasons for denying the application. First, the practice of reserving funds in the name of non-existent organizations had been acknowledged and had received extensive publicity. Second, the trial court found that the ongoing investigation of the practice by United States Attorney's Office and the New York City Department of Investigation was sufficient to safeguard the public interest. The trial court also found that the practice of reserving funds was not the type of transgression that § 1109 was designed to address. The trial court exercised its discretion appropriately in denying the application.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Budget -- Summary Judicial Inquiry into Violation or Neglect of Duty by Government Officials -- Allocation of Funds to Nonexistent Entities during Initial Budgeting Process 

Supreme Court did not abuse its discretion in denying petitioners' request pursuant to New York City Charter § 1109 that it conduct a summary judicial inquiry concerning the practice of the New York City Council of allocating funds to fictitious organizations during the initial budgeting process for the purpose of making later allocations to needy organizations. The charter provision, which states that a Justice of the Supreme Court "may," upon a proper application, "conduct a summary inquiry into any alleged violation or neglect of duty" by government officials, vests the Supreme Court Justice with discretion to determine when such an inquiry is called for or appropriate. The decision to decline to conduct an inquiry should not be subject to judicial review unless there is a clear abuse of discretion. Here, Supreme Court furnished several legitimate reasons for denying the application, including the fact that the practice of reserving funds in the name of nonexistent organizations had been acknowledged and received extensive publicity in the media. In addition, the court found that the ongoing investigation of the practice by two governmental agencies was sufficient to safeguard the public interest. The court also found that the practice of reserving funds was not the type of municipal corruption the charter provision was designed to address. Petitioners otherwise failed to demonstrate what purpose would be served in requiring sworn testimony from past city officials about prior allocations of a small percentage of funds to legitimate community organizations.

 

449 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Summit at Pomona, Ltd. v Village of Pomona


2009-03156


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


72 A.D.3d 797; 898 N.Y.S.2d 650; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3078; 2010 NY Slip Op 3108



April 13, 2010, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent developers sued appellant village, and others, contending that Code of Pomona, N.Y., § 130-18(H) was unconstitutional and that, in order to hinder the development of the property at issue, the village made repeated, improper demands of the developers for money in lieu of parkland. The Supreme Court, Rockland County (New York), denied the village's summary judgment motion and for leave to amend its answer. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue extant was whether the developers had viable claims based on the allegedly improper demands for money in lieu of parkland. The denial of the village's motion to amend the answer to assert a statute of limitations defense was proper. The alleged violations of the developers' constitutional rights were linked together and continuing, such that the statute of limitations for the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim was tolled up until the last violation, which occurred within the three-year limitations period. Further, those claims were not barred based on a failure to include them in the notice of claim. There was testimony at the hearing pursuant to General Municipal Law § 50-h concerning the claims arising from the village's demands for money in lieu of parkland, which supplemented the notice. Moreover, there was no prejudice to the village's defense of the suit. The village failed to establish that there were no triable issues of fact concerning whether the developers had a constitutionally-protected property interest, and whether the village's conduct was arbitrary and irrational in the constitutional sense. However, some of the individual defendants were entitled to immunity.


OUTCOME: The order was modified granting those branches of the motion for summary judgment dismissing the causes of action predicated on state law insofar as asserted against certain individual defendants. As so modified, the order was affirmed insofar as appealed from.


HEADNOTES

Limitation of Actions--Tolling.--In action alleging that defendant Village made improper demands of plaintiff developers for money in lieu of parkland in order to hinder development of property, defendants were not entitled to amend their answer to assert affirmative defense of statute of limitations and that some of plaintiffs' claims pursuant to 42 USC § 1983 should have been dismissed as time-barred; plaintiffs established that defendants' alleged violations of their constitutional rights of repeated, unjustified demands for money in lieu of parkland were linked together and continuing, such that statute of limitations for 42 USC § 1983 claim was tolled up until last violation, which occurred within three-year limitations period; accordingly, proposed amendment was patently devoid of merit.

Municipal Corporations--Notice of Claim.--In action alleging that defendant Village made improper demands of plaintiff developers for money in lieu of parkland in order to hinder development of property, fact that state law claims premised upon demands for money in lieu of parkland were not included in notice of claim did not require dismissal of those claims; testimony at hearing pursuant to General Municipal Law § 50-h concerning claims arising from Village's demands for money in lieu of parkland supplemented notice of claim, and there was no prejudice to defendants' defense of action due to deficiencies in notice of claim.

Civil Rights--Federal Civil Rights Claim

 

450 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Franza v. Olin


194.1 CA 09-01223


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


73 A.D.3d 44; 897 N.Y.S.2d 804; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2383; 2010 NY Slip Op 2224



March 19, 2010, Decided 
March 19, 2010, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff possessor appealed a judgment by the Onondaga County Supreme Court (New York) that declared she did not have title to certain real property based on adverse possession pursuant to RPAPL art. 5; the possessor claimed that the 2008 amendments to art. 5 were unconstitutional as applied to her because they deprived her of a vested property right.


OVERVIEW: The possessor claimed that she acquired title to the disputed property by adverse possession as early as 1985 in accordance with former RPAPL 501(2), CPLR 212(a). The appellate court found, inter alia, that the amendments to art. 5 became effective approximately six weeks before the possessor sought a judicial determination of her rights with respect to the disputed property, well after title to the disputed property had allegedly vested in her. Therefore, inasmuch as title to the disputed property would have vested in the possessor prior to the enactment of the 2008 amendments, application of those amendments to her was unconstitutional. Accordingly, because there were issues of fact whether the possessor acquired title to the disputed property by adverse possession prior to the effective date of the amendments, the trial court erred in dismissing the complaint on the merits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was unanimously reversed, the declaration was vacated, the complaint was reinstated, the action for a declaratory judgment was converted to an action pursuant to art. 15, and the matter was remitted for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Adverse Possession -- What Constitutes -- Actions Sufficient to Obtain Title by Adverse Possession -- Deprivation of Vested Property Rights by Application of 2008 Statutory Amendments 

Supreme Court erred in applying the 2008 amendments to RPAPL article 5 (see L 2008, ch 269, §§ 5, 8 [eff July 7, 2008]) in declaring that plaintiff did not have title to certain real property surrounding her home based on adverse possession. The 2008 amendments, which became effective approximately six weeks before plaintiff sought a judicial determination of her rights with respect to the disputed property, abrogate the common law of adverse possession and define as "permissive and non-adverse" actions that, under the prior statutory law (RPAPL former 522) and long-standing principles of common law, were sufficient to obtain title by adverse possession, such as lawn mowing, landscaping and erecting sheds (see RPAPL 543). Since, according to the facts set forth in the verified complaint and the supporting documentation submitted by plaintiff, her title to the disputed property would have vested long before the 2008 amendments to the adverse possession statute, application of those amendments to plaintiff's claim unconstitutionally deprived her of a vested property right. Where title has vested by adverse possession, it may not be disturbed retroactively by newly enacted or amended legislation. Consequently, plaintiff was entitled to the application of the version of article 5 in effect when her claim to the disputed property allegedly ripened into title. Since there were issues of fact whether plaintiff acquired title to the disputed property by adverse possession prior to July 7, 2008, Supreme Court erred in dismissing the complaint on the merits.

New York State Psychiatric Assn., Inc. v. New York State Dept. of Health


2009-03639


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


71 A.D.3d 852; 898 N.Y.S.2d 153; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2047; 2010 NY Slip Op 2113



March 16, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended March 29, 2010,
Leave to appeal dismissed by New York State Psychiatric Ass'n v. New York State Dep't of Health, 15 N.Y.3d 769, 933 N.E.2d 213, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 1418, 906 N.Y.S.2d 813 (2010)
Subsequent appeal at, Motion to strike granted by New York State Psychiatric Assn., Inc. v. N. Y. State Dept. of Health, 18 N.Y.3d 874, 2012 N.Y. LEXIS 81, 938 N.Y.S.2d 855 (2012)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State Psychiatric Association appealed an amended order by the Nassau County Supreme Court (New York) that denied its motion for summary judgment in its action for declaratory relief concerning the payment of Medicare Part B coinsurance amount for certain individuals pursuant to the 2006 amendment to Social Services Law § 367-a(1)(d)(iii) and to determine that portions of the 2008 budget bill were unconstitutional.

OUTCOME: The amended order was modified, inter alia, by deleting the provision denying the motion for summary judgment, and by substituting therefor a provision granting the motion to the extent of declaring that the portions of the budget in question were declared unconstitutional, and the Department was ordered to pay the full Medicare Part B coinsurance amount sought by the Association; and as so modified, the amended order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Limitation of Actions--Four-Month Statute of Limitations

Health--Medicare Reimbursement Payments.--Licensed psychiatrists were entitled to receive 100% reimbursement of Medicare deductible and coinsurance fees.

 

453 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v Fernandez


2007-11742


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


72 A.D.3d 303; 897 N.Y.S.2d 158; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1964; 2010 NY Slip Op 1977



March 9, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal granted by People v Fernandez, Joao, 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6312 (N.Y. App. Div. 2d Dep't, Mar. 18, 2010)
Leave to appeal granted by People v Fernandez, 14 NY3d 807, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 1884, 899 NYS2d 142 (N.Y., Mar. 18, 2010)
Affirmed by, Sub nomine at People v Correa, 15 NY3d 213, 933 NE2d 705, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 1145, 907 NYS2d 106 (N.Y., June 3, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a nonjury trial, the Integrated Domestic Violence (IDV) Part of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), convicted defendant of three counts of attempted aggravated harassment in the second degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue was whether CPL 210.05 precluded the IDV Part of the Supreme Court from exercising jurisdiction to try misdemeanor charges absent an indictment or a superior court information. The appellate court held that it did not. Judiciary Law § 211 provided the chief judge with constitutional authority to regulate the transfer of cases among the courts, and satisfied the "as may be provided by law" requirement of N.Y. Const. art. VI, § 19. Thus, there was no merit to the claim that a lack of legislative authority foreclosed the trial court's exercise of its removal power under the constitution. Defendant also argued that the transfer of his misdemeanor case violated CPL 210.05 because the trial court did not acquire jurisdiction over the action by indictment or superior court information. However, CPL 210.05 was not intended to prohibit the Supreme Court from exercising its jurisdiction under the New York State Constitution, nor could it have. CPL 210.05 did not preclude the IDV Part of the trial court from exercising its jurisdiction under the New York State Constitution to try misdemeanor charges in the absence of an indictment or a superior court information.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Appeal -- Raising Issue for First Time on Appeal -- Challenge to Court's Jurisdiction 

1. A challenge to the jurisdiction of the Integrated Domestic Violence Part of the Supreme Court to try misdemeanor charges against a defendant in the absence of an indictment or a superior court information may properly be raised for the first time on appeal. The preservation rule does not apply to errors that affect the organization of the court or the mode of proceedings prescribed by law. Defendant's contention that Supreme Court was not competent to entertain the action in the absence of an indictment or a superior court information as required by CPL 210.05 raised the issue of the court's jurisdiction and, thus, preservation was not required.

Crimes -- Removal to Superior Court -- Legislative Authority

2. Judiciary Law § 211, as implemented by the rules promulgated by the Chief Judge and the Chief Administrative Judge pursuant to authority derived from the New York State Constitution, provides statutory authority for the transfer of misdemeanor cases to Integrated Domestic Violence Parts of the Supreme Court pursuant to NY Constitution article VI, § 19 (a), which gives the Supreme Court the authority to transfer cases to itself "[a]s may be provided by law." In view of the phrase "[a]s may be provided by law," the power of removal conferred by article VI, § 19 (a) is not self-executing. However, Judiciary Law § 211 satisfies the "[a]s may be provided by law" requirement of article VI, § 19 (a). Therefore, the Supreme Court's exercise of its removal power under that constitutional provision was not foreclosed by a lack of legislative authority.

Crimes -- Jurisdiction of Offenses -- Trial of Misdemeanors in Supreme Court Absent Indictment or Superior Court Information

3. CPL 210.05 does not preclude the Integrated Domestic Violence (IDV) Part of the Supreme Court from exercising its jurisdiction under the New York State Constitution to try misdemeanor charges against a defendant in the absence of an indictment or a superior court information. IDV Parts were administratively created to hear and determine domestic violence cases in a single forum. CPL 210.05 merely prescribes the method and manner required for a prosecutor to prosecute an offense in a superior court, rather than imposing a limitation on the superior court's constitutional jurisdiction over such a case. Therefore it was not intended to prohibit the Supreme Court from exercising its jurisdiction under the New York State Constitution, nor could it. Once defendant's case was transferred to the IDV Part pursuant to Judiciary Law § 211, as implemented by the rules promulgated by the Chief Judge and the Chief Administrative Judge pursuant to authority derived from the New York State Constitution, it was properly handled pursuant to the appropriate substantive and procedural rules of that court.

Swergold v. Cuomo


507982


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


70 A.D.3d 1290; 896 N.Y.S.2d 495; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1571; 2010 NY Slip Op 1568



February 25, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at, Application denied by, Motion denied by, Sub nomine at Matter of D'Agostino v. DiNapoli, 31 Misc. 3d 1224(A), 929 N.Y.S.2d 198, 2011 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2244 (2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorneys appealed an order by the Albany County Supreme Court (New York) that dismissed their claims against defendants, Comptroller and New York State and Local Employees' Retirement System.


OVERVIEW: In April 2008, the Comptroller announced new regulations that invalidated the attorneys' memberships in the Retirement System. As a result, the attorneys sought declaratory and injunctive relief. They claimed that the defendants had no authority to investigate, reduce, or terminate their retirement benefits and that the procedures used by the defendants were contrary to statute and in violation of N.Y. Const. art. V, § 7. The appellate court found, inter alia, that, pursuant to a prior case, the attorneys were restored all of their service credits and were guaranteed the right to a timely hearing and a predetermination of their membership status in the Retirement System even though they had not yet applied for retirement. Accordingly, the attorneys' claims pertaining to the alleged deprivation of their due process rights were rendered moot and their remaining arguments were premature. Inasmuch as the attorneys' proposed amended complaint would have been dismissed in its entirety, their challenge to the denial of their CPLR 3025(b) motion to amend was also moot.


OUTCOME: The order was modified by reversing the denial of the defendants' cross-motion with respect to the causes of action that were converted into a proceeding pursuant to CPLR art. 78, and by dismissing said causes of action; and, as so modified, the order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Appeal--Academic and Moot Questions--Right to Public Pension Benefits.--In action arising out of dispute between plaintiffs, attorneys claiming entitlement to public pension benefits for their work as counsel to municipalities while at same time maintaining private law practices, and defendants, entities investigating propriety of those claims, plaintiffs' claims pertaining to alleged deprivation of their due process rights were rendered moot to extent that they sought restoration of their benefits pending hearing since, in light of order issued in related case, plaintiffs' service credits were restored and they were guaranteed right to timely hearing and predetermination of their membership status in Retirement System even though they had not yet applied for retirement.

Courts--Ripeness Doctrine--Right to Public Pension Benefits.--In action arising out of dispute between plaintiffs, attorneys claiming entitlement to public pension benefits for their work as counsel to municipalities while at same time maintaining private law practices, and defendants, entities investigating propriety of those claims, certain of plaintiffs' due process claims and plaintiffs' arguments that unilateral revocation of their membership in Retirement System was unconstitutional were premature since, in light of order issued in related case, plaintiffs' service credits were restored and they were guaranteed right to timely hearing and predetermination of their membership status in Retirement System even though they had not yet applied for retirement--likewise, challenges to validity of new rules insofar as they were applied to determine that plaintiffs were independent contractors instead of employees or applied to diminish earned credits, as well as cause of action protesting retroactive application of new rules to plaintiffs, were not ripe for judicial review inasmuch as result and propriety of application of new rules to these plaintiffs was not yet finally determined.

People v Correa


5209, 51080C/05


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION FIRST DEPARTMENT


70 A.D.3d 532; 897 N.Y.S.2d 14; 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1508; 2010 NY Slip Op 1533



February 23, 2010, Decided 
February 23, 2010, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay denied by People v. Correa, 14 NY3d 787, 925 NE2d 922, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 686, 899 NYS2d 119 (2010)
Motion granted by People v. Correa, 14 NY3d 787, 925 NE2d 922, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 693, 899 NYS2d 119 (2010)
Reversed by, Remitted by People v. Correa, 15 NY3d 213, 933 NE2d 705, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 1145, 907 NYS2d 106 (N.Y., June 3, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Division of the Supreme Court, Bronx County (New York), convicted defendant of harassment in the second degree, and sentenced him to a term of 15 days. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the establishment of the trial court by administrative decree was proper. The appellate court held that it was not. N.Y. Const. art. VI vested judicial authority in a unified court system. In transferring all cases charging a class A misdemeanor to the trial court, causing a collapse of the constitutionally created Criminal Court of the City of New York in the Bronx, the Chief Judge and Chief Administrator overstepped their authority under N.Y. Const. art. VI, §§ 19(a), 28, and Judiciary Law §§ 211, 212, and impinged on the legislature's reserved primary power to alter and regulate jurisdiction, practice, and procedure under N.Y. Const. art. VI, § 30. The impact of the establishment of the trial court and the transfer of all Bronx County criminal cases charging class A misdemeanors under N.Y. R. Chief Admin. Off. Ct. pt. 142 far exceeded the routine operation and administration of the Unified Court System contemplated by § 28(c), § 211(1)(a), and § 212(1)(c). Since the Chief Administrator was without authority to order the transfer, the trial court never acquired jurisdiction to try and sentence defendant under a misdemeanor information.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and the misdemeanor information was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Jurisdiction of Offenses--Criminal Division of in Bronx County.--Defendant's conviction was reversed and misdemeanor information dismissed; defendant had been charged by information in Bronx Criminal Court prior to his case being transferred to Criminal Division of of Bronx County; did not possess jurisdiction over defendant's case absent filing of indictment or superior court information as specified in CPL 210.05; there is no statutory authority for transfer of cases being prosecuted by misdemeanor information to unless matter is referred to grand jury and indictment obtained, or right to indictment waived and superior court information filed.

Constitutional Law--Separation of Powers--Authority of Chief Judge and Chief Administrator to Promulgate Rules to Provide for Transfer of Cases to Criminal Division of of Bronx County.--In transferring all cases charging class A misdemeanor to newly created Criminal Division of of Bronx County, through promulgation Rules of Chief Judge (22 NYCRR) part 42 and Rules of Chief Administrator of Courts (22 NYCRR) part 142, causing collapse of constitutionally created Criminal Court of City of New York in Bronx, Chief Judge and Chief Administrator overstepped bounds of administrative and operational authority they possess under State Constitution, article VI, § 28 and § 19 (a), and Judiciary Law §§ 211 and 212, and impinged on Legislature's reserved primary power to alter and regulate jurisdiction, practice and procedure under State Constitution, article VI, § 30.

Courts--Transfer or Removal to Other Court--Authority of Chief Judge and Chief Administrator to Promulgate Rules to Provide for Transfer of Cases to Criminal Division of of Bronx County.--Establishment of Criminal Division of of Bronx County by administrative decree, which eviscerates Bronx Criminal Court by depriving it of its jurisdiction over class misdemeanors and effectively restructures constitutionally created Unified Court System, is not justifiable under State Constitution, Criminal Procedure Law, Judiciary Law or any of statutes or rules governing administrative powers of Chief Judge's of State of New York and Chief Administrator of Courts.

Matter of Sheeran v New York State Dept. of Transp.


506197


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


68 A.D.3d 1199; 891 N.Y.S.2d 167; 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8739; 2009 NY Slip Op 8914



December 3, 2009, Decided 
December 3, 2009, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal granted by Sheeran v. New York State DOT, 14 N.Y.3d 707, 926 N.E.2d 599, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 448, 900 N.Y.S.2d 244 (2010)
Reversed by Matter of Sheeran v. New York State Dept. of Transp., 2011 N.Y. LEXIS 3249 (N.Y., Nov. 17, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee brought a CPLR art. 78 proceeding, seeking to annul a determination of respondent department which placed the employee on involuntary leave of absence. The Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), granted the employee's application. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was on voluntary sick leave when, following a medical examination by a physician chosen by the department and a psychologist, the department placed him on the involuntary leave of absence. The trial court found that the employee should have been afforded the procedures set forth in Civil Service Law § 72. The department argued that the application of § 72 was restricted to situations in which an employer sought to place an employee currently working on involuntary leave. The department also argued that 4 NYCRR 21.3(e) and the collective bargaining agreement (CBA) applied, to the exclusion of § 72, because the employee was already on voluntary sick leave and wanted to return to work. The appellate court agreed. Based on the plain language of § 72, especially when read in juxtaposition to the language of 4 NYCRR 21.3, the former was intended to apply to active employees, whereas the latter applied to employees already on voluntary sick leave. To conclude otherwise would, among other things, have rendered portions of 4 NYCRR 21.3 and the CBA entirely superfluous. Thus, the department's actions were not arbitrary, capricious, irrational, or contrary to law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the petition was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service--Compensation and Benefits--Leave for Ordinary Disability.--Petitioner was properly placed on involuntary leave of absence after voluntary sick leave, upon determination that he was unfit to resume employment, and Civil Service Law § 72, which sets forth notice and hearing procedures to be employed when employee is unable to perform duties of his or her position by reason of disability, was inapplicable--plain language of Civil Service Law § 72 restricts its application to situations in which employer seeks to place employee who is currently working on involuntary leave, and 4 NYCRR 21.3 (e) and provisions of collective bargaining agreement are applicable, to exclusion of Civil Service Law § 72, when employee, like petitioner, is already on voluntary sick leave and wants to return to work.

The estimated acquisition and construction cost for the project were to be funded by the university without any contribution from any municipal entity. The blight designation was mere sophistry. The true beneficiary of the scheme to redevelop the property was not the community that was supposedly blighted, but rather the university. The condemnor intentionally limited the administrative record by arbitrarily closing it, while simultaneously withholding documents that the owners were legally entitled to receive. As a result, the condemnor's actions deprived the owners of a reasonable opportunity to be heard under EDPL 203 and violated their due process rights under amend. XIV, and § 6.


OUTCOME: The petitions was granted, and the determination was annulled.


HEADNOTES

Eminent Domain -- Judicial Review -- Premature Closing of Administrative Record 

The determination of the Empire State Development Corporation (ESDC) approving the acquisition by eminent domain of certain real property for the development of a new campus for a private university was annulled due to the ESDC's premature closing of the administrative record while simultaneously withholding relevant documents that petitioners were legally entitled to receive. The ESDC's actions deprived petitioners of a reasonable opportunity to be heard and to submit other documents concerning the proposed project into the record in violation of both EDPL 203 and their constitutional rights to procedural due process.

461 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Maio v Kralik


2008-02532


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


70 A.D.3d 1; 888 N.Y.S.2d 582; 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8062; 2009 NY Slip Op 8187



November 10, 2009, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed an order by the Rockland County Supreme Court (New York) that granted summary judgment to defendants, sheriff and sheriff department, in his action, inter alia, to recover damages pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and denied his motion for summary judgment on the issue of liability for the destruction of his weapons and shooting accessories.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a temporary order of protection, the owner surrendered three handguns, three rifles, a shotgun, and shooting accessories that he owned to the sheriff's department. When he subsequently returned to the sheriff's department to reclaim his property, he learned that it had been destroyed, purportedly in accordance with the applicable statutory scheme. The appellate court found, inter alia, that although the destruction of the owner's handguns was permissible and in compliance with the applicable statutes as they existed at the time, the destruction of the owner's rifles, shotgun, and shooting accessories was not authorized under Penal Law § 400.05(6), as they were not "firearms" within the meaning of Penal Law § 265.00(3). Accordingly, the owner's § 1983 action was properly brought against the sheriff's department since it was acting under color of law when it deprived the owner of his protectable property interest. However, the sheriff was entitled to qualified immunity since he would not have known that disposing of the owner's rifles, shotguns, and shooting accessories violated the owner's clearly established statutory or constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The order was modified, inter alia, by granting the owner's motion for summary judgment and by denying the department's motion on the issue of liability; and, as so modified, the order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Civil Rights -- Federal Civil Rights Claim -- Wrongful Destruction of Weapons Surrendered Pursuant to Family Court Order -- Liability of Sheriff's Department

1. Defendant Sheriff's Department was liable to plaintiff pursuant to 42 USC § 1983 for violating plaintiff's right to procedural due process under the law by wrongfully destroying the rifles, shotgun, and shooting accessories that plaintiff had surrendered in compliance with a temporary order of protection issued pursuant to Family Court Act § 842-a. The handguns that plaintiff surrendered were lawfully destroyed in accordance with the version of Penal Law § 400.05 (6) then in effect, since those weapons were classified as "firearms" within the meaning of Penal Law § 265.00 (3) that defendant was authorized to destroy because they were not reclaimed within one year of their surrender. However, the remaining items were not similarly categorized as "firearms," and defendant was thus not authorized to destroy them, regardless of plaintiff's failure to reclaim them within one year. Plaintiff's claim was otherwise properly brought against the Sheriff's Department, which was acting under color of law when it deprived plaintiff of his protectable property interest in the items he surrendered. Plaintiff sufficiently demonstrated that there was a municipal policy or custom of disposing of weapons surrendered in accordance with Family Court Act § 842-a, regardless of whether they fit the statutory definition of "firearms." Furthermore, due process was not satisfied by Family Court Act § 842-a (7), which only provided plaintiff with the right to a hearing to contest the surrender order, and did not afford him any notice that his property would be destroyed.

Civil Rights -- Federal Civil Rights Claim -- Wrongful Destruction of Weapons Surrendered Pursuant to Family Court Order -- Qualified Immunity of Sheriff

2. Defendant Sheriff was not liable to plaintiff pursuant to 42 USC § 1983 for wrongfully destroying the rifles, shotgun, and shooting accessories that plaintiff had surrendered in compliance with a temporary order of protection issued pursuant to Family Court Act § 842-a. The Sheriff was entitled to qualified immunity in his individual capacity because he would not have clearly recognized that destroying plaintiff's rifles, shotgun and shooting accessories was unlawful. The items were surrendered pursuant to a Family Court order, and the version of Penal Law § 400.05 (6) then in effect appeared to provide that such items could be disposed of after one year's time. A reasonable official in this circumstance would not have known that Penal Law § 400.05 (6), although authorizing the destruction of plaintiff's handguns, actually excluded rifles and shotguns, and therefore would not have known that disposing of the weapons violated clearly established statutory or constitutional rights of which a reasonable person would have known.

 

462 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Newfield Cent. School Dist. v New York State Div. of Human Rights


506944


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


66 A.D.3d 1314; 888 N.Y.S.2d 244; 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7593; 2009 NY Slip Op 7731



October 29, 2009, Decided 
October 29, 2009, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, Tompkins County (New York), granted the application of petitioner school district, in a proceeding pursuant to CPLR art. 78, to prohibit respondent State Division of Human Rights (SDHR), from investigating discrimination complaints against the school district. The SDHR appealed.


OVERVIEW: The SDHR sought to investigate complaints that two male students were the victims of gender discrimination in the way the school district had disciplined them for an altercation. Ultimately, the SDHR issued an initial determination that it had jurisdiction to conduct the investigations. The school district then brought this proceeding alleging that the SDHR lacked jurisdiction to investigate claims against it under Executive Law § 296(4) because it was not an education corporation or association as contemplated by that statute, and sought a writ of prohibition. The appellate court found that the school district had not exhausted its administrative remedies in that the hearing process was not completed. In the context of that administrative proceeding, the school district could have challenged the applicability of § 296(4) and, at the same time, mounted a defense to the discrimination charges. Once a final determination was issued, the school district, if necessary, had the opportunity to raise these issues in a challenge to SDHR's final determination. In addition, it was by no means certain that the SDHR would not find for the school district as to the discrimination charges.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the petition was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Administrative Law--Failure to Exhaust Administrative Remedies.--Court erred in granting writ of prohibition to prohibit State Division of Human Rights (SDHR) from investigating discrimination complaints against petitioner school district where petitioner failed to exhaust its administrative remedies; in context of administrative proceeding, petitioner would have opportunity to challenge applicability of Executive Law § 296 (4) to public school districts and, at same time, mount defense to charges of discrimination against it; in addition, it was not certain that SDHR would not find for petitioner or that requiring complete exhaustion of administrative remedies would be futile exercise; moreover, petitioner did not show that it would suffer irreparable harm by proceeding with hearings prior to judicial determination as to SDHR's jurisdiction to investigate and adjudicate subject complaints.

Matter of Walsh v Katz


2009-09126


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


66 A.D.3d 1052; 888 N.Y.S.2d 549; 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7614; 2009 NY Slip Op 7774



October 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised October 30, 2009.
Appeal dismissed by Matter of Walsh v. Katz, 15 NY3d 801, 934 NE2d 322, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 3264, 907 NYS2d 753 (2010)
Affirmed by Matter of Walsh v. Katz, 2011 N.Y. LEXIS 1343 (N.Y., June 2, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner residents sought to prohibit respondent candidate's name from being placed on the ballot for a town justice seat. The candidate cross-petitioned, among other things, to validate his designating petition. The Supreme Court, Suffolk County (New York), denied the residents' petition, dismissed the proceeding, and granted that branch of the cross petition which was to validate the designating petition. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to L 1860, ch 113, § 2, as amended by L 1898, ch 373, § 2, as further amended by L 1977, ch 276, § 2, the legislature provided for a fifth town justice who was required to reside in a specific area. The town justice was also required to serve as a member of the town board. The residents objected to the candidate on the ground that he did not meet the residency requirement. The trial court held that the person elected to the seat was required to meet the residency requirement within 30 days after the commencement of the term of office, by January 30, 2010, rather than at the time the designating petition was filed. The candidate first claimed that the residency requirement was unconstitutional. The appellate court disagreed. However, the trial court erred in finding that the candidate would not have been required to meet the constitutional and statutory requirements of the office until 30 days after the commencement of the term of office. In light of the unique dual role of the public office, requiring the office holder to serve not only as a town justice, but as a member of the town board, the earlier date provided for by Election Law § 6-122(3) applied.


OUTCOME: The final order was modified by stating that January 1, 2010, was the date by which the candidate must have become a resident to qualify for the public office of town justice, should he be elected to that public office. As so modified, the final order was affirmed and the case was remitted to the trial court for, inter alia, entry of a judgment declaring that the candidate did not establish that the challenged law was unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Elections--Designating Petitions.--Requirement that fifth Town Justice, holder of island seat, also serve as member of Town Board and reside on island (L 1860, ch 113, § 2, as amended) was not unconstitutional--given location of island and its distance from rest of Town, requirement that holder of island seat be resident of island ensured that Town Board would have at least one member who has first-hand knowledge of unique circumstances and problems faced by island residents, and facilitated full participation of those residents in Town governance--residency requirement was not unconstitutional--Supreme Court erred in finding that candidate for office would not be required to meet constitutional and statutory requirements of office until 30 days after commencement of term of office (see Election Law § 6-122 [3]).

Matter of Highland Hall Apts., LLC v New York State Div. of Hous. & Community Renewal


2008-08953


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


66 A.D.3d 678; 888 N.Y.S.2d 67; 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7097; 2009 NY Slip Op 7255



October 6, 2009, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former owner and proposed petitioner current owner appealed an order and judgment by the Westchester County Supreme Court (New York) that dismissed the former owner's proceeding insofar as asserted against respondents, city and tenants, as time-barred and for lack of standing, and denied the current owner's cross-motion to be substituted as the petitioner.


OVERVIEW: While a petition for administrative review was pending, the former owner conveyed one of its buildings to the current owner. Thereafter, the former owner commenced a hybrid proceeding pursuant to CPLR art. 78 to compel the New York State Division of Housing and Community Renewal (DHCR) to render an administrative determination as to the rent regulatory status of the building and an action for a declaration that the city's resolution was arbitrary, unreasonable, and unconstitutional to the extent that it determined that the building was subject to the Emergency Tenant Protection Act of 1974, L 1974, ch. 576. The appellate court found, inter alia, that contrary to the trial court's determination, a declaratory judgment action rather than a proceeding pursuant to art. 78 was the proper vehicle for resolving the challenge to the resolution. Accordingly, the proceeding was governed by the six-year catch-all limitations period of CPLR 213(1) and was timely interposed. Because the former owner, in effect, conceded, it lacked standing since it did not own the building at the time of commencement of the proceeding, the current owner should have been substituted as the petitioner.


OUTCOME: The appeal of the denial of the current owner's cross-motion to be substituted in the proceeding was dismissed, the order and judgment were modified by deleting the provisions thereof dismissing the action as time-barred, and the matter was remitted for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Declaratory Judgments--When Remedy Appropriate.--Declaratory judgment action rather than proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 was proper vehicle for resolving challenge to resolution which declared that Emergency Tenant Protection Act of 1974 (L 1974, ch 576) applied to buildings owned by petitioner; accordingly, Supreme Court should have determined that insofar as declaratory and injunctive relief was sought against City and tenants, proceeding was governed by six-year catch-all limitations period of CPLR 213 (1) and was timely interposed.

Proceeding against Body or Officer--Mandamus

Parties--Substitution of Parties

People v Kelly


752, 752A, 2207/07


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


65 A.D.3d 886; 885 N.Y.S.2d 52; 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6240; 2009 NY Slip Op 6383



September 8, 2009, Decided 
September 8, 2009, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by People v. Kelly, 13 NY3d 860, 920 NE2d 100, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 4789, 891 NYS2d 695 (N.Y., Nov. 10, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon defendant's guilty plea to attempted robbery in the second degree, the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), convicted him and imposed sentence. Later defendant moved, pursuant to CPL 440.10, 440.20, to vacate his conviction and set aside his sentence. This motion was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the plea proceeding, defendant was adjudicated a second violent felony offender because of a prior Maryland conviction for abducting a child under 12 years old. Defendant admitted to the Maryland conviction, and, after conferring with counsel, answered in the negative when asked if he was making a constitutional challenge to the Maryland conviction. Defendant argued that his conviction and sentence should have been set aside because he was actually not a predicate violent felony offender, that he pleaded guilty under the mistaken belief he was, and that his guilty plea was therefore involuntary. Defendant also claimed that his attorney was ineffective for not challenging his predicate violent felony adjudication at the plea proceeding. The appellate court found that, because defendant failed, during the plea proceedings, to raise the issue of whether the statute under which he was convicted in Maryland was the equivalent of a New York violent felony, he waived that issue. Under the circumstances, the appellate court declined to set aside the plea bargain. Alternatively, the appellate court found that defendant was properly adjudicated a second violent felony offender.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Appeal--Preservation of Issue for Review--Enhanced Sentence.--Because defendant failed, during plea proceedings, to raise issue of whether statute under which he was convicted in Maryland was equivalent of New York violent felony, he waived that issue; defendant pleaded guilty after negotiated plea deal and declined opportunity to challenge prior Maryland conviction as basis for predicate violent felony.

Crimes--Sentence--Second Violent Felony Offender.--Defendant was properly adjudicated second violent felony offender on basis of prior Maryland conviction for crime of abducting child under 12 years old, which was equivalent to New York felony kidnapping; defendant failed to preserve issue as to whether predicate felony statement was facially defective because Maryland conviction it identified occurred more than 10 years prior and it did not set forth term of incarceration that could be used to toll 10-year limitation period under Penal Law § 70.04; moreover, as defendant's period of incarceration for Maryland conviction satisfied 10-year limitation period, any failure to list tolling period on predicate felony statement was harmless.

Crimes--Right to Counsel--Effective Representation

People v. Edwards


776 KA 08-02556


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


65 A.D.3d 829; 884 N.Y.S.2d 528; 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6198; 2009 NY Slip Op 6356



August 28, 2009, Decided 
August 28, 2009, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Motion denied by, Judgment entered by People v. Edwards, 14 NY3d 741, 925 NE2d 576, 2010 N.Y. LEXIS 20, 898 NYS2d 538 (N.Y., Feb. 16, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Erie County Court (New York) that convicted him of first-degree criminal possession of a controlled substance and third-degree assault; defendant claimed that because his extended detention at a roadside traffic stop was unconstitutional, the trial court erred in refusing to suppress the evidence seized as a result thereof.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's vehicle was pulled over for excessively tinted windows, in violation of Vehicle and Traffic Law § 375(12-a)(b)(2). Even though the deputies had the information necessary for issuing a traffic ticket based on that violation, they detained defendant for further investigation based on defendant's nervous appearance, their "gut" feelings, and their experience as narcotics officers. Thereafter, one of the deputies allegedly observed crumbs of crack cocaine on defendant's right palm. After directing defendant to exit the vehicle, a struggle ensued, and one of the deputies was injured. A subsequent inventory search of the vehicle disclosed 8.892 ounces of cocaine. The appellate court found, inter alia, that although the initial seizure was justified, the length and circumstances of the ensuing detention were not. Defendant's alleged nervousness did not, by itself, provide the requisite reasonable suspicion of criminality to justify the extension of the traffic stop. Accordingly, because the deputies were not engaged in the performance of a lawful duty, the assault, resisting arrest, and obstructing governmental administration charges should have been dismissed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated, the motion to suppress was granted, the assault, resisting arrest, and obstructing governmental administration of the indictment were dismissed, and the matter was remitted for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Unlawful Search and Seizure.--Sheriff's Deputies did not have reasonable suspicion to extend traffic stop after its initial justification was exhausted, and motion to suppress should have been granted--although initial seizure was justified, length and circumstances of ensuing detention were not; Deputies delayed issuance of traffic ticket to defendant to further investigate defendant and his vehicle in hope that initial traffic stop would escalate into drug investigation; alleged observation of crumbs of crack cocaine on defendant's palm by one of Deputies occurred during course of extended detention, and inventory search of defendant's vehicle that led to discovery of narcotics was product of inseparable illegal detention of defendant; Deputies' observation that defendant appeared to be nervous did not, by itself, provide requisite reasonable suspicion of criminality to justify extension of initially valid traffic stop--because Deputies' detention of defendant was unlawful when defendant refused to surrender his keys and struggle ensued, they were not engaged in performance of lawful duty to support count charging assault in second degree--count charging resisting arrest should also have been dismissed because arrest was not "authorized" (Penal Law § 205.30)--nor could defendant be convicted of obstructing governmental administration in second degree (Penal Law § 195.05) since Deputies were not engaged in authorized conduct.

Skelos v. Paterson


2009-06673


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


65 A.D.3d 339; 885 N.Y.S.2d 92; 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6116; 2009 NY Slip Op 6265



August 20, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Skelos v Paterson, 13 NY3d 773, 915 NE2d 1170, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 3519, 886 NYS2d 872 (N.Y., Sept. 15, 2009)
Motion granted by Skelos v Paterson, 13 NY3d 773, 915 NE2d 1171, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 3521, 886 NYS2d 873 (N.Y., Sept. 15, 2009)
Motion granted by Skelos v Paterson, 13 NY3d 773, 915 NE2d 1170, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 3522, 886 NYS2d 872 (N.Y., Sept. 15, 2009)
Motion granted by Skelos v Paterson, 13 NY3d 774, 915 NE2d 1171, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 3523, 886 NYS2d 873 (N.Y., Sept. 15, 2009)
Motion granted by Skelos v Paterson, 13 NY3d 774, 915 NE2d 1171, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 3524, 886 NYS2d 873 (N.Y., Sept. 15, 2009)
Motion granted by Skelos v Paterson, 13 NY3d 773, 915 NE2d 1171, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 3527, 886 NYS2d 872 (N.Y., Sept. 15, 2009)
Reversed by, Motion denied by, Certified question answered by Skelos v Paterson, 13 NY3d 141, 915 NE2d 1141, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 3578, 886 NYS2d 846, 2009 NY Slip Op 6585 (N.Y., Sept. 22, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff senators sued defendants governor, secretary of state, and nominee for the office of lieutenant-governor, challenging the governor's appointment of the nominee as lieutenant-governor. The Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York), inter alia, preliminarily enjoined the nominee from exercising the powers of the office of lieutenant-governor. The governor, secretary of state, and nominee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The governor argued that a quo warranto proceeding brought by the attorney general was the exclusive method to challenge the appointment. However, the appellate court found that nothing showed that the attorney general intended to take an active role and that the public interest required that the issues be addressed. A declaratory judgment action and injunctive relief was a proper way to challenge the appointment. The senators had standing. The governor did not have the authority to appoint a lieutenant-governor, and his purported appointment could not have been reconciled with N.Y. Const. art. IV, § 6. No considerations of the state's financial difficulties or of the senate's political strife authorized the appointment. Public Officers Law § 43 did not authorize the governor to fill a vacancy, but only to appoint a person to execute the duties of the office until the vacancy was filled by election. Public Officers Law § 43 could not have been constitutionally applied to a vacancy in the lieutenant-governor office. As the statute could not have been reconciled with the Constitution as far as the lieutenant-governor's office, it yielded. The purported appointment was unlawful.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed insofar as appealed from.


HEADNOTES

Declaratory Judgments -- When Remedy Appropriate -- Challenge to Governor's Appointment of Lieutenant Governor to Fill Vacancy 

1. An action for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief brought by members of the New York State Senate was a permissible way to challenge the constitutionality of the Governor's appointment of an individual to fill a vacancy in the office of lieutenant governor. A quo warranto proceeding brought by the Attorney General (Executive Law § 63-b) was not the exclusive method by which the lawfulness of the Governor's appointment could be challenged inasmuch as there were no disputed issues of fact to be tried and only an issue of law was presented.

Parties -- Standing -- Challenge to Governor's Appointment of Lieutenant Governor to Fill Vacancy 

2. Plaintiffs, members of the New York State Senate, had standing to maintain an action for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief challenging the Governor's appointment of an individual to fill a vacancy in the office of lieutenant governor. Plaintiffs adequately alleged an injury-in-fact that fell within their zone of interest and showed an actual legal stake in the matter sufficient to establish their standing in view of the lieutenant governor's role as the Senate's presiding officer (see NY Const, art IV, § 6) and because the lieutenant governor also has a casting vote in the Senate to break a tie on certain matters.

Trial -- Place of Trial -- Challenge to Governor's Appointment of Lieutenant Governor to Fill Vacancy -- Injunctive Relief

3. An action for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief challenging the Governor's appointment of an individual to fill a vacancy in the office of lieutenant governor could properly be maintained in Supreme Court, Nassau County. CPLR 6311 (1), which provides that a "preliminary injunction to restrain a public officer ... from performing a statutory duty may be granted only by the supreme court at a term in the department in which the officer ... is located or in which the duty is required to be performed," did not require that the action be brought in the Supreme Court at a term in the Third Judicial Department. If the Governor's appointment was not lawful, CPLR 6311 would not apply because the appointee would not be a public officer. If the appointee was lawfully appointed, plaintiffs proffered no grounds to restrain his performance of the duties of that office.

Governor -- Powers of Governor -- Authority to Appoint Lieutenant Governor to Fill Vacancy

4. The Governor lacked authority pursuant to Public Officers Law § 43 to appoint an individual to fill a vacancy in the office of lieutenant governor. NY Constitution, article IV, § 6 provides that where a vacancy occurs in the office of lieutenant governor, the temporary president of the Senate shall perform all the duties of that office. Consequently, Public Officers Law § 43, which authorizes the Governor to fill a vacancy in an elective office until the vacancy is filled by election, could not be constitutionally applied with respect to a vacancy in the office of lieutenant governor. The Governor's purported appointment was unlawful because no provision of the Constitution or of any statute provides for the filling of a vacancy in the office of lieutenant governor other than by election, and only the temporary president of the Senate is authorized to perform the duties of that office during the period of the vacancy.

People v. McCullen


834 KA 07-01775


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT
