Matter of Humane Socy. of U.S. v. Empire State Dev. Corp.


504252


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


53 A.D.3d 1013; 863 N.Y.S.2d 107; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6332; 2008 NY Slip Op 6495; 240 N.Y.L.J. 28



July 31, 2008, Decided 
July 31, 2008, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Humane Soc'y of the United States v Empire State Dev. Corp., 12 NY3d 701, 904 NE2d 503, 2009 NY LEXIS 116, 876 NYS2d 348 (N.Y., Feb. 11, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a humane society and members, sued respondents, the New York Public Authorities Control Board, Empire State Development Corporation (ESDC), and a farm, alleging ESDC violated the New York State Environmental Quality Review Act (SEQRA), ECL art. 8, and improperly denied their New York Freedom of Information Law (FOIL) request. The Albany County Supreme Court (New York) partially granted ESCS's motion to dismiss. Petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: ESDC approved the farm's grant request for funds to build manure treatment plants. It denied petitioners' FOIL request for a project finance memorandum and a cost-benefit analysis concerning the project on the ground that those documents were exempt from disclosure. The appellate court held petitioners lacked standing under State Finance Law § 123-b to challenge the ESDC's and Board's compliance with the New York Urban Development Corporation Act, L 1968, ch. 174, § 1. While one member who lived near the farm had standing to challenge the Board's and ESDC's SEQRA determinations, as the farm's proposed project was rationally classified as a type ch. action, the challenged determinations were exempt from review under 6 NYCRR 617.5(c)(3). Petitioners lacked common-law taxpayer standing since they were not challenging important governmental actions. But, under Public Officers Law § 87 of FOIL, ESDC had to disclose portions of the finance memorandum and cost-benefit analysis that contained purely factual data regarding the farm's financial and operating history. ESDC's opinions and projections as to economic issues, exempt intra-agency materials, could be redacted from those documents.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the dismissal of petitioners' challenge to the denial of their FOIL request and granted the petition to the extent that ESDC was directed to provide petitioners with redacted copies of the requested project finance memorandum and cost-benefit analysis. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Parties--Standing--Citizen Taxpayer Standing.--In connection with respondent farm's application for funding from respondent Empire State Development Corporation to expand its operations, petitioners lacked standing under State Finance Law § 123-b to maintain their causes of action challenging grant for noncompliance with Urban Development Corporation Act; under State Finance Law § 123-b (1), citizen taxpayer may challenge wrongful expenditure, misappropriation, misapplication or any other illegal or unconstitutional disbursement of state funds or state property; claims seeking review of state actor's alleged mismanagement of funds or arbitrary and capricious distribution of funds lawfully allocated to agency are not covered by section 123-b; here, petitioners challenged manner in which disbursement was conducted and distribution of funds to farm as arbitrary and capricious--furthermore, petitioners failed to establish that they had common-law taxpayer standing since they did not challenge any "important governmental actions" or raise issues involving "continued vitality of the constraints on power that lie at the heart of our constitutional scheme."

Parties--Standing--Environmental Quality Review.--In connection with respondent farm's application for funding from respondent Empire State Development Corporation (ESDC) to expand its operations, at least one petitioner had standing to challenge determination that ESDC improperly classified project as type II action under State Environmental Quality Review Act (see ECL art 8) inasmuch as that petitioner allegedly lived adjacent to site of proposed project, his drinking water supply would be affected by project, and he would be impacted by increased noise and truck traffic.

Environmental Conservation--Environmental Quality Review.--In connection with respondent farm's application for funding from respondent Empire State Development Corporation to expand its operations, state respondents properly characterized issuance of grant as type II action, i.e., action determined not to have significant impact on environment or otherwise precluded from environmental review under State Environmental Quality Review Act (see ECL art 8), that required no further action on their part (6 NYCRR 617.5 [a]); improvements to be funded by grant involved construction or maintenance of on-farm buildings to permit treatment of manure and raising of additional livestock; "[a]gricultural farm management practices," including manure management, are expressly deemed to be type II actions.

Records--Freedom of Information Law.--In connection with farm's application for funding from Empire State Development Corporation (ESDC) to expand its operations, ESDC improperly denied petitioners' request pursuant to Freedom of Information Law for project finance memorandum and cost-benefit analysis; portions of these documents contained purely factual data regarding farm's financial and operating history and, thus, those portions of documents were not exempt intra-agency materials (see Public Officers Law § 87 [2] [g] [i]); while ESDC's opinions and projections regarding economic issues addressed by these documents would be exempt intra-agency materials, historical, factual portions of documents should otherwise be disclosed with exempt projections redacted.

 

506 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Grasso


401620/04, 82


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


54 A.D.3d 180; 861 N.Y.S.2d 627; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5853; 2008 NY Slip Op 5970



July 1, 2008, Decided 
July 1, 2008, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 9, 2008.



DISPOSITION:  The court modified the trial court's order by denying the AG's motion for summary judgment as to the third cause of action, granting the CEO's motion to dismiss the second and third causes of action, and granted the chairman's motion to dismiss the seventh cause of action. The appeal from the grant of the AG's motion for summary judgment on the sixth cause of action as against the CEO was dismissed as moot. As so modified, the order was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a former CEO of the New York Stock Exchange (NYSE) and a former chairman of the NYSE compensation committee, sought review of an order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which, inter alia, granted plaintiff state attorney general's (AG's) motion for summary judgment on liability as to his third cause of action against the CEO and denied the CEO's motion for summary judgment dismissing the second and third claims.


OVERVIEW: The NYSE had been converted from a not-for-profit corporation into a for-profit entity. The issue raised was whether the AG had continuing authority to prosecute under N-PCL 720 (b). On appeal, the court modified the trial court's order, finding, inter alia, that the AG's authority to prosecute the second, third, and seventh causes of action seeking monetary relief lapsed with the merger. As to the third cause of action alleging breach of fiduciary duty by the CEO under N-PCL 717(b), a disputed issue of fact existed as to the compensation committee's and board's knowledge of the extent of the CEO's supplemental executive retirement plan (SERP) benefit. While the pending claims were not completely extinguished by virtue of Business Corporation Law § 906(b)(3), the public policy concerns supporting the AG's authority to bring the claims no longer existed as the public interest was not involved in the NYSE as a private corporation. Serious constitutional questions under N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 8(1), regarding state subsidization of a nongovernmental entity, and the concept of standing would be raised if § 720 (b) were construed to permit the continued prosecution of the claim by the AG.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's order by denying the AG's motion for summary judgment as to the third cause of action, granting the CEO's motion to dismiss the second and third causes of action, and granted the chairman's motion to dismiss the seventh cause of action. The appeal from the grant of the AG's motion for summary judgment on the sixth cause of action as against the CEO was dismissed as moot. As so modified, the order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Corporations -- Not-For-Profit Corporation -- Breach of Fiduciary Duty -- Restitution Claim Asserted by Attorney General against Former Chief Executive Officer of New York Stock Exchange 

1. In an action by the Attorney General against defendant, the former chairman and chief executive officer of the New York Stock Exchange, seeking restitution on behalf of the Exchange for alleged breaches of defendant's fiduciary duties under N-PCL 717 (a) and 720 (a) (1) for having influenced and accepted awards of excessive compensation during his tenure, Supreme Court erred in granting summary judgment to the Attorney General on liability, irrespective of whether the Attorney General's authority to prosecute the action lapsed when the Exchange became a for-profit entity. Supreme Court determined that defendant breached his fiduciary duties with respect to his participation in the Supplemental Executive Retirement Plan (SERP) based on its finding that the board of directors had not been "fully informed" about defendant's participation in that plan. However, from the deposition testimony of numerous directors and documentary evidence, a rational trier of fact could have concluded that the board was aware of the accumulated amount of defendant's SERP benefit in 2003 when it unanimously approved his 2003 employment agreement. Supreme Court further concluded with respect to defendant's participation in the Supplemental Executive Savings Plan (SESP), that "an amendment to the SESP was not made" as to permit pretermination payments when defendant was paid the money credited to his SESP account pursuant to his 2003 employment agreement, and that the payout of defendant's SESP money was therefore an "ultra vires" act by the Exchange. However, regardless of whether the 2003 employment agreement effectively amended the SESP as to defendant, the payout was not "ultra vires" as a matter of law, since the board was vested with "absolute discretion" to make modifications to the SESP "at any time" and "in such manner" as it deemed "appropriate or desirable."

Attorney General -- Powers -- Authority to Seek Restitution of Excessive Compensation from Officer or Director of Not-For-Profit Corporation Following Its Conversion into For-Profit Entity 

2. The Attorney General lacked legal authority under N-PCL 720 (b) to maintain an action against defendant, the former chairman and chief executive officer of the New York Stock Exchange, seeking restitution on behalf of the Exchange for alleged breaches of defendant's fiduciary duties in accepting awards of excessive compensation during his tenure since the Exchange ceased to be a not-for-profit corporation over which the Attorney General could exercise regulatory control and enforcement authority when it converted itself through a series of mergers into a for-profit company. While the conversion of the Exchange into a for-profit entity did not extinguish the claims asserted on behalf of the Exchange (see Business Corporation Law § 906 [b] [3]; N-PCL 908 [i] [A], [B]), the conversion divested the Attorney General of the authority or standing to prosecute them. N-PCL 720 (b) should not be construed to permit the Attorney General to continue prosecuting a cause of action seeking only monetary relief on behalf of a not-for-profit corporation after its conversion into a for-profit entity. The prosecution of such a postmerger cause of action would vindicate only the interests of private parties, not any public interest. Moreover, construing the statute to authorize the Attorney General's continued prosecution of a cause of action to redress an alleged wrong that was not perpetrated directly against the State would raise serious constitutional concerns as to whether such use of public funds falls within the constitutional prohibition against gifts of public funds to private entities (NY Const, art VII, § 8 [1]), and would also implicate separation of powers issues.

Declaratory Judgments -- When Remedy Appropriate 

3. In an action by the Attorney General against defendant, the former chairman and chief executive officer of the New York Stock Exchange, seeking restitution on behalf of the Exchange for alleged breaches of defendant's fiduciary duties under N-PCL 717 (a) and 720 (a) (1) for having influenced and accepted awards of excessive compensation during his tenure, defendant's motion to dismiss the Attorney General's cause of action seeking a judgment declaring that the Exchange "made unlawful, ultra vires payments to [defendant]" was properly denied. Because that cause of action was asserted solely against the Exchange, defendant had standing to seek its dismissal only if he would be bound, and therefore, aggrieved, by a determination underlying any judgment that the compensation was ultra vires. There was no basis for concluding that defendant would be bound by virtue of either the law of the case doctrine or collateral estoppel. Moreover, the absence of an actual controversy between the Attorney General and the Exchange was a reason to conclude that defendant would not be bound.

Contracts -- Employment Contracts -- Resignation Not Tantamount to Termination 

4. In an action by the Attorney General against defendant, the former chairman and chief executive officer of the New York Stock Exchange, seeking restitution on behalf of the Exchange for alleged breaches of defendant's fiduciary duties for having accepted awards of excessive compensation during his tenure, Supreme Court properly dismissed defendant's cross claims for breach of contract on the Exchange's motion for summary judgment in the absence of any evidence that defendant was actually terminated. Even if defendant was threatened with discharge, his resignation would not thereby have been rendered an involuntary act that was tantamount to a termination. In any event, defendant's failure to raise the claim that he was entitled to a payment under the Exchange's Supplemental Executive Retirement Plan even if he resigned prior to the Exchange's motion for summary judgment precluded him from raising such claim to avoid summary judgment.

Libel and Slander -- Public Figure -- Proof of Actual Malice 

5. In an action by the Attorney General against defendant, the former chairman and chief executive officer (CEO) of the New York Stock Exchange, seeking restitution on behalf of the Exchange for alleged breaches of defendant's fiduciary duties for having accepted awards of excessive compensation during his tenure, Supreme Court properly granted summary judgment dismissing defendant's cross claims for defamation and vindictive disparagement asserted against both the Exchange and defendant's successor as interim chair and CEO. Defendant failed to adduce evidence sufficient to raise a triable issue of fact with respect to whether the challenged statements made by his successor were made with "actual malice," i.e., that when defendant's successor made the statements he entertained serious doubts as to their truth or had a high degree of awareness of their probable falsity.

 

507 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Tommy L. Jenkins v. Piscotti


591 KAH 07-01176


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


52 A.D.3d 1207; 860 N.Y.S.2d 358; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5170; 2008 NY Slip Op 5132



June 6, 2008, Decided 
June 6, 2008, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought a habeas corpus petition against respondent sheriff. The Wayne County Court (New York) sustained the writ of habeas corpus and, inter alia, ordered the sheriff to release the inmate from his custody. The sheriff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of selling drugs and was sentenced to an indeterminate term of incarceration. He was released on presumptive release, but over two later, he was charged with operating a motor vehicle without a license. The inmate's operation of a motor vehicle without the written permission of his parole officer violated one of the conditions of his presumptive release. The trial court granted the inmate's petition pursuant to Executive Law § 259-j(3-a) upon determining that more than two years had elapsed since the inmate's release and that the release had not been revoked during that period of time. The trial court reasoned that, although Executive Law § 259-j(3-a) required termination of certain sentences after two years of unrevoked "parole," that section should not have been construed to grant presumptive releasees fewer rights than parolees. The appellate court held that this was error. Executive Law § 259-j expressly treated parolees and presumptive releasees separately. Further, Correction Law § 806(7) was not properly read in conjunction with Executive Law § 259-j(3-a) inasmuch as they were enacted at different times and did not cross-reference each other.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.


HEADNOTES

Parole--Presumptive Release.--Executive Law §259-j (3-a), which requires termination of certain sentences after two years of unrevoked parole, is not applicable to presumptive releasees; Correction Law § 806 (7), which provides that "[a]ny reference to parole and conditional release in this chapter shall also be deemed to include presumptive release," is not applicable to Executive Law §259-j (3-a).

 

508 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Sweeney v. Dennison


502689


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


52 A.D.3d 882; 858 N.Y.S.2d 845; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4838; 2008 NY Slip Op 4966



June 5, 2008, Decided 
June 5, 2008, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In CPLR art. 78 proceeding, respondent, chairman of the board of parole, sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which granted petitioner's application to terminate his sentence pursuant to Executive Law § 259-j(3-a).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had been convicted of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the third degree in 2003 and was sentenced to a two to six-year prison term. Petitioner was released from prison in 2004 after being granted presumptive release pursuant to Correction Law § 806 and sought termination of his sentence in 2006; the chairman denied that request. In the instant proceeding, the trial court found that Executive Law § 259-j(3-a) was applicable to periods of unrevoked presumptive release as well as unrevoked parole and granted the petition. On appeal, the court reversed. Based on the plain language of § 259-j(3-a), it was applicable only to parolees and not to those, like petitioner, who had been released pursuant to other programs. The court noted that throughout Executive Law art. 12-B, the legislature consistently distinguished between the various forms of supervised release from prison; thus, its failure to refer to presumptive releasees in § 259-j(3-a) indicated that the exclusion was intentional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Prisons and Prisoners--Calculation of Sentence.--Petitioner was not entitled to compel respondent to terminate his sentence pursuant to Executive Law §259-j (3-a) following two years of unrevoked presumptive release; by its plain language, section 259-j (3-a) is applicable only to parolees, not those who have been released pursuant to other programs.

 

509 of 1817 DOCUMENTS



Matter of DaimlerChrysler Co., LLC v. Billet


502652


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


51 A.D.3d 1284; 858 N.Y.S.2d 836; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4346; 2008 NY Slip Op 4575



May 22, 2008, Decided 
May 22, 2008, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner manufacturer brought a CPLR art. 78 proceeding against respondent commissioner, seeking review of a determination of respondent Tax Appeals Tribunal (New York) which sustained a sales and use tax assessment imposed under Tax Law arts. 28, 29.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer built motor vehicles which it sold to dealers, who then sold the vehicles to consumers. Pursuant to the New Car Lemon Law (Lemon Law), General Business Law § 198-a, the manufacturer accepted the return of 21 defective vehicles from consumers and provided comparable replacement vehicles that the manufacturer bought from franchised dealers. Because sales tax was paid on the purchase of the original vehicles and the replacement vehicles, the manufacturer sought a refund of the sales tax paid on the replacement vehicles. The appellate court found that the manufacturer was not the original vendor, that, while the property was returned and exchanged for a different vehicle, no direct exchange occurred, and that the manufacturer did not resell the replacement vehicles. The purchase of the replacement vehicles from the dealers constituted a second sale subject to sales tax under Tax Law § 1105. Neither the Lemon Law nor the Tax Law entitled the manufacturer to a sales tax refund. The manufacturer did not overcome beyond a reasonable doubt the strong presumption of constitutionality attached to the sales tax laws as they related to compliance with Lemon Law obligations.


OUTCOME: The proceeding was partially converted to an action for declaratory judgment, it was declared that General Business Law § 198-a and Tax Law § 1105(a) had not been shown to be unconstitutional as applied to the manufacturer, the remainder of the petition was dismissed, and the determination was confirmed.



HEADNOTES

Taxation--Sales and Use Taxes.--Petitioner, manufacturer of motor vehicles which it sold to franchised dealers who then sold vehicles to consumers, was not entitled to refund of sales tax it paid on replacement vehicles when it accepted return of 21 defective motor vehicles from consumers under New Car Lemon Law and provided comparable replacement vehicles that it purchased from franchised dealers; governing statutes and regulations required petitioner to pay sales tax on its purchase of replacement vehicles.

Matter of Coalition to Save Cedar Hill v. Planning Bd. of Inc. Vil. of Port Jefferson


2006-12004


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


51 A.D.3d 666; 857 N.Y.S.2d 669; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4104; 2008 NY Slip Op 4347



May 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Coalition to Save Cedar Hill v. Planning Bd. of Inc. Vill. of Port Jefferson, 11 NY3d 702, 894 NE2d 653, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 2582, 864 NYS2d 389 (2008)
Subsequent appeal at Matter of Coalition to Save Cedar Hill v. Planning Bd. of Inc. Vil. of Port Jefferson, 68 AD3d 762, 888 NYS2d 899, 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8846 (N.Y. App. Div. 2d Dep't, Dec. 1, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner coalition appeal a judgment by the Suffolk County Supreme Court (New York) that, inter alia, dismissed its CPLR art. 78 petition to review a resolution by respondent village clerk limiting the public's access to files that were the subject of a hearing.


OVERVIEW: After commencing a hybrid proceeding and action, the coalition attempted to serve the original petition/complaint, inter alia, upon respondent owners. When it realized that the title owners of the subject property were, in fact, the trusts, the coalition filed an amended petition/complaint naming the owners both individually and in their capacities as trustees. The appellate court found that, contrary to the coalition's contentions, it failed to meet the due diligence requirement for service of the original petition/complaint upon the owners, in their individual capacities under CPLR 308(4). Pursuant to CPLR 1001(b), the hybrid action and proceeding, with the exception of the eighth cause of action (concerning public access to the files), could not proceed in the absence of the actual title owners of the subject property. The trial court erred, however, in dismissing the eight cause of action since the owners did not have standing to seek its dismissal, since it sought declaratory relief only with respect to the village clerk. Accordingly, the coalitions' CPLR art. 78 petition should not have been dismissed in its entirety.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified by deleting the provision dismissing the cause of action related to the access to files, as so modified, the judgment was affirmed, and the cause of action was reinstated; the cross-motion to dismiss the amended petition/complaint was denied, the action insofar as asserted against the village clerk was severed, and the order was modified accordingly.


HEADNOTES

Process--Service of Process.--After commencing hybrid proceeding and action just before expiration of statute of limitations, appellants attempted to serve original petition/complaint upon respondents, in their individual capacities, by "nail and mail" service pursuant to CPLR 308 (4); upon later realizing that title owners of subject property were, in fact, trusts, appellants filed amended petition/complaint naming respondents both individually and in their capacities as trustees of subject trusts--appellants failed to meet due diligence requirement for service of original petition/complaint upon respondents, in their individual capacities, pursuant to CPLR 308 (4); moreover, hybrid action and proceeding could not proceed in absence of actual title owners of subject property--court did not err in declining to let hybrid proceeding and action continue without respondents pursuant to CPLR 1001 (b) and in declining to extend time for service pursuant to CPLR 306-b.

People v. Adams


3401, 2924/02


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


50 A.D.3d 433; 855 N.Y.S.2d 481; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3281; 2008 NY Slip Op 3308



April 15, 2008, Decided 
April 15, 2008, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Adams, 10 NY3d 955, 893 NE2d 445, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 2868, 863 NYS2d 139 (N.Y., July 24, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Bronx County Supreme Court (New York) that convicted him of attempted first-degree coercion; defendant claimed that his conviction violated Apprendi and that Penal Law § 135.65(1) unconstitutionally contained a mandatory presumption of "heinousness."


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found, inter alia, that defendant failed to preserve his claim that "heinous quality" was an element of first-degree coercion. On the contrary, in the situation of coercion by threat of injury to person or property, the elements of first- and second-degree coercion were the same, and the discretion to decide what was an exceptional case warranting prosecution for the lower degree was entrusted to the prosecutor. There was no Apprendi violation because the trial court did not increase the penalty for the crime of which defendant had been convicted based upon facts not found by the jury. Furthermore, the trial court did not instruct the jury that "heinousness" was presumed. Penal Law § 135.65(1) did not shift the burden of proving any element of the crime to the defendant. Even when viewed in a light most favorable to defendant, there was no reasonable view of the evidence that would support a finding that he committed the lesser offense but not the greater offense. Defendant's remaining claims were considered and rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgment was unanimously affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Coercion

Crimes--Lesser Included Offense

513 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Alvarez


6210/04, 1957


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


51 A.D.3d 167; 854 N.Y.S.2d 70; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2673; 2008 NY Slip Op 2773



March 27, 2008, Decided 
March 27, 2008, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Alvarez, 11 NY3d 785, 896 NE2d 97, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 3684, 866 NYS2d 611 (N.Y., Sept. 10, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), convicted defendant of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the third degree. The trial court imposed sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court excluded defendant's girlfriend from the courtroom during the trial testimony of two undercover police officers. The appellate court found that was proper. At a reopened Hinton hearing, one officer testified that he understood from what defendant had told him that the girlfriend was involved in selling drugs. The appellate court held that, because both undercovers continued to work in an undercover capacity in the same area where the sale occurred and defendant's girlfriend lived, a credible and legitimate threat existed that the girlfriend might spot the officers on the street during their operations and recognize them from court. This danger could not have been overlooked merely because neither defendant nor his associates had threatened either officer in the past. There was clear judicial error that justified the reopening of the initial Hinton hearing to introduce further evidence. The trial court also correctly excused the officers from disclosing their names due to safety concerns. Defendant's argument that the trial court erred in refusing to submit to the jury a lesser included offense instruction was unpreserved for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Right to Public Trial -- Closure of Courtroom--Reopening Hinton Hearing -- Exclusion of Defendant's Girlfriend

1. In a prosecution for criminal sale of a controlled substance based upon defendant's sale of cocaine to an undercover police officer, in which the prosecution sought to exclude all members of the public from the courtroom during the testimony of two undercover officers, with the exception of family members, the court properly exercised its discretion in reopening the Hinton hearing to correct its initial error in declining to exclude defendant's girlfriend and to receive additional testimony regarding the particularized threat posed by the girlfriend because she lived with defendant in the vicinity of the instant drug sale where the undercovers were actively operating and was also allegedly involved in the drug trade. Pursuant to established case law, the girlfriend's residence in the specific area of continuing undercover operations was itself sufficient to warrant her exclusion from the courtroom during the testimony of the undercover officers. Under the circumstances, there was clear judicial error that justified the prosecution's request to reopen the hearing to introduce further evidence. The court's discretionary determination to reopen the hearing was also warranted in view of the need for greater flexibility in Hinton hearings to protect the safety of undercover officers and their families.

Crimes -- Right of Confrontation -- Undercover Officers Testifying under Assumed Names

2. In a prosecution for criminal sale of a controlled substance based upon defendant's sale of cocaine to an undercover police officer, defendant's confrontation rights were not violated by the trial court's ruling permitting two undercover officers to testify under assumed names. The prosecution's evidence at the initial Hinton hearing was sufficient to establish that the officers should be excused from disclosing their names due to safety concerns, and such concerns outweighed defendant's interest in learning the names of the officers.

Crimes -- Appeal -- Preservation of Issue for Review -- Failure to Charge Lesser Included Offense

3. Defendant's argument that the trial court committed reversible error in refusing to submit to the jury a lesser included offense was unpreserved for appellate review. By failing to request that the court charge the lesser included offense or by failing to object to its refusal to charge, defendant failed to preserve an issue of law for review. Nor did the prosecutor's request that the court charge the lesser included offense suffice to preserve the issue on defendant's behalf.

Crimes -- Lesser Included Offense -- Controlled Substances

4. In a prosecution for criminal sale of a controlled substance in the third degree based upon defendant's sale of cocaine to an undercover police officer, although the issue was unpreserved for appellate review, the trial court properly denied the prosecutor's request to charge the lesser included offense of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the seventh degree, in light of the weak agency defense and the substantial evidence that defendant was acting as a drug seller. There was no reasonable view of the undercover's testimony that defendant unlawfully possessed narcotics, but did not sell them. In any event, any error was harmless in light of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt.

Matter of 10 E. Realty, LLC v. Incorporated Vil. of Val. Stream


2006-05848


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


49 A.D.3d 764; 854 N.Y.S.2d 461; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2545; 2008 NY Slip Op 2605



March 18, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by 10 E. Realty, LLC v. Inc. Vill. of Valley Stream, 11 NY3d 773, 896 NE2d 85, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 2606, 866 NYS2d 600 (2008)
Motion granted by 10 E. Realty, LLC v. Inc. Vill. of Valley Stream, 11 NY3d 912, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 208, 873 NYS2d 526 (N.Y., Jan. 15, 2009)
Reversed by, in part, Judgment entered by Matter of 10 E. Realty v. Inc. Vil. of Val. Stream, 12 NY3d 212, 907 NE2d 274, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 142, 879 NYS2d 361 (N.Y., Mar. 31, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner owners, and others, brought a CPLR art. 78 proceeding challenging a determination of the trustees of respondent village which authorized the village to close on the sale of a municipal parking lot to respondent buyer of the property and to enter into a purchase money mortgage with the buyer. The Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York), denied the petition and, in effect, dismissed the proceeding. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petition asserted, inter alia, that the subject parking lot was impressed with a public trust, and therefore could not be sold by the village for private use without specific authorization from the state legislature, and that taking back the purchase money mortgage constituted an unconstitutional loan by a municipality to a private entity. The appellate court found that the owners submitted no evidence showing that the parking lot at issue had been dedicated for public use through express provisions in a deed or legislative enactment, and thus failed to carry their burden of proof. In any event, Village Law § 1-102(1) empowered the village sell its property, and the owners cited no authority for the proposition that the village's power to dispose of surplus property under Village Law § 1-102(1) was constrained by the public trust doctrine where the property in question was not used for park or recreational purposes. However, the purchase money mortgage entered into by the village and the buyer was a "loan" and therefore was impermissible under the Gift or Loan Clause, N.Y. Const. art. VIII, § 1.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified by granting that branch of the petition which was to annul so much of the determination as authorized the village to enter into a purchase money mortgage with the buyer. As so modified, the judgment was affirmed.



HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations--Sale of Property--Public Trust Doctrine.--Village was authorized to close on sale of municipal parking lot with respondent but was not authorized to enter into purchase money mortgage with respondent--public trust doctrine did not preclude Village's sale of parking lot to respondent--however, financing arrangement between Village and Lincoln Realty constituted loan by municipality to private entity, and therefore was impermissible under Gift or Loan Clause of New York Constitution (NY Const, art VIII, § 1).

 

516 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Bernstein v. Feiner


2005-03677, 2005-06091


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


50 A.D.3d 212; 852 N.Y.S.2d 238; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1327; 2008 NY Slip Op 1338



February 13, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Bernstein v. Feiner, 11 NY3d 767, 896 NE2d 77, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 2627, 866 NYS2d 594 (2008)
Appeal dismissed by Matter of Bernstein v. Feiner, 11 NY3d 917, 902 NE2d 435, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 3, 874 NYS2d 1, 2009 NY Slip Op 265 (N.Y., Jan. 22, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, a town supervisor and a town, appealed an amended order and judgment by the Westchester County Supreme Court (New York) that granted petitioner resident's CPLR art. 78 petition to declare that Town Law § 232 prohibited the town from financing the cost of acquiring certain property for parkland by imposing a tax solely upon property owners residing in the unincorporated area of the town.


OVERVIEW: The park was purchased through the joint efforts of the town, the county, and the state. The resident, who lived in the unincorporated area of the town, claimed, and the trial court agreed, that since the park was open to all residents, its cost should be borne by all of the town's taxpayers. The appellate court found that the Finneran Law, L 1982, ch. 891, countered the effect of Town Law § 232 by directing that all costs of any public park were to be raised by the levy of a tax upon the land located outside of the incorporated town. Therefore, the town followed the "established procedure" by requiring the cost of the park be paid solely by residents in the unincorporated portions of the town. The fact that the town effectively opened the parks to all residents was not a basis upon which the town could alter the allocation of costs mandated by the Finneran Law. In addition, the Finneran Law was not applied. Instead of burdening the taxpayers of the unincorporated area in the amount of $ 10.9 million for a restricted park, the town has chosen to require that they pay one-third of that amount for an unrestricted park. Therefore, the resident was not entitled to CPLR art. 78 relief.


OUTCOME: The amended order and judgment were reversed, the petition for a judgment declaring that Town Law § 232 prohibited the allocation of costs to certain residents was denied, the CPLR art. 78 petition was denied in its entirety, and it was declared that the town correctly allocated the cost of the park.


HEADNOTES

Parks and Parkways -- Allocation of Cost of Park Lands

Respondent Town of Greenburgh properly imposed the cost of a park that is located in the unincorporated area of the Town of Greenburgh only upon the taxpayers of the Town's unincorporated area even though the park was open to use by all town residents, including those who resided in its incorporated villages. Ordinarily, the cost of parkland that was for the benefit of all the residents of a town would be borne by all of the town's taxpayers (see Town Law § 232). Special legislation applicable only in the Town of Greenburgh (L 1982, ch 891 [Finnernan Law]), however, required that the cost of the park be borne only by the taxpayers of the Town's unincorporated area. The Finneran Law also provided that the park may not be used by residents of the incorporated villages that did not choose to bear their share of the park's costs. Although the Town had chosen not to deny access to the park to residents of the noncontributing villages due to state and federal subsidy considerations even though the Finnernan Law required that it do so, full compliance with the Finneran Law by restricting use of the park was not the relief sought by petitioner and was not a basis upon which the Town might alter the allocation of costs.

People v. Estrella


1152 KA 07-01064


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


48 A.D.3d 1283; 851 N.Y.S.2d 793; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1141; 2008 NY Slip Op 1239



February 8, 2008, Decided 
February 8, 2008, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by People v. Estrella, 10 NY3d 818, 886 NE2d 817, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 1281, 857 NYS2d 52 (2008)
Affirmed by People v. Estrella, 10 NY3d 945, 893 NE2d 134, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 1926, 862 NYS2d 857 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Estrella v. New York, 129 S Ct 608, 172 L Ed 2d 457, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8409 (U.S., Nov. 17, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered by the Monroe County Court (New York), which convicted defendant, upon his plea of guilty, of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the second degree under Penal Law § 220.18(1).


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped a Mercedes Benz with a rear window that appeared to be heavily tinted. A tint meter indicated that the level of light transmittance was 10% and, thus, in violation of Vehicle and Traffic Law § 375(12-a)(b)(4) which did not allow light transmittance of less than 70%. The vehicle had Georgia license plates, and defendant indicated that he was Georgia resident. The officer obtained information that Georgia required light transmittance of 32%; however, that statute had been held unconstitutional prior to the stop. On appeal, the court affirmed. While it was argued that the officer knew that defendant was exempt under Vehicle and Traffic Law § 250(1) from the requirements of Vehicle and Traffic Law § 375(12-a)(b)(4) based on the vehicle's Georgia plates, the officer did not know whether defendant was the vehicle owner or whether the vehicle was properly registered in Georgia. Thus, the officer had probable cause to make the stop as the tint appeared to violate New York law. Using a narcotics-detection dog to sniff the vehicle's exterior during the lawful stop did not violate defendant's right against an unlawful search and seizure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Unlawful Search and Seizure.--Court properly refused to suppress evidence seized from defendant's vehicle--officer who knew only that vehicle with Georgia license plates was operated on public highway with rear window that appeared to be tinted with material having light transmittance of less than 70%, had requisite probable cause to believe that violation of Vehicle and Traffic Law § 375 (12-a) (b) (4) had occurred; stop of vehicle was necessary to obtain information whether Vehicle and Traffic Law § 250 (1) was applicable and thus whether defendant was exempt from requirements of section 375 (12-a) (b) (4).

Crimes--Unlawful Search and Seizure--Search Warrant.--Use of narcotics-detection dog to sniff exterior of vehicle during lawful stop of defendant's vehicle did not violate defendant's right to be protected from unlawful search and seizure, and upon obtaining positive indication from dog that drugs were present in vehicle, police properly obtained search warrant--hearing challenging veracity of affidavit in support of search warrant application was not warranted; although affiant stated that dog was certified narcotics-detection dog when in fact dog's certification had expired one month before search and dog was not recertified until two weeks after search, defendant failed to establish need for hearing, to show that affiant deliberately falsified allegations to demonstrate probable cause.

 

518 of 1817 DOCUMENTS



Graham v. Dunkley


2006-09666


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


50 A.D.3d 55; 852 N.Y.S.2d 169; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 593; 2008 NY Slip Op 958



February 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Graham v. Dunkley, 10 NY3d 835, 889 NE2d 484, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 1101, 859 NYS2d 607 (N.Y., Apr. 29, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lessor appealed an order by the Queens County Supreme Court (New York) that denied its motion to dismiss plaintiff's personal injury complaint; the lessor claimed that the Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, barred the plaintiff's vicarious liability action against it.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiff allegedly was injured in a two-car collision involving the lessor's car. The complaint did not allege any affirmative negligence on the part of the lessor, but sought damages from it based on vicarious liability. The appellate court found that the Graves Amendment aided in the regulation of the national market for leased and rented automobiles, which were "things in" interstate commerce. It also regulated an economic "class of activities" that, taken in the aggregate, substantially affected interstate commerce. Accordingly, the statute was constitutional, and the plaintiff's cause of action against the lessor based solely on vicarious liability failed to state a cause of action. Therefore, the trial court should have the lessor's motion to dismiss the complaint.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, and the lessor's motion to dismiss the complaint was granted.



HEADNOTES

Motor Vehicles--Imputing Driver's Negligence to Owner

Plaintiff's tort claim against the lessor of the vehicle involved in his automobile accident based solely upon vicarious liability was dismissed as being preempted by the federal statute which preempted Vehicle and Traffic Law §388 by barring vicarious liability actions against professional lessors and renters of vehicles (49 USC §30106). Supreme Court erred in finding the federal statute unconstitutional as exceeding congressional power under the Commerce Clause (US Const, art I, §8 [3]). The rental and lease of vehicles, and the conditions under which such transactions occur, were economic activities impacting the national market. Consequently, since the federal statute aided in the regulation of both instrumentalities of, and things in, interstate commerce, the statute was a constitutional exercise of congressional power to legislate under the Commerce Clause. The fact that the statute regulated an economic activity by preempting rules of state tort law did not make it unconstitutional.

Stern v. Bluestone


1926, 111895/05


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


47 A.D.3d 576; 850 N.Y.S.2d 90; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 583; 2008 NY Slip Op 611



January 31, 2008, Decided 
January 31, 2008, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Stern v. Bluestone, 10 NY3d 826, 888 NE2d 394, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 1004, 858 NYS2d 652 (2008)
Reversed by, Remitted by, Certified question answered by Stern v. Bluestone, 12 NY3d 873, 911 NE2d 844, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 1845, 883 NYS2d 782 (N.Y., June 11, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff recipient of faxes sued defendant attorney, the sender of the faxes, asserting causes of action under the Telephone Consumer Protection Act of 1991 (TCPA), 47 U.S.C.S. § 227. The Supreme Court, New York County (New York), granted the recipient's motion for partial summary judgment as to liability on his TCPA claim, and dismissed the attorney's second affirmative defense. The attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The attorney faxed to the recipient, who was also a lawyer, documents entitled "Attorney Malpractice Report." The recipient asserted that he never authorized the attorney to transmit the faxes, never had a business relationship with the attorney, and had never heard of the attorney until he received the faxes. The appellate court found that the trial court properly found the attorney liable to the recipient for the faxes sent to the recipient and a former subtenant on the recipient's fax machine. All of the faxes at issue were unsolicited advertisements. The faxes had the purpose and effect of influencing lawyers to procure the attorney's services, which were for legal malpractice claims. The faxes included the attorney's name and contact information, and indirectly advertised the commercial availability and quality of his services. Merely stating on the faxes that they were not advertisements did not make it so. The trial court also properly awarded treble damages because the attorney continued to send the faxes after he was served with a summons and complaint, and was found liable for TCPA violations in another case with similar facts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Consumer Protection--Telephone Consumer Protection Act.--In action alleging violation of Telephone Consumer Protection Act (TCPA), defendant was liable to plaintiff for faxes he sent to former subtenant on plaintiff's fax machine; otherwise, fax sender could easily avoid purpose of TCPA by putting incorrect name on addressee portion of fax.

Consumer Protection--Telephone Consumer Protection Act.--Faxes sent by defendant constituted unsolicited advertisements within meaning of Telephone Consumer Protection Act (TCPA); faxes at issue had purpose and effect of influencing recipients to procure defendant's services, which were for specialized field of legal malpractice claims; faxes included name of defendant's law firm and contact information; while faxes did not directly offer defendant's services as legal malpractice attorney, they indirectly advertised commercial availability and quality of such services; faxes invited contact for further information and listed two Web sites that boasted of defendant's specialization in attorney malpractice suits.

Consumer Protection--Telephone Consumer Protection Act.--Court properly awarded treble damages for willful or knowing violation of Telephone Consumer Protection Act (TCPA); since defendant was served with summons and complaint for possible violations of TCPA in prior case involving similar complaint by different plaintiff, he was fully aware of TCPA's proscriptions, yet he sent similar faxes to plaintiff even though at that point he knew or should have known that his conduct would violate statute. 

Limitation of Actions--What Statute Governs

 

520 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Boudreaux v. State of La., Dept. of Transp.


111287/06, 247


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


49 A.D.3d 238; 849 N.Y.S.2d 262; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 423; 2008 NY Slip Op 434



January 24, 2008, Decided 
January 24, 2008, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Boudreaux v. State of La., Dept. of Transp., 11 NY3d 321, 897 NE2d 1056, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 3300, 868 NYS2d 575 (N.Y., Oct. 28, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, Louisiana flood victims, sought review of an order entered by the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which denied their motion for leave to make two technical changes in a Louisiana judgment against defendants, the State of Louisiana, its Department of Transportation, and others (Louisiana), so that it could be docketed in New York and vacated the filing of that judgment.


OVERVIEW: The flood victims had obtained a judgment against Louisiana of over $91 million. While Louisiana had waived sovereign immunity under La. Const. art. XII, § 10(A), the flood victims, as judgment creditors, could only collect on the judgment by appropriation pursuant to La. Const. art. XII, § 10(C) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5109. The Louisiana legislature had declined to appropriate the funds necessary to pay the judgment, and the flood victims had attempted to docket the judgment in New York. On appeal, the court affirmed. Pursuant to the Full Faith and Credit Clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1, the New York courts could only give the Louisiana judgment the same preclusive effect that Louisiana would give under its own law. Additionally, under the doctrine of comity, the court made a voluntary decision to defer to the laws and policies of Louisiana, noting that the underlying events had no connection to New York. The Louisiana judgment was not a judgment within the meaning of CPLR § 5402 because the statute only contemplated an actual judgment that was enforceable in the jurisdiction in which it was rendered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.


HEADNOTES

Judgments -- Foreign Judgment -- Full Faith and Credit -- Judgment Unenforceable in Rendering Jurisdiction Not Subject to Enforcement in New York

A judgment obtained by plaintiffs against the Louisiana Department of Transportation in a Louisiana class action arising out of their property losses from a devastating flood could not be docketed and enforced in New York where the judgment remained unpaid due to the absence of an appropriation by the Louisiana legislature as provided by the laws and constitution of that state. The fact that the contingent award of damages to plaintiffs was denominated a "judgment" under Louisiana law did not render it a foreign judgment subject to enforcement pursuant to CPLR 5402. That statute contemplates a judgment that is enforceable in the rendering jurisdiction, and excludes a nominal judgment like the judgment awarded here that is unenforceable in the rendering jurisdiction. Under the Full Faith and Credit Clause (US Const, art IV, § 1), New York would only be required to give the Louisiana judgment the same preclusive effect that Louisiana would give under its own law. The Louisiana judgment could not be given any greater effect in New York than it would in Louisiana. Consequently, since plaintiffs' judgment would not become "payable" against the State of Louisiana until the state legislature appropriated the funds for that purpose, it could not be enforced in New York in an effort to circumvent Louisiana's laws and state constitution, especially where New York had no discernible interest in the matter.

 

521 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Khrapunskiy v. Doar


404175/04, 9369


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


49 A.D.3d 201; 852 N.Y.S.2d 40; 2008 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 316; 2008 NY Slip Op 351



January 17, 2008, Decided 
January 17, 2008, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Khrapunskiy v. Doar, 10 NY3d 926, 892 NE2d 395, 2008 N.Y. LEXIS 1902, 862 NYS2d 329 (2008)
Motion granted by Khrapunskiy v. Doar, 12 NY3d 746, 904 NE2d 834, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 81, 876 NYS2d 697 (2009)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by, Certified question answered by Khrapunskiy v. Doar, 12 NY3d 478, 909 NE2d 70, 2009 N.Y. LEXIS 943, 881 NYS2d 377 (N.Y., May 12, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Office of Temporary and Disability Assistance (agency) appealed an order by the New York County Supreme Court (New York) that, inter alia, granted plaintiff legal aliens' motion for summary judgment, enjoined the agency from failing to provide assistance to the aliens and the class in Social Services Law § 209(2), directed that the agency provide retroactive benefits, and certified the class.


OVERVIEW: The legal aliens were originally eligible for Federal Supplemental Security Income (SSI) and additional state payments (ASP), but became ineligible solely by reason of their failure to become American citizens within the allotted seven years. The court found that the Legislature intended to guarantee all legally resident aged, blind, and disabled persons, citizen and non-citizen alike, with assistance at the more generous level set forth in § 209(2). The aliens were not seeking SSI or ASP; they were seeking to increase their monthly grants for safety net assistance pursuant to Social Services Law § 131-a(2) to the standard of monthly need set by Social Services Law § 209(2). The State could not stop paying benefits at the level it established in 1974 merely because the federal government chose to deny SSI benefits to a particular subgroup. The class certification was affirmed with the proviso that the ultimate eligibility determination would rest with the agency, provided, of course, that such determination was not based on improper factors or considerations. The agency's remaining arguments were considered and found to be unavailing.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Social Services -- Public Assistance -- Additional State Payments for Eligible Aged, Blind and Disabled Persons -- Impermissible Discrimination against Legal Aliens 

Plaintiffs, the class of elderly, blind and disabled persons who were legal resident aliens of New York and who became ineligible to continue receiving federal Supplemental Security Income (SSI) and federally administered additional state payments (ASP) by virtue of the Personal Responsibility and Work Opportunity Reconciliation Act of 1996 (8 USC § 1601 et seq.) solely because of their failure to have become American citizens within the allotted seven years, thereby relegating them to receiving benefits at the lower standard of need set forth by Social Services Law § 131-a (2) (see Social Services Law § 209 [1] [a] [iv]), were entitled under the equal protection guarantees of the State Constitution to receive the same level of public assistance benefits as similarly-situated aged, blind or disabled citizens as set forth in Social Services Law § 209 (2). Plaintiffs were thus entitled to state safety net assistance plus some form of supplement to bring their benefits up to the ASP level. The standard of monthly need in Social Services Law § 209 (2) set forth the minimum income standard determined by the Legislature to meet the needs of New York's elderly, blind and disabled residents (see NY Const, art XVII, § 1). The State could not stop paying benefits at the level set forth in that statute merely because the federal government chose to deny SSI benefits to a particular subgroup of those the State had previously and continued to classify as the needy aged, blind and disabled.
