People v. Santiago


584 KA 99-01149


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


41 A.D.3d 1172; 839 N.Y.S.2d 369; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7153; 2007 NY Slip Op 4913



June 8, 2007, Decided 
June 8, 2007, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Santiago, 9 N.Y.3d 964, 878 N.E.2d 617, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 3614, 848 N.Y.S.2d 33 (2007)
Appeal after remand at People v. Santiago, 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8415 (N.Y. App. Div. 4th Dep't, Nov. 12, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Monroe County Court (New York), which convicted defendant, upon a jury verdict, of murder in the first degree, murder in the second degree, and attempted murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress certain physical evidence seized from a kennel behind his residence, as the record established that defendant's mother freely and repeatedly consented to a search of the residence and the area around the house. Also, defendant's statements to the police were properly admitted in evidence at trial, as defendant was not placed under arrest until after he was identified as the perpetrator by two of the surviving victims at the hospital, at which time the police had probable cause to arrest him. However, the court agreed with defendant that the second degree felony murder convictions had to be reversed, and those counts of the indictment had to be dismissed pursuant to CPL 300.40(3)(b), because defendant was also convicted of first degree intentional felony murder, and felony murder (pursuant to Penal Law § 125.25(3)) was a lesser-included crime under intentional felony murder. Also, defendant's sentences for first degree murder had to be vacated on the ground that they were imposed after the court gave the deadlock instruction contained in CPL 400.27(10), which was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified on the law by reversing those parts convicting defendant of murder in the second degree and dismissing those counts of the indictment, and by vacating the sentences imposed for murder in the first degree. As modified the judgment was affirmed, and the matter was remitted to the trial court for resentencing on the murder in the first degree counts.


HEADNOTES  [***1] 

Crimes--Unlawful Search and Seizure--Consent to Search.--Court properly refused to suppress evidence seized from kennel behind defendant's residence--defendant's mother consented to search of residence, and told officers that they could search area around house, but that they could not enter outdoor kennel because dog confined there could be controlled only by defendant; officers waited until Animal Control officers arrived and secured dog before searching that area--defendant's mother gave comprehensive consent to search house and areas surrounding it, and her indication that police could not enter kennel based on presence of dog was insufficient to impose limitation on or constitute revocation of consent.

Crimes--Arrest--Probable Cause.--Defendant's statements to police were admissible; defendant was not placed under arrest until after he was identified as perpetrator by two of surviving victims at hospital, at which time police had probable cause to arrest him; fact that he was placed in handcuffs prior to showup identification at hospital did not transform otherwise valid detention of defendant for showup purposes into full-blown arrest.

Crimes--Confession.--Defendant's contention that his statements to police should have been suppressed because, before he was advised of his Miranda rights, he told them that he had previously sold drugs, was rejected; that statement did not require suppression of post-Miranda statements because it was nonresponsive to officer's question that immediately preceded statement concerning drugs and thus was spontaneous; officer's question was permissible because its purpose was to determine whether defendant was under influence of drugs.

Crimes--Lesser Included Offense--Murder

Crimes--Sentence--First Degree Murder--Deadlock Instruction.--Sentences imposed for first degree murder were vacated since they were imposed after court gave deadlock instruction contained in CPL 400.27 (10)--instruction at issue violated NY Constitution because vote for life imprisonment or death, driven by fear that defendant might be parole-eligible if jurors fail to reach unanimity, does not satisfy heightened standard of reliability required by State Constitution.

Crimes--Jurors--Selection of Jury.--Defendant failed to make requisite prima facie showing of discrimination by prosecutor with respect to prosecutor's use of peremptory challenges against female prospective jurors--although prosecutor exercised majority of his peremptory challenges against female prospective jurors, he peremptorily excused less than 50% of women in jury pool from which petit jury was chosen; consequently, because no showing was made beyond disproportionate number of strikes against women, defendant's claims fell short of requisite burden.

People v. Jenner


16200


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


39 A.D.3d 1083; 835 N.Y.S.2d 501; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5120; 2007 NY Slip Op 3599



April 26, 2007, Decided 
April 26, 2007, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v. Jenner, 9 N.Y.3d 845, 872 N.E.2d 885, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 2174, 840 N.Y.S.2d 772 (2007)
Related proceeding at People v. VanPatten, 48 A.D.3d 30, 850 N.Y.S.2d 213, 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13258 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, 2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Certificate of appealability denied Jenner v. Brown, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 35290 (N.D.N.Y, Apr. 9, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Madison County Court (New York) denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charges in the interests of justice, he was convicted of making a terroristic threat (Penal Law § 490.20) and was sentenced to 15 years to life imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant told an employee of the county department of social services (DSS) he was going to get a gun and "take care of" a his girlfriend's DSS caseworker and the caseworker's supervisor since "he had nothing to lose"-- he had terminal liver disease. The appellate court held the testimony established that he threatened to kill DSS employees, that he thereby intended to coerce them to influence DSS policy, that he intended through murder to interfere with the DSS's enforcement of its policy, and that his words and conduct caused reasonable fear of the imminent commission of such a murder. Denial of his motion for dismissal in the interest of justice, due to his poor health, was not an abuse of discretion. His counsel was not ineffective for failing to move to disqualify the district attorney, as there was no basis for such a motion. He was properly restrained by leg shackles during trial due to his prior assault conviction, the serious nature of the charges, his threats to witnesses, and his statement that he had nothing to lose because he was dying. As he was a persistent felony offender under Penal Law § 70.10(1), the sentence of 15 years to life was the minimum permissible one.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law--Validity of Statute.--Although issue was unpreserved for review, Penal Law § 490.20 was not unconstitutional as applied--statutory language sufficiently apprises persons of ordinary intelligence of type of conduct that is forbidden and provides law enforcement officials with clear standards for enforcement--defendant claimed that his conduct was not what Legislature had in mind when it enacted statute after terroristic attacks of September 11, 2001 and he should not be labeled terrorist--regardless of Legislature's intent, plain words of Penal Law § 490.20 clearly inform public and law enforcement officials of conduct forbidden by statute. 

Crimes--Making Terroristic Threat.--Evidence was sufficient to support conviction of making terroristic threat--testimony of Department of Social Services (DSS) employees, investigator and other witnesses established that defendant threatened to kill DSS employees, threat was intended to intimidate or coerce public employees to influence DSS's policy regarding contact between children and sex offenders, defendant intended through such murder to interfere with DSS's conduct of enforcing this policy, and his words and conduct caused reasonable fear of imminent commission of such murder; statute eliminates as defenses lack of intent or capability of committing murders, and that threat was made to someone other than person subject to threat (see Penal Law § 490.20 [2])--prosecution's witnesses established each element of offense.

Crimes--Indictment--Dismissal in Interest of Justice.--Dismissal of indictment charging making terroristic threat was not warranted in interest of justice; despite defendant's poor health and his argument that his actions did not fit typical definition of terrorism so as to subject him to these charges, no injustice was likely to result from prosecuting him for threatening lives of public servants.

Crimes--Right to Counsel--Effective Representation

Crimes--Fair Trial.--Defendant was not deprived of fair trial due to court's order that he be restrained during trial--court instructed jury three separate times that use of restraints was ordinary security measure and could not be used as any indication of guilt--court articulated reasons for requiring restraints and took efforts to avoid any prejudice to defendant.

People v. Berlin


502, Ind. 5375/05


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


39 A.D.3d 351; 835 N.Y.S.2d 54; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4845; 2007 NY Slip Op 3331



April 19, 2007, Decided 
April 19, 2007, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v. Berlin, 9 N.Y.3d 840, 872 N.E.2d 880, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 2296, 840 N.Y.S.2d 767 (2007)
Related proceeding at Matter of Berlin v. Evans, 2011 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1757 (N.Y. Sup. Ct., Apr. 11, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, New York County, New York, convicted defendant, after a jury trial, of sexual abuse in the first degree, under Penal Law § 130.65(3), and sentenced him to a term of 5 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The instant court found that the verdict was based on legally sufficient evidence. The trial court properly found that the child victim was capable of giving unsworn testimony, and her account of the crime was consistent with defendant's statements to the police. Moreover, there was additional evidence establishing defendant's opportunity to commit the crime, and connecting him to it. Defendant's therapist reported to law enforcement authorities the substance of statements defendant had made relating to an act of sexual abuse of the victim. Even if the therapist's testimony was improper, the error was harmless because defendant waived any privilege when he spoke to the police and gave them the same information he provided to his therapist. Nor was defendant entitled to a new trial on account of his claim premised on the rule of completeness. The trial court correctly determined that an endangering the welfare of a child charge was not a lesser included offense of the sexual abuse charge. Thus, the trial court was not required to submit the endangering charge to the jury. Defendant's claim that the sentence was unconstitutional as applied to him was unpreserved and without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Corroboration as to Sex Offenses.--Verdict was based on sufficient evidence; child victim's account of crime was consistent with defendant's statements to police, and child victim's account and defendant's statements properly corroborated each other; moreover, there was additional evidence establishing defendant's opportunity to commit crime, and connecting him to it.

Crimes--Witnesses--Testimony of Therapist in Sex Case.--In prosecution for sexual abuse, in which defendant's therapist was permitted to testify about statements defendant had made relating to act of sexual abuse of child victim, defendant waived any privilege regarding such testimony when he spoke to police and gave them same information he had provided to therapist.

Crimes--Appeal--Preservation of Issue for Review

Crimes--Harmless and Prejudicial Error.--Although defendant failed to preserve issue for review, any error in precluding testimony that defendant told his therapist that he was "revulsed" by child's presence was harmless; defendant admitted he had rubbed child's "chest and vaginal area" and that he had "played with the little girl," and statement about defendant's revulsion did not indicate when he became revolted.

Crimes--Lesser Included Offense.--Endangering welfare of child was not lesser included offense of sexual abuse, since it was possible for defendant to have touched victim in manner constituting sexual abuse without requisite mens rea necessary for endangering offense.

 

547 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Taylor


2005-07382


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


42 A.D.3d 13; 835 N.Y.S.2d 241; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4538; 2007 NY Slip Op 3111



April 10, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal dismissed by, Motion dismissed by People v. Taylor, 9 N.Y.3d 887, 874 N.E.2d 731, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 2360, 842 N.Y.S.2d 766 (2007)
Application granted by People v. Taylor, 2010 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 613 (N.Y. Sup. Ct., Mar. 15, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed an order of the County Court, Westchester County (New York), which granted defendant's motion to be excluded from the classification and registration requirements of the New York Sex Offender Registration Act (SORA), specifically Correction Law art. 6-C, after he was convicted of kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: There was no sexual misconduct involved in the offense. The appellate court held that it was not irrational or unconstitutional to apply SORA to defendant. The statutory definitions made it clear that "sex offenders" applied to offenders whose crime had no apparent sexual component. The New York legislature's finding that registration of sex offenders would allow local law enforcement officials to resolve incidents involving sexual abuse and exploitation promptly and to alert the community when necessary applied equally to child abductors. Since unlawful imprisonment and kidnapping involved either the restraint or abduction of the victim and such conduct was a frequent precursor to a sex offense, the legislature could reasonably have found that kidnappers should be required to register. The legislature found that the policies effectuated in SORA brought New York into compliance with the federal crime control act, now codified at 42 U.S.C.S. § 14071. Finally, whether in common parlance defendant was a sex offender, or his offense was a sex offense, was of no legal significance as the legislature had rationally chosen to categorize defendant or the offense as such.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was reversed. Defendant's motion to be excluded from the classification and registration requirements of Correction Law art. 6-C was denied. The matter was remitted to the trial court for a new SORA risk level assessment hearing and a new determination thereafter.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Application of Sex Offender Registration Act to Convicted Child Kidnapper 

Defendant's 1976 conviction of kidnapping in the first degree (Penal Law § 135.25 [1]) involving a person less than 17 years old required him to register as a "sex offender" under the Sex Offender Registration Act (SORA) (Correction Law § 168-a [1], [2] [a] [i]), even though there was no apparent sexual component to his crime. SORA's application to defendant was constitutionally permissible, and did not violate his substantive due process right to be free from arbitrary, capricious and irrational legislation. In light of the facts of defendant's particular crime, it was not irrational to classify him a "sex offender" and subject him to the registration requirements of SORA. The protection of children from the dangers of sexual predators constitutes a legitimate and compelling, governmental purpose. The Legislature could reasonably have concluded in furtherance of that purpose that child kidnappers should be required to register as "sex offenders," even in the absence of sexual contact, because such conduct is a frequent precursor to a sex offense. Furthermore, the inclusion of defendant's crime as "sex offense" in the State's registration program was necessary to comply with federal standards so that the State would remain eligible to receive federal aid (see 42 USC § 14071 [a] [3] [A] [i]). The Legislature could rationally have determined that it was in the public interest to establish a registration program in compliance with federal law, and, on that basis, have also concluded rationally that requiring the registration of convicted kidnappers furthered the legitimate purposes of the statute, even in the absence of a sexual component to the kidnapping.

Garber v. Board of Trustees of State Univ. of N.Y.


2006-01073, (Index No. 8179/05)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


38 A.D.3d 833; 834 N.Y.S.2d 203; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4008; 2007 NY Slip Op 2700



March 27, 2007, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for declaratory and injunctive relief, plaintiffs, hotels and others, appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County (New York), which granted a motion by defendants, university trustees and others, to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that defendants' conduct in entering into a contract with a private developer for construction of a hotel on a university campus was illegal and constituted an unconstitutional gift of state property. State Finance Law § 123-b granted citizen taxpayers standing to bring an action for equitable or declaratory relief against an officer or employee of the state to prevent a wrongful expenditure, misappropriation, misapplication, or any other illegal or unconstitutional disbursement of state funds or state property. The statute was narrowly construed as a grant of standing to correct clear illegality of official action, but did not allow the interposition of litigating plaintiffs and the courts into the management and operation of public enterprises. The appellate court held that the trial court correctly determined that the proposed construction proceeded in accordance with specific enabling legislation. Within the time frame allowed by the enabling legislation, the university and the developer entered into a ground lease and the ground lease was approved by state officials as required by the statute.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed, with one bill of costs to respondents appearing separately and filing separate briefs.


HEADNOTES  [***1] 

Parties--Standing.--Plaintiffs lacked standing as citizen taxpayers under State Finance Law § 123-b to maintain action for judgment to permanently enjoin defendants from entering into contracts for construction of hotel and conference center on portion of campus of State university unless they comply with competitive bidding laws--plaintiffs' conclusory allegations of illegality and gift of State property were contradicted by evidence that proposed hotel construction proceeded in accordance with enabling legislation.

Matter of Foley v. Masiello


150 CA 06-02004


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


38 A.D.3d 1201; 833 N.Y.S.2d 342; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3420; 2007 NY Slip Op 2183

March 16, 2007, Entered


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Limitation of Actions - Four-Month Statute of Limitations.--Petition was dismissed as time-barred under four-month statute of limitations applicable to CPLR article 78 proceedings--petitioners challenged constitutionality of respondent authority's action as applied to their members, not constitutionality of underlying state legislation that created respondent and authorized it to impose wage freeze if necessary; article 78 proceeding is generally proper vehicle to determine whether statute, ordinance or regulation has been applied in unconstitutional manner; although CPLR article 78 proceeding is not proper vehicle to challenge legislative act, it is customary procedural vehicle for review of administrative determinations; respondent's action in imposing wage freeze was administrative rather than legislative given its individualized application, limited duration and informal adoption.

People v. Gomez


286 KA 05-02660


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


38 A.D.3d 1271; 832 N.Y.S.2d 369; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3547; 2007 NY Slip Op 2256



March 16, 2007, Decided 
March 16, 2007, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Gomez v. Lempke, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 103138 (W.D.N.Y., Sept. 8, 2010)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Vacated by People v. Gomez, 122 A.D.3d 1345, 995 N.Y.S.2d 522, 2014 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7841, 2014 NY Slip Op 7905 (N.Y. App. Div. 4th Dep't, 2014)
Different results reached on rehearing at People v. Gomez, 2016 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3180 (N.Y. App. Div. 4th Dep't, Apr. 29, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Steuben County Court (New York), convicting defendant, upon a jury verdict, of burglary in the second degree, attempted assault in the second degree (Penal Law §§ 110.00, 120.05(1)), assault in the second degree (Penal Law § 120.05(2)), criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree, criminal mischief in the fourth degree, petit larceny and tampering with physical evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he received ineffective assistance of counsel because his first assigned counsel did not inform the People that defendant wanted to testify before the grand jury. The appeals court rejected that contention. Viewing the evidence, the law, and the circumstances of the case, in totality and as of the time of the representation, defendant received meaningful representation. The appeals court also rejected defendant's claim that the County Court erred in allowing the People to introduce evidence of his prior drug dealing activity. That evidence was relevant with respect to the issue of defendant's motive for the assault, and the probative value of that evidence outweighed its prejudicial effect. The appeals court rejected defendant's contention that the persistent felony offender statutes were unconstitutional, and the appeals court concluded that the County Court properly adjudicated defendant a persistent felony offender. The sentence was not unduly harsh or severe.


OUTCOME: The judgment was unanimously affirmed.


HEADNOTES  [***1] 

Crimes--Proof of Other Crimes.--Evidence of defendant's prior drug dealing activity was relevant with respect to issue of defendant's motive for assault, and probative value of that evidence outweighed its prejudicial effect.

Matter of McNear v. State of New York


99025


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


38 A.D.3d 1093; 831 N.Y.S.2d 591; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2832; 2007 NY Slip Op 2017



March 15, 2007, Decided 
March 15, 2007, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by McNear v. State, 9 NY3d 801, 872 NE2d 252, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 1629, 840 NYS2d 566 (N.Y., June 27, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed an order by the Clinton County Supreme Court (New York) that denied his habeas corpus application for poor person status; the inmate claimed that the lower court's erred in finding that his attorney's certificate of merit was in error.


OVERVIEW: The lower court declined to issue a writ of habeas corpus to the inmate and took no action on the inmate's request for poor person status pending receipt of an attorney's certificate of merit under CPLR 1101(b) within 60 days. While the inmate subsequently filed a purported certificate, it was not executed by an attorney; rather, the inmate authored it himself. The lower court found the certificate deficient and denied the inmate's request for permission to proceed as a poor person. The appellate court found that even if the lower court erred in requiring a certificate executed by an attorney, the inmate's averments in regard to his case did not constitute an adequate statement of merit. The inmate's remaining contentions were considered and rejected for lack of merit.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Parties--Poor Person Status.--Court did not err in denying petitioner's request for permission to proceed as poor person on ground that attorney's certificate of merit was executed by petitioner and not by attorney--under CPLR 1101 (b), court may direct filing of attorney's certificate of merit when party is seeking poor person relief; CPLR 1101 (a) requires court to review poor person applications on their merits; this necessity was not obviated by fact that applicant was prison inmate--even if court erred in requiring certificate executed by attorney, petitioner's averments did not constitute adequate statement of merit.

 

553 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


14875, 16661


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


38 A.D.3d 1057; 832 N.Y.S.2d 312; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2861; 2007 NY Slip Op 1992



March 15, 2007, Decided 
March 15, 2007, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 1, 2007.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), of the crime of burglary in the second degree under Penal Law § 140.25. He was sentenced as a second felony offender under Penal Law § 70.02 to a prison term with post-release supervision. The trial court, without a hearing, entered an order denying defendant's motion under CPL 440.10 and 440.20 to vacate the judgment and set aside the sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that she was alone in her apartment during the day and, upon hearing noises, she came out of her bedroom and found defendant and another man in her living room holding large garbage bags. They were hunched over her television disconnecting the electronic components, and complied when she ordered them to leave. Shortly thereafter, defendant and another man were apprehended a few blocks away and the victim identified defendant as one of the intruders. On appeal, the court found that the weight of the credible evidence amply supported the verdict. Additionally, defendant neither overcame the presumption of constitutionality attached to the legislative classification of the crime as a violent felony offense under Penal Law § 70.02(1)(b), nor established any due process deprivation resulting from it. Further, a factual determination that defendant engaged in violence was not a prerequisite to classifying the crime under Penal Law § 70.02, as the conviction alone qualified defendant for the enhanced sentencing that statute provided. Finally, there was no extraordinary circumstance or abuse of discretion warranting a sentence reduction in the interest of justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment and the order were affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Burglary.--Evidence was sufficient to establish that defendant knowingly and unlawfully entered dwelling "with intent to commit a crime therein" (Penal Law § 140.25 [2]); People established defendant's general intent to commit crime through victim's account of defendant's culpable conduct inside apartment and defendant's unauthorized presence supported inference of his subjective intent to commit crime therein; People were not required to prove what particular crime was intended as they never expressly limited their case--verdict was not against weight of evidence.

Crimes--Sentence--Burglary--Violent Felony Offense.--Defendant's challenge to court's imposition of sentence for burglary in second degree as violent felony offense (see Penal Law § 70.02 [1] [b]) was rejected--defendant challenged as unconstitutional or illegal legislative classification of burglary in second degree as violent felony because no violence was used or proven--Legislature's classification of burglaries of dwellings as class C or higher as violent felonies was not unreasonable; there was rational basis for classification, namely, potential for violence in all home invasions--defendant's meritless disagreement with legislative classification of crime did not raise issue under Apprendi v New Jersey.

People v. Cuadrado


8401, SCI 15082/91


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


37 A.D.3d 218; 830 N.Y.S.2d 65; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1787; 2007 NY Slip Op 1197



February 13, 2007, Decided 
February 13, 2007, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal granted by People v Cuadrado, 8 NY3d 951, 868 NE2d 245, 2007 NY LEXIS 1269, 836 NYS2d 562 (2007)
Appeal granted by People v Cuadrado, 2007 NY App Div LEXIS 4591 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, Apr. 12, 2007)
Motion granted by People v Cuadrado, 8 NY3d 995, 870 NE2d 155, 2007 NY LEXIS 1486, 838 NYS2d 836 (2007)
Affirmed by People v Cuadrado, 9 NY3d 362, 880 NE2d 861, 2007 NY LEXIS 3713, 850 NYS2d 375 (N.Y., Dec. 18, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People sought review of an order entered by the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which granted defendant's motion pursuant to CPL 440.10 and vacated a prior judgment convicting defendant of assault in the first degree, upon his plea of guilty to a superior court information charging him with that crime, and sentencing him to a term of 4 to 12 years.


OVERVIEW: Over the course of two days, defendant committed two armed robberies. The indictments arising from both incidents were consolidated but did not include an assault charge arising from the first robbery. Defendant entered into a plea agreement in full satisfaction of both indictments, including an agreement to waive indictment and be prosecuted by a superior court information charging him with assault in the first degree and to plead guilty thereto. Defendant raised an excessive sentence claim on direct appeal, which was denied. With respect to defendant's motion to vacate, the trial court agreed that the information was jurisdictionally defective. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the failure to comply with the statutory requirements for waiving indictment did not need to be addressed based on the language of CPL 440.10. CPL 440.10(2)(c) mandated that defendant's motion to vacate be denied because the issue regarding any jurisdictional defect relating to the information could have been raised on direct appeal but was not. The court noted that no language in the provision indicated that it was inapplicable when the issue raised was a jurisdictional defect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, denied defendant's motion, and reinstated the judgment of conviction and sentence.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Appeal--Preservation of Issue for Review.--Bar of CPL 440.10 (2) (c) was applicable to jurisdictional defect posited by defendant, who had waived indictment and pleaded guilty to superior court information charging him with felony, and moved to vacate judgment 12 years later on ground that information was jurisdictionally defective, issue which he had failed to raise on direct appeal; provisions of CPL 440.10 (1) and (2), when read together, make it clear that all jurisdictional challenges to conviction that are reviewable on trial record must be raised on direct appeal.

Crimes--Right to Counsel--Effective Representation

Martinez 2001 v. New York City Campaign Fin. Bd.


9083, Index 101420/05


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


36 A.D.3d 544; 829 N.Y.S.2d 55; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 867; 2007 NY Slip Op 562



January 30, 2007, Decided 
January 30, 2007, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Matter of Martinez v. New York City Campaign Finance Board, 2008 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 9636 (N.Y. Sup. Ct., Dec. 15, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a City Councilman and his campaign committee (Councilman), filed suit against defendant New York City Campaign Finance Board. The Supreme Court, New York County (New York), granted the Councilman's motion for a preliminary injunction such that it restrained the Board from conducting a hearing on certain alleged violations and any further adjudication of several alleged violations, and denied the Board's cross-motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The Board appealed. The Board issued a violation notice claiming that the Councilman violated the New York City Campaign Finance Act. The appellate court held that the exhaustion of administrative remedies doctrine was not always inapplicable in proceedings seeking a writ of prohibition or mandamus. The Councilman's claim that his due process rights were violated because the allegations were not specific enough did not allege the type of unconstitutional agency action that was excepted from the exhaustion doctrine. The Councilman had an adequate remedy at law by way of a CPLR art. 78 proceeding. It was within the Board's discretion whether to publicize the names of those who violated the Act. There was no basis to presume that any adverse findings would be made against the Councilman, that such adverse findings would result from inadequate notice, or that the Board intended to publish such findings prior to completion of an art. 78 review. Thus, the type of reputational harm that was alleged by the Councilman did not qualify as irreparable injury since any individual who was the subject of an administrative proceeding faced the possibility of reputational harm.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. The motion for injunctive relief was denied and the cross-motion to dismiss was granted. The Clerk was directed to enter judgment in favor of the Board dismissing the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Administrative Law--Failure to Exhaust Administrative Remedies.--In action arising from postelection audit by defendant city campaign finance board, in which plaintiffs sought injunction restraining defendant from conducting administrative hearing regarding alleged violations of Campaign Finance Law, court erred when it found that exhaustion requirement was inapplicable because plaintiffs were seeking relief in nature of mandamus to compel.

Administrative Law--Failure to Exhaust Administrative Remedies.--Plaintiffs, who accused defendant city campaign finance board of providing constitutionally deficient notice of alleged violations of Campaign Finance Law, did not establish exception to exhaustion requirement based on alleged violation of due process; exception is limited to situations where statute or administrative scheme itself is alleged to be unconstitutional, thus undermining legality of entire proceeding.

Administrative Law--Failure to Exhaust Administrative Remedies.--Court erred when it found that plaintiffs would suffer irreparable injury in absence of injunctive relief restraining defendant city campaign finance board from conducting hearing regarding alleged violations of Campaign Finance Law, and that therefore, exception to exhaustion requirement was applicable; potential harm to plaintiff's reputation was based on speculation, since it was within defendant's discretion whether to publicize its findings; in any event, type of reputational harm alleged did not, in that specific administrative context, qualify as irreparable injury.

 

556 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Patricia Ann Cottage Pub, Inc. v. Mermelstein


2005-02063, (Index No. 5806/04)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


36 A.D.3d 816; 830 N.Y.S.2d 184; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 750; 2007 NY Slip Op 536



January 23, 2007, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pubs commenced an action to review and annul the determinations and penalties of the Commissioner of the County of Suffolk Department of Health Services that the pubs violated Public Health Law § 1399-o and for a declaration that § 1399-o was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner received complaints that the pubs were permitting smoking in their establishments. An inspector visited the pubs, for less than 30 minutes, observed patrons smoking but did not see the bartenders take any action to prevent or stop the individuals from smoking. Each owner testified that staff members were directed to inform patrons of the law prohibiting smoking and to request that they extinguish their cigarettes. In two of the pubs, several "No Smoking" signs were prominently displayed, as required by Public Health Law § 1399-p. In the third pub, there was conflicting testimony about whether the required "No Smoking" signs were displayed. The appellate court concluded, based on the record before it, that there was not substantial evidence to support the Commissioner's determination as to the two pubs with the necessary signs displayed. Among other things, the appellate court noted that Public Health Law § 1399-o did not inform the proprietors of what affirmative steps needed to be taken to insure that smoking was not permitted. The record was devoid of evidence the bartenders failed to act in a manner consistent with the instructions of the Commissioner.


OUTCOME: The Commisoner's determinations with respect to two pubs were annulled. The Commissioner's determination with respect to the third pub was modified so as to find that pub guilty of violating Public Health Law § 1399-p(1).


HEADNOTES

Health--No Smoking Regulations.--Determinations that two of establishments at issue permitted smoking in violation of Public Health Law §1399-o were not supported by substantial evidence--investigator saw patrons smoking during very brief period of time and did not see bartender take any affirmative steps to cure patrons' violation of statute--Public Health Law §1399-o does not inform proprietor of what affirmative steps must be taken to insure that smoking is not permitted, both establishments displayed several "No Smoking" signs as required by Public Health Law §1399-p, both establishments had removed all ashtrays from their premises, both establishments submitted uncontradicted testimony that patrons who smoked were advised not to, there was no proof that investigator or anyone else at bar asked bartender to insure that smoking desist and that bartender refused to so act, and there was no proof that smoking patrons were served--record was devoid of evidence that bartenders failed to act in manner consistent with instructions of Commissioner of County Department of Health--although there was substantial evidence to support determination that third establishment violated Public Health Law §1399-o by permitting smoking on premises, portion of Commissioner's order which directed compliance with Public Health Law §1399-o was vague and not capable of enforcement since it failed to specify steps which had to be taken to make third establishment compliant.

Matter of Kelch v. Town Bd. of Town of Davenport


500895


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


36 A.D.3d 1110; 829 N.Y.S.2d 250; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 542; 2007 NY Slip Op 357



January 18, 2007, Decided 
January 18, 2007, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner new justice appealed a judgment by the Delaware County Supreme Court (New York) that dismissed his CPLR art. 78 application seeking to compel respondent town board to pay him a higher annual salary; the justice claimed that the board violated U.S. Const. art. III, § 1, NY Const. art. VI, § 25(a) in determining his salary.


OVERVIEW: The voters approved a resolution by the town board to reduce the number of town justices from two to one. After the new justice was elected, but before he took office, the board set the salaries for the two town justices by raising the incumbent's salary from $ 5,000 to $ 7,500 annually and setting the justice's salary at $ 500 annually. The appellate court found that the board violated public policy and the constitutional principals of separation of powers in setting the justice's exceedingly meager salary. Although the board could approve different salary amounts for its two justices under Town Law § 27(1), it had no legitimate reason to set the new justice's salary at such a low amount. As the board acted in a manner likely to affect or impinge upon the independence of the judiciary, its action in setting the new justice's salary at $ 500 per year violated the U.S. Const. art. III, § 1, NY Const. art. VI, § 25(a). Consequently, the trial court erred in dismissing the new justice's CPLR art. 78 application.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified by declaring that the board's actions violated state and federal constitutions, and the matter was remitted for a new determination of the new justice's annual salary; and, as so modified, the judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional Law--Separation of Powers

Judges--Judicial Salaries.--Respondent Town Board's legislative action in setting petitioner town justice's annual salary at $ 500 violated US and NY Constitutions--judicial interference in legislative action was necessary because respondent violated public policy and constitutional principals of separation of powers in setting petitioner's exceedingly meager salary--although respondent could approve different salary amounts for its two justices (see Town Law § 27 [1]), especially considering that other justice had more experience than petitioner, respondent had no legitimate reason to set petitioner's salary at such low amount--respondent acted in manner likely to affect or impinge upon independence of judiciary.

El Paso Corp. v. New York State Dept. of Taxation & Fin.


2005-04201, (Index No. 3436/04)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


36 A.D.3d 655; 828 N.Y.S.2d 209; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 465; 2007 NY Slip Op 265



January 16, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by El Paso Corp. v New York State Dep't of Taxation & Fin., 8 NY3d 813, 868 NE2d 235, 2007 NY LEXIS 1000, 836 NYS2d 552 (N.Y., May 8, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, property owners, sought a declaration that defendant, the New York State Department of Taxation and Finance, improperly assessed a real estate transfer tax pursuant to Tax Law § 1400 et seq. on certain transfers of property. The Supreme Court, Westchester County, New York, granted the Department's motion to dismiss the first two counts of the complaint while denying the owners' cross-motion for summary judgment. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners came into ownership of two natural gas pipelines, together with the easements in which the pipelines were located. The Department determined that the acquisition of the easements was subject to the real estate transfer tax. Because, in their first cause of action, the owners claimed that the easements did not constitute an interest in real property within the meaning of the Tax Law, the declaratory judgment action for a determination of that claim was proper. Thus, the supreme court should not have dismissed the owners' first cause of action, but should have determined the owner's cross motion for summary judgment on the merits. The cross-motion should have been denied on the merits, however, because the easements provided the owners with the right to use the property for the purpose of constructing a pipeline, and thus constituted an interest in real property for purposes of the real estate transfer tax. The owners' second cause of action involved the proper application of the real estate transfer tax statute to persons and property within the Department's jurisdiction, and thus was properly dismissed due to the owners' failure to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The order was modified to deny the motion to dismiss the owners' first cause of action, and the Department was granted summary judgment on that cause of action. Otherwise, the order was affirmed, and the matter was remitted to the supreme court for the entry of judgment declaring that the easements constituted interests in real property subject to the Department's jurisdiction for purposes of assessment of the real estate transfer tax.


HEADNOTES

Declaratory Judgments--When Remedy Appropriate

Taxation--Real Property Transfer Gains Tax.--Plaintiffs came into ownership of two natural gas pipelines within State, together with easements in which those pipelines were located, and subject easements constituted interests in real property subject to jurisdiction of New York State Department of Taxation and Finance for purposes of assessment of New York real estate transfer tax.

People v. Campbell


15730


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


36 A.D.3d 1016; 827 N.Y.S.2d 768; 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 233; 2007 NY Slip Op 172



January 11, 2007, Decided 
January 11, 2007, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered by the County Court of Chemung County (New York), which convicted defendant, upon his plea of guilty, of the crime of aggravated unlicensed operation of a motor vehicle in the first degree in violation of Vehicle and Traffic Law § 511(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that § 511(3) was unconstitutionally vague because it did not inform a person that an indefinite continuation of a license suspension was contemplated until one took action to lift it by paying the appropriate fee under Vehicle and Traffic Law § 503(2)(j). On appeal, the court disagreed and affirmed defendant's conviction. The court determined that Vehicle and Traffic Law § 511(3) required that the prosecution establish that defendant knew or had reason to know that his license was suspended as a result of a prior conviction under Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1192. At his plea allocution, defendant admitted that his license had previously been suspended for a conviction for driving while intoxicated, and he did not dispute that he failed to pay the termination of suspension fee required by Vehicle and Traffic Law § 503(2)(j). Based on a reading of § 503(2)(j) and Vehicle and Traffic Law § 511(3) together, the court held that defendant was on notice that a license suspension continued in effect until his arrest due to his failure to pay the termination of suspension fee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional Law--Validity of Statute.--Defendant's conviction of aggravated unlicensed operation of motor vehicle was affirmed; when read together, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 503 (2) (j) and § 511 (3) put defendant on notice that aggravated unlicensed operation of motor vehicle encompassed suspension that continued in effect due to his failure to pay termination of suspension fee required by section 503 (2) (j).

Mayor of the City of New York v. Council of the City of New York


7099, Index 404987/01


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


38 A.D.3d 89; 825 N.Y.S.2d 201; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14400; 2006 NY Slip Op 9059



December 5, 2006, Decided 
December 5, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion granted by Mayor of N.Y. v. Council of N.Y., 8 NY3d 894, 865 NE2d 5, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 304, 832 NYS2d 896 (2007)
Motion granted by Mayor of City of N.Y. v. Council of City of N.Y., 8 NY3d 914, 865 NE2d 1250, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 560, 834 NYS2d 84 (2007)
Motion granted by Mayor of City of N.Y. v. Council of City of N.Y., 8 NY3d 915, 865 NE2d 1251, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 566, 834 NYS2d 84 (2007)
Motion granted by Mayor of City of N.Y. v. Council of City of N.Y., 8 NY3d 914, 865 NE2d 1250, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 568, 834 NYS2d 84 (2007)
Motion granted by Mayor of City of N.Y. v. Council of City of N.Y., 8 NY3d 914, 865 NE2d 1250, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 570, 834 NYS2d 83 (2007)
Affirmed by Mayor of the City of New York v. Council of the City of New York, 9 NY3d 23, 874 NE2d 706, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 1564, 842 NYS2d 742 (N.Y., June 12, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Mayor of the City of New York, sued appellee, the Council of the City of New York, in the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), for a declaratory judgment that New York City, N.Y., Loc. Laws No. 18 and 19 (2001) were unlawful. The trial court granted summary judgment to the Council. The Mayor appealed.


OVERVIEW: New York City, N.Y., Loc. Laws No. 18 and 19, by amending Administrative Code of the City of NY § 12-307(a)(4), required that the Mayor negotiate with the unions representing fire alarm dispatchers and their supervisors, as well as emergency medical technicians and their supervisors, over all terms and conditions of employment. The Mayor contended that the local laws were unlawful on the ground that they violated the New York Civil Service Law, the New York Municipal Home Rule Law, and the New York City Charter. On appeal, the court found that the Council was authorized to enact the local laws because they were not prohibited by the New York Taylor Law, Civil Service Law §§ 204(2) and 212. Further, the local laws were not invalid under separation of powers principles. Furthermore, because the local laws were enacted in accordance with the authority conferred by Civil Service Law § 212, they were not subject to the referendum requirement of Municipal Home Rule Law § 23. Finally, NY City Charter § 38(5) did not make the local law subject to a mandatory referendum, because state statutes provided that the local laws were not subject to a mandatory referendum.


OUTCOME: The order and judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Home Rule Powers -- Labor Relations -- Curtailment of Scope of Mayoral Collective Bargaining Authority

1. The New York City Council validly enacted two local laws under its home rule powers (see NY Const, art IX, § 2 [c] [ii] [1]; Municipal Home Rule Law §10 [1] [ii] [a] [1]) that amended the City's Collective Bargaining Law (see Administrative Code of City of NY §12-307 [a] [4] [i]) by exempting certain nonuniformed Fire Department employees from the citywide collective bargaining agreement negotiated on behalf of all other nonuniformed municipal employees and conferring on them the same authority enjoyed by uniformed personnel to negotiate with the Mayor all terms and conditions of employment, thereby curtailing the authority the Mayor previously enjoyed to negotiate and enter into collective bargaining agreements that bound the affected Fire Department employees without the participation of their respective unions. The challenged local laws were not invalid as "inconsistent" with and "unauthorized and prohibited" by the Taylor Law. The City Council was not prohibited by the Taylor Law from exercising its constitutional and statutory authority (see Civil Service Law §206 [1]; § 212) to curtail the scope of the authority the Mayor previously enjoyed without otherwise impairing the Mayor's exclusive authority under the Taylor Law to bargain and negotiate over the terms and conditions of employment with employee organizations. The right to bargain and negotiate is not itself a term or condition of employment over which the Mayor's authority is exclusive under the Taylor Law. Furthermore, the Taylor Law does not authorize the Mayor or any local government not to negotiate with a union representing a group of municipal employees and thereby impose upon them terms and conditions of employment to which they have not acceded.

Municipal Corporations - Home Rule Powers - Local Laws Subject to Mandatory Referendum - Curtailment of Scope of Mayoral Collective Bargaining Authority

Municipal Corporations -- Home Rule Powers -- Local Laws Subject to Mandatory Referendum -- Curtailment of Scope of Mayoral Collective Bargaining Authority

2. The New York City Council validly enacted two local laws under its home rule powers (see NY Const, art IX, § 2 [c] [ii] [1]; Municipal Home Rule Law § 10 [1] [ii] [a] [1]) that amended the City's Collective Bargaining Law (see Administrative Code of City of NY § 12-307 [a] [4] [i]) by exempting certain nonuniformed Fire Department employees from the citywide collective bargaining agreement negotiated on behalf of all other nonuniformed municipal employees and conferring on them the same authority enjoyed by uniformed personnel to negotiate with the Mayor all terms and conditions of employment. The challenged local laws were not subject to a mandatory referendum ordinarily required when a local law "curtails any power of an elective officer" (see Municipal Home Rule Law § 23 [2] [f]; NY City Charter § 38 [5]). Even though the subject laws curtailed the authority the Mayor previously enjoyed under the Collective Bargaining Law to negotiate and enter into collective bargaining agreements that bound the affected Fire Department employees without the participation of their respective unions, not every local law that curtails mayoral power is subject to a mandatory referendum. A local legislative body may by local law curtail a power of an elective officer if its acts "under the authority of a state statute." Consequently, since the City Council was acting under its authority under the Taylor Law to enact substantive and procedural provisions governing labor relations that are "substantially equivalent" to the Taylor Law (see Civil Service Law § 212), a referendum was not required.

People v. Downey


9600, Ind. 4458/93


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


34 A.D.3d 342; 824 N.Y.S.2d 287; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13740; 2006 NY Slip Op 8653



November 21, 2006, Decided 
November 21, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by, Motion dismissed by People v. Downey, 8 NY3d 806, 864 NE2d 618, 2007 NY LEXIS 196, 832 NYS2d 488 (N.Y., Feb. 22, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the New York County Supreme Court (New York) that adjudicated him a level three sex offender under Correction Law § 168-a(2)(a)(I); defendant claimed that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to him, because his crime allegedly lacked any sexual aspect or motive.


OVERVIEW: After defendant approached a child he did not know, forcibly seized a four-year-old child from her mother, and kissed the child, he was convicted of first-degree unlawful imprisonment. The hearing court adjudicated him a sex offender pursuant to Correction Law § 168-a(2)(a)(I). The appellate court found that there was no other reasonable explanation for defendant's conduct other than a sexual motive. Therefore, the underlying unlawful imprisonment case clearly had a sexual aspect. In addition, defendant has two prior convictions for sex crimes. As a result, the record supported the hearing court's finding that defendant should be designated a level three sex offender. Consequently, § 168-a(2)(a)(I) was constitutional as applied to defendant. The various mitigating factors argued by defendant were outweighed by the danger of future recidivism, and did not warrant a downward departure from the presumptive risk level.


OUTCOME: The order was unanimously affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Sex Offenders--Sex Offender Registration Act.--Defendant's adjudication as sex offender based on his conviction of unlawful imprisonment was affirmed; defendant approached child he did not know, forcibly seized child from her mother, and kissed child, with no other reasonable explanation for his conduct other than sexual motive.

 

562 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Cobos v. Dennison


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


34 A.D.3d 1325; 825 N.Y.S.2d 332; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16045; 2006 NY Slip Op 8529



November 17, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected January 17, 2007.
Appeal dismissed by Cobos v. Dennison, 8 NY3d 851, 862 NE2d 786, 2007 NY LEXIS 221, 830 NYS2d 695 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cobos v. Dennison, 128 S Ct 94, 169 L Ed 2d 69, 2007 US LEXIS 9565 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


HEADNOTES

Parole--Board of Parole.--Contention that standards for parole release determinations under Executive Law §259-i were unconstitutional because they did not differentiate between adult offenders and offenders who committed crimes when they were less than 18 years of age, was rejected; statutory framework regarding discretionary parole decisions allows Parole Board to consider "any mitigating and aggravating factors" associated with offense and thus allows Parole Board to consider offender's juvenile status when making parole release determinations.

 

563 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Riddick


15296


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


34 A.D.3d 923; 823 N.Y.S.2d 594; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13198; 2006 NY Slip Op 7999



November 9, 2006, Decided 
November 9, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v. Riddick, 9 N.Y.3d 868, 872 N.E.2d 1204, 2007 N.Y. LEXIS 2513, 840 N.Y.S.2d 898 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Riddick, 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6645 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, Jan. 4, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the County Court of Broome County (New York) that convicted him of second-degree murder under Penal Law § 125.25(2); defendant claimed that the evidence was legally insufficient to support the conviction and that the depraved indifference murder statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: After defendant and his companion were involved in an altercation during a pool game, the companion struck at least one bar patron an aluminum bat, smashed the front picture window of the bar, and left. Defendant and his companion then obtained a shotgun from the companion's residence and returned to the bar where defendant fired a single shotgun blast through the open front door into a crowd of approximately 30 bar patrons, killing a patron seated at the bar. The appellate court found that defendant failed to preserve his argument regarding legal insufficiency of the evidence. In any event, defendant's written confession and the evidence introduced at trial provided the jury an adequate basis upon which to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was, in fact, the individual who discharged the shotgun into the bar. That action constituted the type of morally reprehensible conduct without regard to human life that established the requisite depravity under § 125.25(2). The statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it clearly apprised defendant of the forbidden conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes - Appeal--Preservation of Issue for Review.--Defendant's argument regarding legal insufficiency of evidence was not preserved for review; although defendant moved for trial order of dismissal, his challenge to sufficiency of evidence, based only on contention that testimony of accomplice was not believable, did not preserve challenge on appeal to adequacy of corroborative evidence to accomplice testimony.

Crimes--Murder--Sufficiency of Evidence.--Although issue was unpreserved for review, trial testimony of bar patron, trial testimony and written statement of accomplice, written confession of defendant and physical evidence introduced provided jury adequate basis upon which to conclude beyond reasonable doubt that defendant was individual who discharged shotgun into bar, thereby causing death to another.

Crimes--Murder--Depraved Indifference Murder.--Defendant's challenge to constitutionality of depraved indifference murder statute (see Penal Law § 125.25 [2]) was unpreserved and without merit--critical statutory language that separates second-degree manslaughter from depraved indifference murder is defendant's underlying depraved indifference, which is more heinous and despicable than reckless conduct which creates risk of death--jury could properly reject lesser included charge of manslaughter and conclude that defendant's discharge of shotgun into bar he knew was populated by 30 people constituted type of morally reprehensible conduct without regard to human life which established requisite depravity.

 

564 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cassano


9479


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


34 A.D.3d 239; 823 N.Y.S.2d 395; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13225; 2006 NY Slip Op 8039



November 9, 2006, Decided 
November 9, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by, Motion dismissed by People v Cassano, 8 NY3d 804, 862 NE2d 792, 2007 NY LEXIS 253, 830 NYS2d 700 (N.Y., Feb. 13, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), adjudicating defendant a level three sex offender pursuant to the New York Sex Offender Registration Act, Correction Law art. 6-C.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted kidnapping in the second degree and was adjudicated a sex offender under Correction Law § 168-a(2)(a)(I), which included within the category of sex offenses certain abduction related crimes committed against children by persons other than their parents. Defendant claimed that this was unconstitutional because there was no evidence that his crime had a sexual aspect or motive. Pursuant to CPLR 4017, 5501(a)(3), defendant improperly raised this claim for the first time on appeal. The appellate court declined to reach the claim. The appellate court also found that, had it reached the claim, it would have failed. Defendant had a prior felony conviction involving sex crimes against two children, he had a diagnosed personality disorder, and his attempted kidnapping of a child was committed under circumstances that did not negate a possible sexual motive.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Sex Offenders--Sex Offender Registration Act.--Although defendant's claim that he should not have been adjudicated sex offender based on attempted kidnapping conviction was improperly raised for first time on appeal, statute was constitutional as applied to him; defendant had prior felony conviction involving sex crimes against children and diagnosed personality disorder, and circumstances underlying attempted kidnapping did not negate possible sexual motive.

 

565 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Nash v. New York State Dept. of Labor


98585


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


34 A.D.3d 905; 824 N.Y.S.2d 438; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13011; 2006 NY Slip Op 7951



November 2, 2006, Decided 
November 2, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by Nash v. N.Y. State Dep't of Labor, 8 NY3d 803, 862 NE2d 792, 2007 NY LEXIS 247, 830 NYS2d 700 (N.Y., Feb. 13, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a self-employed electrician and business owner proceeding pro se, petitioned for review of a decision of respondent, the Commissioner of the New York State Department of Labor, pursuant to Labor Law §§ 220 and 220-b, which found that he willfully failed to pay prevailing wages and supplements.


OVERVIEW: The business owner entered into contracts to perform electrical work for two municipalities, and hired two men to assist him. He paid them $15.70 per hour with no additional benefits. The Department found that the business owner violated the prevailing wage rate laws by not paying his employees journeyman electrician wages of $25 per hour plus supplemental benefits and that the underpayment was willful. The court concluded that the classification of the employees as journeymen electricians was supported by substantial evidence because they performed the same work designated for journeyman electricians under a collective bargaining agreement between the Albany Electrical Contractors Association and the local union of the International Brotherhood of Electrical Workers. Substantial evidence also supported the finding of willfulness. While the projects constituted the first time the business owner hired others on a public works project, he had previously worked on such projects and knew that the wage rates were higher. He also discussed the federal prevailing wage statutes with one employee and stated that he would not pay prevailing wages because no person deserved such a salary.


OUTCOME: The Department's determination was confirmed, without costs, and the petition was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Labor--Prevailing Rate of Wages--Trade Classification.--Respondent properly classified petitioner's employees as journeyman electricians; since employees were not registered under bona fide apprentice program, respondent was required to determine appropriate wage rate "for the classification of work [they] actually performed" (Labor Law § 220 [3-e]); although petitioner testified that his employees had no prior training in electrical work, they performed same work designated for journeyman electrician under collective bargaining agreement between local contractors association and local union of electrical workers.

Labor--Prevailing Rate of Wages.--Respondent's finding that petitioner willfully violated Labor Law § 220 was supported by substantial evidence that petitioner knew or should have known that he was violating law; while subject projects constituted first time that petitioner hired others on public works project, he worked as electrician for 30 years, previously performed labor on public works projects and knew that wage rates were higher on public works projects.

 

566 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Litto


2005-02978, (Ind. No. 404/04)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


33 A.D.3d 625; 822 N.Y.S.2d 130; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12006; 2006 NY Slip Op 7180



October 3, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal granted by People v Litto, 7 NY3d 926, 860 NE2d 997, 2006 NY LEXIS 4030, 827 NYS2d 695 (2006)
Affirmed by People v Litto, 8 NY3d 692, 872 NE2d 848, 2007 NY LEXIS 1613, 840 NYS2d 736 (N.Y., June 27, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed an order by the Kings County Supreme Court (New York) that, inter alia, granted defendant's motion to dismiss the counts of the indictment charging him with second-degree vehicular manslaughter and driving while intoxicated under Penal Law § 125.12 and Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1192(3), respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving a car with three passengers when he allegedly inhaled a portion of the contents of a spray can of "Dust-Off," veered into oncoming traffic, and collided with an oncoming car. The appellate court found that Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1192(3) only related to intoxication by alcohol. It did not relate to intoxication by a drug, which was found in § 1192(4). Therefore, because the charges against defendant under § 1192(3) and Penal Law § 125.12 were alcohol-related, the trial court properly dismissed them.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Motor Vehicles--Operating Vehicle while Under Influence of Alcohol or Drugs.--Charges of driving while intoxicated pursuant to Vehicle and Traffic Law §1192 (3) and vehicular manslaughter in second degree pursuant to Penal Law §125.12 were dismissed against defendant, who was driving car with three passengers when he allegedly inhaled portion of contents of spray can of "Dust-Off," veered into oncoming traffic, and collided with oncoming car; Vehicle and Traffic Law §1192 (3) was intended to apply only to intoxication caused by alcohol.

 

567 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smith


1126 KA 04-01650


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


32 A.D.3d 1318; 821 N.Y.S.2d 723; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11701; 2006 NY Slip Op 7011



September 29, 2006, Decided 
September 29, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v. Smith, 7 N.Y.3d 929, 860 N.E.2d 1000, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 4169, 827 N.Y.S.2d 698 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of conviction entered by the Oneida County Court (New York), upon a jury verdict, of attempted murder in the first degree, in violation of Penal Law §§ 110.00, 125.27(1)(a)(i),(b), assault in the second degree, criminal possession of a weapon in the second degree, criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree, and false personation.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's contention that the evidence was legally insufficient to support the conviction of attempted murder in the first degree. The People presented evidence that defendant had the specific intent to commit murder and engaged in conduct to carry out that intent. There was evidence that showed that defendant pointed a loaded revolver at close range at the chest of a police officer who was pursuing him, but during a struggle the officer grabbed the revolver and prevented defendant from firing it. Defendant failed to preserve for the court's review his contention that a jury charge related to the weapons possession charge was misleading or confusing. Defendant also failed to preserve for review his contention that the People failed to establish his knowledge that the revolver was defaced as required for the conviction of criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree under Penal Law § 265.02(3). There was no dispute that defendant possessed the defaced revolver on his person and that its condition was visible as he pointed it to police in a shooter's stance. The court found that the sentence was not unduly harsh or severe.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Murder--Attempt.--Evidence that defendant pointed loaded revolver at police officer and engaged in conduct consistent with shooting that revolver was legally sufficient to support conviction of attempted murder in first degree.

Crimes--Instructions--Possession of Weapon.--Contention that jury charge with respect to criminal possession of weapon in second degree was misleading and should have specified that "defendant was not required to present any evidence in order for the jury to reject the inference" of intent to use weapon unlawfully was unpreserved for review and without merit; Penal Law § 265.15 (4) specifies that possession by any person of any weapon is presumptive evidence of intent to use same unlawfully against another; charge sufficiently conveyed to jury that it had choice as to whether to apply statutory presumption.

Crimes--Possession of Weapon.--Although issue was unpreserved for review, People presented legally sufficient evidence that defendant knew that revolver in his possession was defaced and thus conviction of criminal possession of weapon in third degree under Penal Law § 265.02 (3) was proper--defendant possessed defaced revolver on his person and its condition was visible as he pointed it at police officer in shooter's stance; photographs of defaced revolver were admitted in evidence, and thus jury was able to evaluate whether it was possible to possess revolver without knowledge that its identifying features were illegible.

 

568 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Chantel Nicole R. (Pamela R.)


8513


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


34 A.D.3d 99; 821 N.Y.S.2d 194; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10922; 2006 NY Slip Op 6628



September 21, 2006, Decided 
September 21, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal dismissed by In re Chantel Nicole R., 8 NY3d 840, 862 NE2d 784, 2007 NY LEXIS 107, 830 NYS2d 692 (N.Y., Jan. 16, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mental hygiene legal service, on behalf of an adult mentally retarded daughter, objected to the appointment by the Surrogate's Court, New York County (New York), of petitioner mother as guardian of the person of the daughter under the New York Surrogate's Court Procedure Act (NYSCPA), specifically SCPA 1750, to the extent that the guardianship extended to decisions concerning life-sustaining treatment.


OVERVIEW: The daughter argued that she objected to granting her mother the power to terminate life-sustaining medical care. The appellate court held that treating the daughter differently from a competent person did not violate the Equal Protection Clause as the State had a legitimate interest in advancing the right of mentally retarded persons to be free from prolonged suffering. There was no opportunity to show that a mentally retarded person would have elected to terminate life-sustaining measures under circumstances providing no hope for recover. The NYSCPA did not offend equal protection by failing to redress the plight of all similarly situated persons who were never competent to make an informed decision. The daughter's claim that the failure of the NYSCPA to require a hearing violated her due process rights did not provide a basis for appellate review as the daughter received a hearing before the appointment of a guardian. Finally, no opinion was offered on whether the extraordinary burden standard for the withholding or withdrawal of life support was unconstitutionally vague as the daughter might never be the subject of any procedure, determination, or action under SCPA 1750-b.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court, which appointed the mother the guardian of the daughter's person with authority to make decisions concerning life-sustaining treatment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Incapacitated and Mentally Disabled Persons -- Guardian for Mentally Retarded and Developmentally Disabled Persons -- Health Care Decisions for Mentally Retarded Persons 

Petitioner, the mother of a "moderately retarded" 26-year-old daughter not currently suffering from any condition requiring medical treatment, was properly appointed, following a hearing, as guardian of her daughter's person with authority to make decisions concerning life-sustaining treatment pursuant to SCPA 1750. The statutory scheme authorizing the appointment of guardians to make health care decisions for mentally retarded persons is not violative of equal protection for treating mentally retarded persons differently from persons who were once competent. The disparate treatment of mentally retarded persons and once-competent persons with regard to the procedures for terminating life-sustaining treatment is rationally related to a legitimate government interest in advancing the right of mentally retarded persons to be free from prolonged suffering. The Equal Protection Clause only prohibits the government from treating persons differently from others who are similarly situated, and mentally retarded persons are not similarly situated to those who were once competent. Furthermore, respondent could not challenge the constitutionality of the statute on due process grounds because the statute does not require a hearing where, as here, both parents consented to the appointment of a guardian (see SCPA 1754). Since respondent sought and received a hearing, she was not aggrieved by the order of Surrogate's Court (see CPLR 5511). In addition, since respondent might never require life-sustaining measures, her challenge to the statute as being unconstitutionally vague under the "extraordinary burden" criterion (SCPA 1750-b [4] [b] [ii]) did not present a justiciable controversy.

 

569 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Stark v. Kelleher


501016


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


32 A.D.3d 663; 820 N.Y.S.2d 193; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10033; 2006 NY Slip Op 6267



August 17, 2006, Decided 
August 17, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by Stark v. Kelleher, 7 NY3d 707, 854 NE2d 1276, 821 NYS2d 812, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2105 (N.Y., Aug. 23, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate challenged a judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), that dismissed his application to declare valid a designating petition naming him as a party's candidate for the office of New York State Senator in a primary election. Respondents, Commissioners of the New York State Board of Elections, invalidated the petition for signature deficiencies under N.Y. Elec. Law § 6-130 on respondent individual's objection.


OVERVIEW: The Board found that 259 of the 1,175 signatures on the candidate's petition were deficient, leaving the candidate with fewer than the 1,000 required signatures. In the candidate's proceeding under N.Y. Elec. Law § 16-102, the trial court found that the failure of signers to correctly list their town or city was a fatal defect requiring dismissal. The appellate court affirmed the judgment. The requirement for setting forth the town or city served legitimate purposes of facilitating the discovery of fraud and allowing rapid, efficient verification of signatures. Failure to include the town or city with a signature resulted in the signature's invalidation. The establishment of a statewide voter database under the Help America Vote Act of 2002 (Act), 42 U.S.C.S. § 15483, did not change the result because states had discretion to determine the manner of compliance with the Act. Any finding that the information required by N.Y. Elec. Law § 6-130 was no longer necessary was to be made by the legislature and not by the courts. The town and city requirement did not restrict access to the ballot or place unconstitutional burdens on the candidate's 1st or 14th Amendment rights to associate.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court judgment.


HEADNOTES

Elections--Designating Petitions.--Signers' failure to correctly list their town or city on designating petition was fatal defect requiring dismissal of petition to declare designating petition valid--Election Law § 6-130 provides that "sheets of a designating petition must set forth in every instance the name of the signer, his or her residence address, town or city (except in the city of New York, the county), and the date when the signature is affixed"--compliance with this statute is substantive requirement and failure of signers of petition to accurately set forth their town or city will result in invalidation of such signatures.

People v. Knox


15921


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT

Law § 440.20 to set aside the sentence following defendant's conviction for two counts of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the third degree.

Defendant subsequently appealed from the lower court's denial of his motion under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.20 to vacate his sentence.
