Law was unconstitutional when it was applied to him for a 1993 sentence was not properly before the court on appeal because it had been raised for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Sentence--Persistent Felony Offender

 

571 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Gilmartin v. Tax Appeals Trib.


96849


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


31 A.D.3d 1008; 818 N.Y.S.2d 682; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9455; 2006 NY Slip Op 5860



July 20, 2006, Decided 
July 20, 2006, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an action against respondent, the New York Tax Appeals Tribunal, to obtain review of a determination of the Tribunal, which, inter alia, sustained an assessment of personal income tax imposed against petitioner for the two tax years at issue.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner admitted that he worked and was compensated for the two tax years at issue, but that he did not file New York State income tax returns. Petitioner contended that the Internal Revenue Code did not define "income" making it impossible for petitioner to determine his liabilities. The Audit Division of the New York Department of Taxation and Finance issued two notices of deficiency. The validity of both deficiency notices was sustained during a 2002 conciliation conference and again at a tax appeals hearing. The administration law judge (ALJ) also imposed a frivolous position penalty against petitioner. The Tribunal upheld the decisions of the ALJ. The court rejected petitioner's assertion that the Tribunal and the ALJ could not rely upon documentation from the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) because under N.Y. A.P.A. § 306 the state agencies were not required to comply with technical rules of evidence. The IRS documents were both relevant and material to establish the deficiencies. There was no merit to petitioner's argument that the Division failed to produce sufficient evidence of petitioner's income.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the deficiency determination.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Taxation--Personal Income Tax.--Determination which sustained assessment of personal income tax was confirmed--Internal Revenue Service documents were relevant and material to establish petitioner's deficiencies, and were properly considered by administrative law judge--constitutional right of confrontation was not applicable--argument that individuals acting on behalf of state were without authority to act because they had not filed oath of office as required by Public Officers Law was without merit; even if Public Officers Law was applicable, acts performed by public officer who has not taken and filed official oath are as valid and effective as if oath had been taken and filed--sufficient evidence of petitioner's income was produced; petitioner failed to support his claim that his business expenses and contributions reduced his taxable income, failed to prove that methods used to arrive at assessment were erroneous, and failed to rebut presumption of correctness which attached to notice of deficiency--Congress has constitutional authority to impose income tax, and argument that term "income," as used in Internal Revenue Code, is unconstitutionally vague and indefinite, was without merit.

 

572 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Avella v. Batt


98847


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


33 A.D.3d 77; 820 N.Y.S.2d 332; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9459; 2006 NY Slip Op 5867



July 20, 2006, Decided 
July 20, 2006, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the treasurer of a political party, sought review of a decision of the Supreme Court, Albany County, (New York), which partially granted the application of petitioners, registered voters, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. Elec. Law § 16-114 to compel respondents to comply with reporting requirements under New York election laws.


OVERVIEW: The voters obtained a ruling that the political party violated N.Y. Elec. Law § 2-126 by spending party funds to aid the campaign of a candidate involved in the Democratic primary election for county district attorney. The lower court concluded that the political party violated § 2-126 by spending money to promote a Democratic candidate, and the lower court rejected the party's argument that § 2-126 violated the First Amendment. The court determined initially that the voters had standing to bring the claim because they were five qualified voters as set forth in N.Y. Elec. Law § 16-114(3) and that the matter was justiciable. The court found that the party's decision to provide financial support to the Democratic candidate violated § 2-126. However, under the circumstances, the court found that § 2-126 violated the First Amendment rights of political expression and association. The statute on its face prohibited all expenditures in aid of candidates for a primary election, and as such, the statute prohibited core First Amendment activity. The court rejected the argument that a compelling state interest to protect against corruption did not justify a complete prohibition on spending.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision to the extent that it granted partial judgment in favor of the registered voters.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- Primary Elections -- Challenge to Expenditure of Party Funds -- Standing

1. Petitioner voters had standing to commence a proceeding seeking an order declaring that respondent political party violated Election Law § 2-126 by spending party funds to aid the campaign of a particular candidate in another party's primary election for District Attorney in petitioners' county. Election Law § 16-114 (3) states that "any five qualified voters" may commence a proceeding in Supreme Court to "compel by order any person who has failed to comply ... with any of the provisions of this chapter." Therefore, petitioners, as five voters registered to vote in the political subdivision conducting the election at issue, had standing.

Appeal -- Academic and Moot Questions -- Election Law Challenge to Expenditure of Party Funds

2. Although the proceeding brought by petitioners, five registered voters, seeking an order declaring that respondent political party violated Election Law §2-126 by spending party funds to aid the campaign of a particular candidate in another party's primary election for District Attorney in petitioners' county was initiated after the primary election had concluded, thereby rendering the proceeding moot because Supreme Court could no longer compel compliance with Election Law §2-126, the exception to the mootness doctrine was applicable. The issue raised was important and novel, likely to recur and, most notably, will typically evade judicial review in light of the fact that the challenged expenditures are often made immediately before the primary election, as they were here, and may not be disclosed in campaign finance records until after the primary election has concluded.

Elections -- Primary Elections -- Challenge to Expenditure of Party Funds

3. Respondent political party violated Election Law § 2-126 by spending party funds to aid the campaign of a particular candidate in another party's primary election for a county District Attorney. Election Law § 2-126 prevents the expenditure of party funds "in aid of the designation or nomination of any person to be voted for at a primary election." The statute is not directed solely at intraparty spending by party leadership on its own endorsed candidate; it also prohibits a party's use of its funds to support a candidate in a primary election of another political party, as was done here. The vast majority of the funds spent by respondent were spent prior to the primary election. Although respondent maintained that its expenditures related to only the general election, the mailings sent out by respondent prior to the primary election specifically referenced the other party's primary election instead of the general election and compared the candidate it supported only to the other party's nominee, without mentioning any other candidates running in the general election.

Elections - Primary Elections -- Challenge to Expenditure of Party Funds -- Constitutionality of Election Law § 2-126

4. Although respondent political party violated Election Law § 2-126 by spending party funds to aid the campaign of a particular candidate in another party's primary election for a county District Attorney, Election Law § 2-126, as applied here, unconstitutionally burdened respondent's First Amendment rights of political expression and association. Since the time that the statute was enacted, the case law of the United States Supreme Court regarding the First Amendment implications of legislation regulating expenditures in connection with elections has evolved significantly, and expenditures by political parties in elections are now understood to constitute "core" First Amendment activities entitled to substantial protection. By prohibiting all expenditures by political parties in aid of candidates to be voted for at a primary election, Election Law § 2-126 prohibits "core" First Amendment activity. Regulations that impact a political party's capacity to communicate with the public will not survive constitutional scrutiny unless they are narrowly tailored to serve a compelling state interest. Here, the state's interest in avoiding corruption and the appearance thereof in electoral politics was not a sufficiently compelling interest, standing alone, to support expenditure limits. Nor did the unsupported assertions that permitting a political party to spend money in communicating with the public regarding candidates running in primary elections will lead to interparty manipulation and the control of the primary process by party machines constitute a sufficiently compelling state interest.

 

573 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lisle-Cannon


2004-08081, (Ind No. 8640/98)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


31 A.D.3d 467; 820 N.Y.S.2d 280; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8874; 2006 NY Slip Op 5390



July 5, 2006, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), denying his motion under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.20(1) to be relieved of his duty to register as a sex offender pursuant to N.Y. Correct. Law art. 6-C.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to the charge of attempted kidnapping in the second degree. Despite the fact that defendant's criminal conduct was entirely devoid of any sexual component, he was certified as a sex offender under N.Y. Correct. Law §§ 168-a(1), (2)(a)(i), 168-d(1)(a). The trial court assigned defendant to risk level one, and defendant did not appeal from that determination. Defendant subsequently moved in the trial court, pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.20(1), to be relieved of his duty to register annually as a sex offender. The trial court properly found that defendant's request for relief was not properly before it. While defendant's certification as a sex offender was part of the judgment of conviction under N.Y. Correct. Law § 168-d(1)(a), it was not part of the sentence. Thus, the relief sought by defendant was not available to him under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.20(1), which only authorized a motion to set aside a sentence. Nothing prevented defendant from seeking relief under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.10.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes--Sex Offenders--Sex Offender Registration Act.--Order which denied defendant's motion pursuant to CPL 440.20 (1) to be relieved of his duty to register as sex offender pursuant to Correction Law article 6-C was affirmed--while defendant's certification as sex offender under Sex Offender Registration Act was part of judgment of conviction, it was not part of sentence, and relief sought by defendant was not available to him under CPL 440.20 (1), which only authorizes motion to set aside sentence.

 

574 of 1817 DOCUMENTS



Matter of C/S 12th Ave. LLC v. City of New York


7926-7927 [M-6216]- 7928 [M-6217]- 7929 [M-6228]- 7930 [M-6230]


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


32 A.D.3d 1; 815 N.Y.S.2d 516; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6897; 2006 NY Slip Op 4172



May 25, 2006, Decided 
May 25, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Matter of City of New York, 21 Misc. 3d 1132A, 875 N.Y.S.2d 819, 2008 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 6680 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated proceedings under N.Y. Em. Dom. Proc. Law § 207, petitioner property owners challenged the determination and findings of respondents, the City of New York and the Metropolitan Transportation Authority, which approved the acquisition of certain real property and easements and approved related zoning for a redevelopment project.


OVERVIEW: Respondents approved a redevelopment project and accepted a Final Generic Environmental Impact Statement (FGEIS). The city issued a findings statement implementing a rezoning plan and allowing for acquisition of certain property. Respondents conducted a hearing to consider the proposed acquisition and issued their determination and findings. The owners, whose properties were subject to condemnation, filed petitions challenging the determination and findings. The court held that respondents satisfied their obligations under the New York State Environmental Quality Review Act (SEQRA), N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law art. 8, by taking a hard look at the anticipated areas of environmental concern and making a reasoned elaboration of the basis for their determination because the lead agencies held scoping sessions, accepted the FGEIS and reviewed community and expert input before reaching their findings. The court also held that the rezoning plan was not an unconstitutional reverse spot zoning because the rezoning for creation of a mid-block boulevard and park was part of a well-considered and comprehensive plan calculated to serve the general welfare of the community.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitions, confirmed respondents' determinations and dismissed the proceedings.



HEADNOTES

Environmental Conservation -- Environmental Quality Review -- Condemnation of Property in Furtherance of Large-Scale Redevelopment Project in Midtown Manhattan

1. Respondents' determination and findings approving the acquisition by condemnation of petitioners' real property and/or easements thereto in furtherance of a proposed subway extension/rezoning and redevelopment project in Midtown Manhattan were confirmed in consolidated proceedings pursuant to EDPL 207 as being in compliance with the substantive requirements of the State Environmental Quality Review Act (SEQRA). Respondents satisfied their obligations under SEQRA by taking a "hard look" at the anticipated areas of environmental concern of the proposed project and making a "reasoned elaboration" of the basis for their determination. During the extensive review process, the lead agencies held scoping sessions, accepted both the draft and final generic environmental impact statements and reviewed input from the community and experts. The elimination of a proposed multiuse stadium and convention center expansion from the project did not render respondents' reliance on the final environmental impact statement improper.

Eminent Domain -- Acquisition of Easement -- Notice -- Subway Tunnel Construction

2. Respondents' determination and findings approving the acquisition by condemnation of a temporary easement on petitioner's real property in furtherance of a proposed subway extension/rezoning and redevelopment project in Midtown Manhattan complied with EDPL 204 insofar as respondents' adequately apprised petitioner of the nature, timing and extent of the easement. The statute only requires that the approximate location and the reasons for the location selection for the proposed project be set forth. Given the complexity of the subway tunnel construction process and the nature of the subsurface easements, the respondents' determination and findings provided reasonable specificity as to the extent and duration of the easements.

Eminent Domain -- Inverse Condemnation -- Illegal Regulatory Taking Claim

3. Respondents' determination and findings approving the acquisition by condemnation of petitioners' real property and/or easements thereto in furtherance of a proposed subway extension/rezoning and redevelopment project in Midtown Manhattan could not be challenged as constituting an illegal regulatory taking in consolidated proceedings pursuant to EDPL 207. Since there was an adequate mechanism to seek compensation, including an inverse condemnation claim, petitioners' recourse was limited to a plenary action, where they would be required to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the land regulation destroyed the economic value of their properties.

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning -- "Reverse Spot Zoning"

4. Respondents' determination and findings approving the acquisition by condemnation of petitioners' real property and/or easements thereto in furtherance of a proposed subway extension/rezoning and redevelopment project in Midtown Manhattan could not be set aside on equal protection grounds as constituting "reverse spot zoning." The rezoning for the creation of a midblock boulevard and park was part of a well-considered and comprehensive plan calculated to serve the general welfare of the community.

Eminent Domain -- Public Use -- Condemnation of Property in Furtherance of Large-Scale Redevelopment Project in Midtown Manhattan

5. Respondents' determination and findings approving the acquisition by condemnation of petitioners' real property and/or easements thereto in furtherance of a proposed subway extension/rezoning and redevelopment project in Midtown Manhattan were confirmed as being rationally related to a public purpose. In New York, the term "public use" broadly encompasses any use, including urban renewal, which contributes to the health, safety and general welfare of the public. Judicial review is limited to ascertaining whether the proposed project is rationally related to a conceivable public purpose. Moreover, the fact that a private party might benefit from the condemnation of property to be used for a public purpose is an insufficient basis to reject a condemnation.

Sandoval v. Martinez


2005-06995, (Index No. 16050/04)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT

577 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


State of N.Y. ex rel. Harkavy v. Consilvio


7675, Index 403590/05


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


29 A.D.3d 221; 812 N.Y.S.2d 496; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3874; 2006 NY Slip Op 2451



March 30, 2006, Decided 
March 30, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion granted by State ex rel. Harkavy v. Consilvio, 7 NY3d 782, 853 NE2d 1110, 820 NYS2d 542, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2071 (2006)
Reversed by, Remitted by State of New York v. Consilvio, 7 NY3d 607, 859 NE2d 508, 825 NYS2d 702, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 3580 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner felony sex offenders filed a habeas petition seeking their release from inpatient psychiatric facilities operated by respondent executive directors. The parties filed cross-appeals from an order and judgment (one paper) of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which granted the petition insofar as to order the conditional release of the offenders.


OVERVIEW: The offenders argued that they should have been committed under the New York Correction Law. The appellate court held that the Correction Law was inapplicable as two offenders' applications were submitted on the date of their release and there was no possibility that the other offenders would be returned to the custody of the New York Department of Correctional Services (DOCS). Further, a few hours or days remaining in the sentence when the application was filed did not render offenders "persons serving a sentence of imprisonment." The New York Mental Hygiene Law applied as each offender was committed on the date of his release from prison. Under both the New York Mental Hygiene Law and the New York Correction Law, retention was properly sought under N.Y. Mental. Hyg. Law art. 9. DOCS had standing to make the applications. Article 9 did not deprive the offenders of their due process rights. It was error to file the habeas proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 70 as N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law § 33.15 was the more specific habeas provision. Finally, the order conditionally releasing the offenders without conducting a review as to the state of each offender's mental disability was improper.


OUTCOME: The order and judgment was reversed, the order for the conditional release was vacated, and the petition was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Incapacitated and Mentally Disabled Persons -- Involuntary Commitment -- Involuntary Transfer of Convicted Sex Offenders to State Psychiatric Facility at Conclusion of Prison Terms

Petitioners, convicted sex offenders who were certified as being dangerously mentally ill by two Office of Mental Health (OMH) physicians immediately prior to their scheduled release from prison, were not entitled to a precommitment hearing pursuant to Correction Law § 402 before their transfers to an OMH psychiatric facility for involuntary commitment at the conclusion of their prison terms upon the required certification of a third physician in accordance with Mental Hygiene Law § 9.27. The procedures of Correction Law § 402 for mentally ill inmates did not govern petitioners' commitment, since petitioners were no longer prisoners at the time of their commitment. The Mental Hygiene Law commitment procedures control where a hospitalized inmate no longer serving a sentence becomes a free individual (see Correction Law § 404 [1]). The Department of Correctional Services (DOCS) had standing to make the applications for petitioners' involuntary commitment as "an officer of any public or well recognized charitable institution or agency or home in whose institution the person alleged to be mentally ill resides" (Mental Hygiene Law § 9.27 [b] [4]). As used in the statute, the word "public" has an independent meaning, modifying institution, agency and home, and DOCS thus qualified as a "public" agency. Finally, while Supreme Court properly determined that the habeas corpus petition should have been brought pursuant to Mental Hygiene Law § 33.15, it erred by conditionally releasing petitioners without conducting its own review as to the state of each individual's mental disability.

 

578 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Garcia


7863, Ind. 4439/03


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


29 A.D.3d 255; 812 N.Y.S.2d 66; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3714; 2006 NY Slip Op 2315



March 28, 2006, Decided 
March 28, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v. Garcia, 7 NY3d 789, 854 NE2d 1283, 821 NYS2d 818, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2782 (2006)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Garcia v. Rivera, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 59722 (S.D.N.Y., Aug. 16, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), convicting him, after a nonjury trial, of attempted assault in the second degree, criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree, criminal mischief in the third degree, assault in the third degree (three counts), endangering the welfare of a child (three counts), and aggravated cruelty to animals, and imposing sentence as a second violent felony offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed his "stomping" on a pet goldfish was a misdemeanor (N.Y. Agric. & Mkts. Law § 353) and not a felony under N.Y. Agric. & Mkts. Law § 353-a(1) because a fish was not a "companion animal" and his actions did not constitute aggravated cruelty. The appeals court found the Legislature did not require a reciprocity of affection in the definition of "companion animal." The statute's language was consistent with the People's claim that "domesticated" was commonly understood to mean "to adapt (an animal or plant) to life in intimate association with and to the advantage of humans." Thus, a goldfish was a domesticated rather than a wild animal under the common meaning. Section 353-a was sufficiently clear to apprise a person of ordinary intelligence that the sort of conduct in which defendant engaged came within its prohibition. The trial court improperly exercised discretion in considering attempted assault in the second degree as a lesser-included offense of first-degree attempted assault. It was not until after summations that the court indicated it would consider attempted second-degree assault, a significant departure from the prosecution's theory of the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified, on the law, to the extent of vacating the conviction for attempted assault in the second degree, and replacing the second violent felony offender adjudication with a second felony offender adjudication, reducing the aggregate sentence to 5 1/2 to 11 years, and otherwise affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Aggravated Cruelty to Animals -- Stomping of "Pet" Goldfish

1. Defendant was lawfully convicted of the felony of aggravated cruelty to animals (Agriculture and Markets Law § 353-a [1]) for having stomped to death three "pet" goldfish kept by his girlfriend's nine-year-old son following an altercation with his girlfriend in the apartment they shared. The statute, which proscribes intentionally killing or intentionally causing "serious physical injury to a companion animal with aggravated cruelty," is not unconstitutionally vague. A "companion animal," in addition to any dog or cat, includes "any other domesticated animal normally maintained in or near the household of the owner or person who cares" for the animal (Agriculture and Markets Law § 350 [5]). A "pet" goldfish is a "domesticated animal" that falls within the statutory definition of "companion animal," and defendant's "stomping" constituted "aggravated cruelty" within the meaning of the statute. The statute is sufficiently clear to apprise a person of ordinary intelligence that the sort of conduct in which the defendant engaged comes within its prohibition.

Crimes -- Lesser Included Offense -- Attempted Second Degree Assault

2. In defendant's prosecution for assault and related charges arising from an altercation with his girlfriend in the apartment they shared, the trial court in the bench trial improperly exercised its discretion pursuant to CPL 300.50 in considering, sua sponte, the charge of attempted assault in the second degree as a lesser included offense of first degree assault and finding defendant guilty of that charge based upon defendant's use of his hand to injure his girlfriend during the altercation. The prosecution tried its case on the theory that defendant's use of a knife in the struggle against his girlfriend established the necessary element of attempt to cause serious physical injury. The court's consideration of attempted assault in the second degree without the use of a weapon as a lesser included offense represented a significant departure from the prosecution's case against defendant, requiring a reversal of the conviction. When the People have limited the theory of the prosecution, the court is obliged to observe that limitation.

Crimes -- Criminal Mischief -- Proof of Amount of Damage to Property -- Photographic Evidence 

3. Defendant was properly convicted of criminal mischief in the third degree (Penal Law § 145.05 [2]) for damaging his girlfriend's property in the apartment they shared in an amount exceeding $ 250, even though there was no expert testimony or documentation as to repair costs. The photographic evidence of the damage to the television screen and a glass wall unit, coupled with complainant's testimony as to what she paid for those items and her claim that the repair cost would be $ 500 for the wall unit and $ 700 for the television, were sufficient to establish repair cost in excess of $ 250 beyond a reasonable doubt.

Crimes -- Sentence -- Second Violent Felony Offender

4. Although defendant's adjudication as a second violent felony offender was necessarily vacated because he was not convicted of any violent felony in this case, there was no need for resentencing since the sentences imposed were all lawful for a nonviolent second felony offender and the trial court stated its intention to sentence defendant to the maximum possible term.

Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State of New York


6915, Index 111070/93


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


29 A.D.3d 175; 814 N.Y.S.2d 1; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3598; 2006 NY Slip Op 2284



March 23, 2006, Decided 
March 23, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 7 NY3d 824, 855 NE2d 1167, 822 NYS2d 752, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2573 (2006)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 7 NY3d 824, 855 NE2d 1167, 822 NYS2d 753, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2554 (2006)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity v. State, 7 NY3d 829, 855 NE2d 1170, 856 NE2d 208, 822 NYS2d 755, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2594 (2006)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 7 NY3d 829, 855 NE2d 1171, 822 NYS2d 756, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2593 (2006)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity v. State, 7 NY3d 829, 856 NE2d 208, 823 NYS2d 118, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2595 (2006)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity v. State, 7 NY3d 830, 856 NE2d 209, 823 NYS2d 118, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2596 (2006)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity v. State, 7 NY3d 829, 208 NE2d 208, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2599 (2006)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity v. State, 7 NY3d 828, 855 NE2d 1170, 822 NYS2d 755, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2613 (2006)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by, Vacated by, in part Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State of New York, 8 NY3d 14, 861 NE2d 50, 828 NYS2d 235, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 3566 (N.Y., Nov. 20, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State of New York and others, appealed the order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), granting plaintiffs' motion to confirm the referees' report, denying the cross motion of the State and other defendants to reject the report in part, and directing the State and others to implement a plan to provide the New York City School District with a minimum amount of additional annual operating and capital improvement funds.


OVERVIEW: In previous litigation in the instant case, the state high court found that schoolchildren in the New York City School District were not receiving the opportunity for the constitutional sound basic education as required under N.Y. Const. art. XI, § 1 and that there was a causal link between the state's funding system and the constitutional failure. The New York State Governor and Legislature were unable to agree on an amount of funding required to remedy the constitutional failure. At a hearing before referees appointed by the trial court, the State and other defendants submitted a plan that proposed $ 4.7 billion in additional funds for the District. The referees recommended additional annual funds of $ 5.63 billion and capital improvements of $ 9.179 billion. The separation of powers doctrine made it erroneous for the trial court to adopt the referees' recommendations. Under N.Y. Const. art. VII, §§ 1-7, budgeting was for the Governor and Legislature. Furthermore, N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 1 required the Legislature to provide for the maintenance of the public education system. Lastly, the courts were ill equipped to determine the appropriate amount of funding.


OUTCOME: The order was modified insofar as the confirmation of the referees' report was vacated and the New York State Governor and Legislature were directed, in part, in enacting a budget, to consider an amount in between $ 4.7 billion and $ 5.63 billion for annual operating funds and that they implement a capital improvement plan of $ 9.179 billion over five years or otherwise meet the District's capital needs. The order was otherwise affirmed.



HEADNOTES

Schools -- State Aid to School Districts -- Remedy for Failure to Provide "Sound Basic Education" -- Separation of Powers Doctrine

Supreme Court, in implementing the directive of the Court of Appeals that the State reform the current system of school funding for the New York City public school system to ensure that the City's schoolchildren receive a "sound basic education" as required by the Education Article of the State Constitution (NY Const, art XI, § 1), erred in confirming the report of the Referees and directing that the State appropriate at least $ 5.63 billion in additional annual operating funds for the 2006 fiscal year. Although the State can be directed to appropriate the necessary funding to meet its educational mandate, it is for the Governor and the Legislature, not the courts, to adopt a dollar-specific budget. Under the separation of powers doctrine, the courts cannot usurp the budgetary and educational powers of the Governor and the Legislature and substitute their own budgetary calculations for those of the other branches. The record established that a range of between $ 4.7 billion and $ 5.63 billion phased in over four years would satisfy the State's constitutional education funding obligations, and respondents were directed to consider a funding plan within that range in enacting a budget. Supreme Court did not, however, err in confirming the Referees' recommendation that the State expend a minimum of $ 9.179 billion on capital improvements over the next five years in view of the State's failure to refute or offer an alternative to plaintiffs' proposed capital improvement plan that was adopted by the Referees.

People v. Evans


16134


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


27 A.D.3d 905; 810 N.Y.S.2d 590; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2869; 2006 NY Slip Op 1856



March 16, 2006, Decided 
March 16, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v Evans, 6 NY3d 847, 849 NE2d 976, 816 NYS2d 753, 2006 NY LEXIS 1586 (N.Y., Apr. 28, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the County Court of Sullivan County (New York), which convicted him of unlawful surveillance in the second degree, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 250.45(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant placed a video camera in the bedroom of his girlfriend's 12-year-old daughter in order to record the girl undressing. He was indicted on five counts, and as part of an agreement, he entered a guilty plea to one count of unlawful surveillance. The trial court sentenced defendant as an admitted second felony offender to a term of imprisonment. On appeal, the court initially noted that defendant did not effect a knowing, voluntary, and intelligent waiver of his right to appeal as part of his agreement, as there was no mention of the waiver during the plea recitation. However, his claims lacked merit. His challenge to the constitutionality of § 250.45(3) was not preserved and the court declined to review it in the interest of justice. Defendant also failed to preserve the issue as to the sufficiency of his plea allocution. However, the colloquy unequivocally established that defendant had intentionally used or installed the video camera in the victim's bedroom without her knowledge or consent, and that he was guilty as charged. The allocution was not fatally deficient, as defendant was not required to expressly admit that he had "no legitimate purpose" for his conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Unlawful Surveillance.--Judgment convicting defendant of unlawful surveillance in second degree in connection with his placement of video camera in bedroom of his girlfriend's 12-year-old daughter, with whom he resided, recording her undressing, was affirmed--Penal Law § 250.45 (3) proscribes intentional use or installation of any "imaging device" (Penal Law § 250.40 [2]) to "surreptitiously view, broadcast or record a person" in specific locations where person has reasonable expectation of privacy, i.e., "bedroom, changing room, fitting room, restroom, toilet, bathroom, washroom, shower or any room assigned to guests or patrons in a motel, hotel or inn, without such person's knowledge or consent"; in view of surreptitious nature of conduct and private character of locations, statute creates rebuttable presumption that person who engages in such conduct did so for "no legitimate purpose."

Crimes--Appeal--Waiver of Right to Appeal.--Defendant did not effect knowing, voluntary and intelligent waiver of his right to appeal as part of negotiated agreement--when People recited plea terms, no mention was made of appeal waiver; only reference to appeal waiver was question by court in context of explaining trial rights that defendant would be foregoing by guilty plea; there was no record discussion or explanation concerning appeal waiver or effort to ascertain if defendant understood that right or had discussed it with counsel and no indication that defendant ever signed appeal waiver, and knowing and voluntary waiver cannot be inferred from silent record.

Crimes--Plea of Guilty--Sufficiency of Allocution

People v. Bautista


7860


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


26 A.D.3d 230; 809 N.Y.S.2d 62; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1998; 2006 NY Slip Op 1222



February 16, 2006, Decided 
February 16, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal granted by People v. Bautista, 6 NY3d 831, 847 NE2d 376, 814 NYS2d 79, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 976 (2006)
Motion granted by People v. Bautista, 6 NY3d 822, 846 NE2d 468, 813 NYS2d 38, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 564 (2006)
Motion granted by People v. Bautista, 6 NY3d 880, 850 NE2d 24, 817 NYS2d 209, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1263 (2006)
Appeal dismissed by People v. Bautista, 7 NY3d 838, 857 NE2d 49, 823 NYS2d 754, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 2627 (N.Y., Sept. 21, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the New York County Supreme Court (New York) that denied his motion to be resentenced pursuant to the 2005 Drug Law Reform Act, 2004 N.Y. Laws ch. 643, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that pursuant to N.Y. Correct. Law § 851(2), an "eligible inmate" was a person confined in an institution who was eligible for release on parole or who would become eligible for release on parole or conditional release within two years. Because defendant would not be eligible for parole until March 2008, he was did not come under the provisions of the Drug Law Reform Act, 2004 N.Y. Laws ch. 643, § 1. Therefore, the trial court correctly denied his motion to be resentenced under the Act. The Act was not unconstitutional, since the distinction was rationally related to the achievement of the valid state objective of ameliorating the conditions of those A-II offenders facing the longest prison time.


OUTCOME: The order was unanimously affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Sentence.--Defendant was not entitled to be resentenced under 2005 version of Drug Law Reform Act (L 2005, ch 643, § 1) since such law, when read together with Correction Law § 851 (2), requires that, in order to be eligible for resentencing, defendant convicted of class A-II offense must be eligible for release on parole within two years, and defendant was eligible for parole within three years.

Samuels v. New York State Dept. of Health


98084


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


29 A.D.3d 9; 811 N.Y.S.2d 136; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2005; 2006 NY Slip Op 1213



February 16, 2006, Decided 
February 16, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion granted by Hernandez v. Robles, 6 NY3d 863, 850 NE2d 14, 817 NYS2d 199, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1219 (2006)
Motion granted by Hernandez v. Robles, 6 NY3d 862, 850 NE2d 13, 817 NYS2d 199, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1217 (2006)
Motion granted by Hernandez v. Robles, 6 NY3d 865, 850 NE2d 15, 817 NYS2d 201, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1180 (2006)

Motion granted by Hernandez v. Robles, 6 NY3d 879, 850 NE2d 23, 817 NYS2d 208, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1261 (2006)
Motion granted by Hernandez v. Robles, 6 NY3d 878, 850 NE2d 21, 817 NYS2d 207, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1283 (2006)
Motion granted by Samuels v. N.Y. State Dep't of Health, 6 NY3d 881, 850 NE2d 24, 817 NYS2d 210, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1284 (2006)
Motion granted by Hernandez v. Robles, 6 NY3d 880, 850 NE2d 23, 817 NYS2d 209, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1281 (2006)
Affirmed by, Sub nomine at Hernandez v. Robles, 7 NY3d 338, 855 NE2d 1, 821 NYS2d 770, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1836 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff same-sex couples challenged an order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which dismissed their complaint seeking a judgment declaring the New York Domestic Relations Law unconstitutional to the extent that it prohibited marriage licenses from being issued to same-sex couples. Plaintiffs had requested marriage licenses under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 15 and were informed that such licenses would not be issued to same-sex couples.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs asserted that the restriction violated the due process, equal protection, and free speech provisions of the state constitution. The court found that the case was not simply about the right to marry the person of one's choice, but represented a significant expansion into new territory which was, in reality, a redefinition of marriage. The court was not persuaded that plaintiffs had established beyond a reasonable doubt that it was irrational for the legislature to preserve the historic legal and cultural understanding of marriage. The court was also unpersuaded by plaintiffs' argument that the relevant restrictions placed by New York on the issuing of marriage licenses violated their constitutional right to free speech; the state's laws defining marriage were general in nature and did not target any speech or expressive conduct. The legislature acted consistent with its constitutional role, and the parameters that it placed on marriage were undergirded by sufficient governmental interests to uphold marriage as historically understood and defined. The court concluded that the legislature was where changes to marriage of the nature urged by plaintiffs should be addressed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.


HEADNOTES

Marriage -- Same Sex Marriage -- Constitutionality of Marriage Laws

1. New York's marriage laws are not unconstitutional to the extent that they prohibit marriage licenses from being issued to same-sex couples (see Domestic Relations Law § 15). Substantive due process under the State Constitution (NY Const, art I, § 6) is not violated by limiting marriage to heterosexual couples. While traditional marriage is a fundamental right, that right does not encompass same-sex marriages. Furthermore, New York's marriage laws are not violative of equal protection under the rational basis standard. The otherwise facially neutral marriage laws do not create an unconstitutional gender-based discriminatory scheme. Rather, permitting only opposite-sex couples to marry is rationally based on the State's legitimate interest in preserving the historic legal and cultural understanding of heterosexual marriage as a social institution in which procreation occurs. Any changes to the marriage laws require legislative action, and cannot be accomplished by a judicial redefinition of marriage to include same-sex couples.

Marriage -- Same Sex Marriage -- Constitutionality of Marriage Laws

2. New York's marriage laws prohibiting marriage licenses from being issued to same-sex couples do not violate plaintiffs' constitutional right to free speech. Even if it is assumed that the Legislature's actions in fulfilling its long-established duty of defining the parameters of marriage implicated plaintiffs' free speech rights, when speech and nonspeech elements are combined a sufficiently important governmental interest in regulating the nonspeech element can justify incidental limitations on First Amendment freedoms. The State's laws defining marriage are general in nature and do not target any speech or expressive conduct.

Korotun v. Incorporated Vil. of Bayville


2004-07840, (Index No. 3134/02)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


26 A.D.3d 311; 809 N.Y.S.2d 533; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1657; 2006 NY Slip Op 1001



February 7, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by Korotun v. Inc. Vill. of Bayville, 7 NY3d 701, 850 NE2d 1166, 818 NYS2d 191, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1410 (N.Y., June 6, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners appealed a judgment by the Nassau County Supreme Court (New York) that granted defendant village's motion for summary judgment in the owners' action to declare that a village law was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The owners lived in a home that was constructed as part of a six-home subdivision on a cul-de-sac. The newer section of the cul-de-sac was divided from the older section by the presence of stone pillars on each side of the road at the entrance of the cul-de-sac. A homeowners association that represented the newer, northern section of the cul-de-sac petitioned the village to ban all on-street parking on that section of the street due to numerous complaints that the owners habitually parked their vehicles near the stone pillars. The appellate court found that the village's decision to ban parking in the northern section of the cul-de-sac had a rational basis, to wit: to ensure emergency and service vehicles access and maneuverability and unobstructed views when exiting and entering driveways. The southern section of the cul-de-sac did not necessarily have the same issues. Consequently, because the parking ban was not unconstitutional, the trial court did not err in granting the village's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified by adding a provision declaring that the local law was constitutional; as so modified, the grant of summary judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Local Laws--Validity Local law which imposed on-street parking ban on cul-de-sac at northern end of street was constitutional--law was passed due to complaints that plaintiffs parked their vehicles in cul-de-sac and near stone pillars at entrance to cul-de-sac, impeding access and maneuverability of Village emergency and service vehicles, obstructing residents' views while at tempting to exit and enter their driveways, and creating aesthetic-related problems--parking ban had rational basis, to wit: to ensure emergency and Village service vehicles access and maneuverability and residents' unobstructed views when exiting and entering their driveways; homeowners' association representing southern section of street, which did not necessarily have these same issues, did not petition Village for similar parking ban; two sections of street had physical and geographical distinctions and, therefore, were not similarly situated.

People v. Hilton


4250- 4250A Ind. 5405/01


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


25 A.D.3d 505; 810 N.Y.S.2d 19; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 865; 2006 NY Slip Op 551



January 31, 2006, Decided 
January 31, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v. Hilton, 6 N.Y.3d 895, 850 N.E.2d 677, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1944, 817 N.Y.S.2d 630 (2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hilton v. New York, 549 U.S. 958, 127 S. Ct. 390, 166 L. Ed. 2d 278, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 7589 (2006)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Hilton v. Brown, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 142326 (S.D.N.Y., Feb. 24, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment on jury verdict of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), convicting him of third-degree robbery and sentencing him as a persistent felony offender, and also appealed an order of the same court that denied his N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.20 motion to set aside his sentence to a term of imprisonment of 15 years to life.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a long history, over decades, of committing violent acts in the course of snatching purses from, primarily, elderly women victims. The incident giving rise to his robbery prosecution had occurred shortly after his release from a previous long incarceration. The evidence indicated that he blocked the victim's exit while demanding money from her and threatening her with a bottle. This was sufficient to supply the "force" element needed to prove third-degree robbery, even though the jury had not found that the bottle was a "dangerous instrumentality" so as to prove first-degree robbery. While defendant's appeal was pending, the state's highest court had determined that the practice, used in defendant's case, of having a judge decide whether persistent felony offender sentencing was appropriate, based on facts originally found by the jury, did not violation constitutional safeguards. For this reason, and because the record showed that the public could best be protected by imposition of a long sentence, relief from that sentence was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Robbery.--Evidence sufficiently supported verdict convicting defendant of third degree robbery--defendant used and threatened immediate use of force to facilitate his theft of victim's purse by blocking victim's exit, demanding money and holding bottle in threatening manner.

Crimes--Sentence--Persistent Felony Offender.--Defendant's sentence as persistent felony offender after conviction of third degree robbery was not disturbed given his lengthy and serious criminal record which included many violent acts against women; court carefully considered defendant's troubled childhood, his drug addiction and his affliction with AIDS.

Elmy v. City of Amsterdam


97302


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


25 A.D.3d 1038; 807 N.Y.S.2d 490; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 635; 2006 NY Slip Op 415



January 26, 2006, Decided 
January 26, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by Elmy v. City of Amsterdam, 6 NY3d 713, 849 NE2d 972, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1312, 816 NYS2d 749 (N.Y., May 9, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured pedestrian appealed an order of the Supreme Court, Montgomery County (New York), that granted motions by defendants, a city and certain landowners, for summary judgment dismissing her complaint seeking damages for injuries sustained in a fall on a sidewalk.


OVERVIEW: The pedestrian fell on a public sidewalk in front of the landowners' property. The pedestrian's husband claimed to have seen one landowner trying to repair the sidewalk, but there was no evidence indicating negligent repairs by anyone. The court held, first, that the failure to provide notice of a defect to the city as required by Amsterdam, N.Y., Local No. 2, § C127, precluded any action against the city. The meaning of the ordinance was plain enough, even though it was missing a few words. The pedestrian could not recover from the landowners either, as she had failed to show an exception to the rule that abutting landowners were not responsible for the condition of a public sidewalk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Statutes--Construction

Municipal Corporations--Sidewalks--Prior Notice of Defective Condition.--In action by plaintiff, who tripped and fell while jogging on sidewalk, complaint was dismissed against City--plaintiff failed to show compliance with City's prior written notice statute--although certain words were omitted from statute, intent of law was readily apparent; inadvertent drafting omission did not vitiate clear purpose of law.

Negligence--Sidewalks.--In action by plaintiff, who tripped and fell while jogging on sidewalk that fronted property owned by defendants, complaint was dismissed against defendants--evidence was insufficient to create triable issue on any exception to general rule that abutting landowners are not liable for injuries on public sidewalks--plaintiff's husband's statement that he had seen defendant making cement repair to sidewalk prior to date of accident was insufficient to raise triable issue since there was no indication that repair was done negligently, that it was done at place where plaintiff fell, or that it otherwise was cause of accident.

Catholic Charities of Diocese of Albany v. Serio


96621


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


28 A.D.3d 115; 808 N.Y.S.2d 447; 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 278; 2006 NY Slip Op 194



January 12, 2006, Decided 
January 12, 2006, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion granted by Catholic Charities of the Diocese of Albany v Serio, 7 NY3d 746, 853 NE2d 231, 2006 NY LEXIS 1799, 819 NYS2d 862 (2006)
Motion granted by Catholic Charities of the Diocese of Albany v Serio, 7 NY3d 746, 853 NE2d 232, 2006 NY LEXIS 1800, 819 NYS2d 862 (2006)
Motion granted by Catholic Charities of the Diocese of Albany v Serio, 7 NY3d 747, 853 NE2d 232, 2006 NY LEXIS 1803, 819 NYS2d 863 (2006)
Motion granted by Catholic Charities of the Diocese of Albany v Serio, 7 NY3d 747, 853 NE2d 232, 2006 NY LEXIS 1814, 819 NYS2d 863 (2006)
Motion granted by Catholic Charities of the Diocese of Albany v Serio, 7 NY3d 747, 853 NE2d 233, 2006 NY LEXIS 1816, 819 NYS2d 863 (2006)
Motion granted by Catholic Charities of the Diocese v Serio, 7 NY3d 798, 854 NE2d 1269, 2006 NY LEXIS 2444, 821 NYS2d 804 (N.Y., Aug. 29, 2006)
Affirmed by Catholic Charities of the Diocese of Albany v Serio, 7 NY3d 510, 859 NE2d 459, 2006 NY LEXIS 3201, 825 NYS2d 653 (N.Y., Oct. 19, 2006)



DISPOSITION: The judgment was  [***2] affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a legislative enactment requiring employers providing group insurance coverage for prescriptions to include prescriptive contraceptives, the Albany County Supreme Court (New York) granted defendant insurance superintendent's cross motion for summary judgment dismissing a complaint filed against him by plaintiffs, various religious employers that did not qualify for the narrow statutory exemption. The employers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employers' constitutional challenges to the Women's Health and Wellness Act (Act) all fell within the religion clauses of the First Amendment to the United States Constitution and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 3. Within the Act, the legislature provided an exemption from the contraceptive coverage mandate which generally included religious institutions in their capacity as ecclesiastical bodies, but which might not include religious institutions in their capacity as ministries. The contraceptive coverage mandate burdened the employers' right to freely exercise their religious beliefs. However, despite this burden, the Act did not offend the constitutional or statutory provisions the employers invoked. Moreover, while an exemption could give rise to entanglement problems if a court or agency were asked to determine what types of religious activity constituted the inculcation of religious values, such an inquiry was not presented in light of the employers' concessions that their primary focus was not the inculcation of religious values. To the extent that any of the arguments asserted by the employers were not explicitly addressed, they were considered and found to be lacking in merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Religion -- Contraception Coverage Mandate -- "Religious Employer" Exemption

1. The Women's Health and Wellness Act (WHWA) (L 2002, ch 554), which requires employers that provide group insurance coverage for prescriptions to include prescription contraceptives in that coverage, is not unconstitutional to the extent that the "religious employer" exemption from the contraceptive coverage for religious institutions in their capacity as ecclesiastical bodies (Insurance Law § 3221 [l] [16] [A]; § 4303 [cc] [1]) does not extend to faith-based entities like plaintiffs that operate ministries in areas of human service whose primary purpose is not the inculcation of religious values. The incidental burdens imposed by the WHWA's contraceptive coverage mandate upon plaintiffs' sincerely held religious beliefs do not violate the Free Exercise Clause of the First Amendment. The WHWA is facially neutral and its object, to increase women's access to health care, does not target religious practices. Furthermore, the Free Exercise Clause of the State Constitution (NY Const, art I, § 3) does not afford plaintiffs any greater protection. The State's important conjoined interests in gender equity and health care addressed in the WHWA outweigh plaintiffs' free exercise rights. Moreover, plaintiffs failed to rebut the presumption that the Legislature conducted adequate fact-finding to support its enactment of the WHWA.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Contraception Coverage Mandate -- "Religious Employer" Exemption

2. The Women's Health and Wellness Act (L 2002, ch 554), which requires employers that provide group insurance coverage for prescriptions to include prescription contraceptives in that coverage, is not unconstitutional under the First Amendment's Free Speech Clause to the extent that the "religious employer" exemption from the contraceptive coverage for religious institutions in their capacity as ecclesiastical bodies (Insurance Law § 3221 [l] [16] [A]; § 4303 [cc] [1]) does not extend to faith-based entities like plaintiffs that operate ministries in areas of human service whose primary purpose is not the inculcation of religious values. Plaintiffs failed to state a "hybrid" constitutional claim deriving from the rights of expressive association and conduct as speech. The provision of group health insurance coverage for prescription contraceptives is not constitutionally protected expressive conduct. Consequently, the statute cannot be deemed to compel plaintiffs to communicate a particularized message endorsing contraceptive use that is contrary to their sincerely held religious beliefs.

Constitutional Law -- Establishment of Religion -- Contraception Coverage Mandate -- "Religious Employer" Exemption

3. The Women's Health and Wellness Act (L 2002, ch 554), which requires employers that provide group insurance coverage for prescriptions to include prescription contraceptives in that coverage, is not violative of the Establishment Clause of the First Amendment to the extent that the "religious employer" exemption from the contraceptive coverage for religious institutions in their capacity as ecclesiastical bodies (Insurance Law § 3221 [l] [16] [A]; § 4303 [cc] [1]) does not extend to faith-based entities like plaintiffs that operate ministries in areas of human service whose primary purpose is not the inculcation of religious values. The exemption's distinction between religious and secular activities does not constitute a prohibited gerrymander, since it does not distinguish between religions or sects. The statute on its face does not give rise to excessive entanglement between church and state. Furthermore, the contraception coverage mandate does not impermissibly interfere with "church autonomy."

Civil Rights -- Discrimination in Employment -- Contraception Coverage Mandate -- "Religious Employer" Exemption

4. The Women's Health and Wellness Act (L 2002, ch 554), which requires employers that provide group insurance coverage for prescriptions to include prescription contraceptives in that coverage, is not invalid for being contrary to the Human Rights Law to the extent that the "religious employer" exemption from the contraceptive coverage for religious institutions in their capacity as ecclesiastical bodies (Insurance Law § 3221 [l] [16] [A]; § 4303 [cc] [1]) does not extend to faith-based entities like plaintiffs that operate ministries in areas of human service whose primary purpose is not the inculcation of religious values. The doctrine of preemption does not apply to conflicts between two provisions of state law. In any event, the Human Rights Law exemption for religious-related employers (Executive Law § 296 [11]) merely excuses such employers from compliance with Executive Law § 296 and does not otherwise restrict the power of the Legislature to otherwise impose affirmative requirements upon religious-related employers.

Constitutional Law -- Establishment of Religion -- Contraception Coverage Mandate 

5. In an action challenging the constitutionality of the Women's Health and Wellness Act (WHWA) (L 2002, ch 554) insofar as it requires employers that provide group insurance coverage for prescriptions to include prescription contraceptive coverage, to the extent that plaintiffs are religious corporations, their argument that certain provisions of the Religious Corporations Law explicitly subordinated the WHWA to the governance of religious denominations, thus barring the Legislature from imposing the contraceptive coverage mandate upon them, lacks merit. There is nothing in the provisions cited by plaintiffs that would insulate them from a generally applicable law such as the WHWA.

 

588 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Simms


1548 KA 04-02474


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


24 A.D.3d 1281; 807 N.Y.S.2d 503; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14448; 2005 NY Slip Op 9937



December 22, 2005, Decided 
December 22, 2005, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v. Simms, 6 N.Y.3d 838, 847 N.E.2d 383, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 1133, 814 N.Y.S.2d 86 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Stay denied by, Certificate of appealability denied Simms v. LaClair, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 1400 (W.D.N.Y., Jan. 6, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Monroe County Court (New York) convicted defendant of robbery in the second degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment on the ground that his trial was not commenced within the time period set forth in N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 580.20. The appellate court disagreed. Certain delays were attributable to the disposition of motions made by defendant, the hearing on such motions, and the decisions rendered by the trial court, and thus those delays were excluded from the time chargeable to the People. The remaining delays were adjournments requested by defendant after he was assigned new counsel. Contrary to defendant's contentions, there was no requirement that the court make "a formal finding" on the record of good cause for a continuance, and the record established that the continuances were reasonable and necessary. Defendant failed to meet his burden of establishing good cause for substitution of counsel. The tension that arose between defendant and defense counsel because of defendant's disagreement with defense counsel's strategy was not requisite good cause for substitution. The only conflict of interest was that created by defendant because of his unjustified hostility toward his assigned counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Right to Speedy Trial.--Contention that court erred in denying motion to dismiss indictment on ground that trial was not commenced within time period set forth in article IV (c) of Interstate Agreement on Detainers (CPL 580.20) was rejected--delays attributable to disposition of motions made by defendant were excluded from period of time chargeable to People; remaining delays were adjournments requested by defendant after he was assigned new counsel; there is no requirement that court make "formal finding" on record of good cause for continuance, and record established that continuances were reasonable and necessary.

Crimes--Right to Counsel.--Tension that arose between defendant and defense counsel because of defendant's disagreement with defense counsel's strategy did not constitute requisite good cause for substitution; only conflict of interest was that created by defendant because of his unjustified hostility toward his assigned counsel.

 

589 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Ciafone v. Kenyatta


2003-09892


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


27 A.D.3d 143; 807 N.Y.S.2d 114; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14463; 2005 NY Slip Op 9668



December 19, 2005, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the Son of Sam Law, N.Y. Executive Law § 632-a, (Son of Sam Law), plaintiff crime victim sued defendant inmate, seeking to reach proceeds of the inmate's medical malpractice settlement. The inmate moved to dismiss the complaint on grounds that § 632-a was unconstitutional; the Westchester County Supreme Court (New York) denied the motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim, a transit police officer, was shot with his own revolver by the inmate. While incarcerated for his crimes, the inmate settled a medical malpractice action brought against the State of New York. Learning of the settlement, the victim filed the instant suit. The inmate argued that the Son of Sam Law violated the Ex Post Facto Clause, U.S. Const. art. 1, § 9, by affording crime victims new rights to sue that did not exist at the time of his conviction, and violated the Contracts Clause, U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10, by impairing an existing contract between himself and the State. The appellate court disagreed. The Son of Sam Law did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause because it was a civil law that was not punitive in intent or affect, it advanced the State's compelling interest in ensuring that crime victims were compensated by the perpetrators, and it was rationally connected to that objective. Nor did it violate the Contracts Clause, as it did not operate upon the contract itself, but only against the property that was the subject of the stipulation settling the inmate's malpractice claim. The law merely exposed that malpractice recovery to the victim.


OUTCOME: The order denying the inmate's motion to dismiss was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Son of Sam Law 

1. Plaintiff, a New York City Transit Authority police officer who was severely injured in a line-of-duty shooting by defendant in 1974, stated a claim under the Son of Sam Law (Executive Law § 632-a) against the medical malpractice settlement received by defendant from the State in 2001 during his incarceration. The Son of Sam Law, which permits a crime victim to recover damages from the convicted perpetrator of the crime, does not unconstitutionally impose further punishment upon convicted criminals in violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause (US Const, art I, § 9 [3]). The statute was intended to provide the opportunity for restitution to crime victims, not to impose additional punishment upon convicted criminals. Furthermore, the statute is not punitive in effect. The statute does not impose any affirmative disabilities or restraints upon a convicted criminal, nor does the statute serve a retributive or deterrent effect. Rather, the statute merely enables a crime victim to pursue compensation for an injury, a remedy that has not historically been regarded as punishment.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Son of Sam Law 

2. The Son of Sam Law (Executive Law § 632-a) as applied to defendant inmate, did not violate the Contract Clause of the United States Constitution (US Const, art I, § 10) by exposing defendant's medical malpractice recovery to plaintiff police officer's claims arising out of defendant's shooting of the officer. The law does not operate upon the contract (the stipulation between defendant and the State settling his malpractice claim) itself, but only against the property that was the subject of the stipulation, and therefore does not impair the performance of the contract (where the contract was performed by depositing the money in the inmate's account), but merely exposes the malpractice recovery to plaintiff. In any event, if there were an impairment, it was to accomplish the legitimate public purpose of the recompense of crime victims.

 

590 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Hession v. New York State & Local Employees' Retirement Sys.


98267


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


24 A.D.3d 1008; 806 N.Y.S.2d 281; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14126; 2005 NY Slip Op 9613



December 15, 2005, Decided 
December 15, 2005, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, petitioner employee sought review of a determination by respondent comptroller, which denied the employee's reinstatement to tier 1 membership in respondent New York State and Local Employees' Retirement System.


OVERVIEW: The employee sought reclassification to tier 1 status under N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 645, which was denied. The system granted her reinstatement to tier 2 status. The employee had review by the comptroller, who rejected a hearing officer's conclusion that the employee was entitled to tier 1 status and held that she was entitled only to tier 2 status. The employee petitioned for review. The court found the employee's N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 803 claim was time barred as she did not appeal a decision from years earlier that she was not entitled to tier 1 status since she was not in continual public service. Regardless, as a seasonal employee, she had left county employment for nearly 10 years before returning, so she was not in continuous public service as required by § 803(b)(2). Moreover, N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 645 allowed tier reinstatement only if the employee was a mandatory member of the retirement system during the prior service or had joined at that time. Her prior seasonal employment did not require membership and the fact she was not informed during her prior service of her option to join did not estop the comptroller from performing his duty.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the comptroller's decision.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Civil Service--Retirement and Pension Benefits--Retroactive Membership.--Petitioner was not entitled to reinstatement to tier 1 membership in State and Local Employees' Retirement System--petitioner's claim under Retirement and Social Security Law § 803 for retroactive membership based on 1973 seasonal employment with Town was time-barred--pursuant to Retirement and Social Security Law § 645, which grants tier reinstatement only when petitioner was mandatory member of Retirement System at time of prior service or actually joined Retirement System at that time, petitioner was entitled to tier 2 status based on her subsequent employment with County--statutes were not meant to be read together, and erroneous advice by Town, including its failure to inform petitioner that she could have joined Retirement System in 1973, did not estop Comptroller from denying reinstatement that was contrary to statutes.

Hernandez v. Robles


6598, 6599


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT
